when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她確實做了一些 , 但真正的一件事是說 , 未來會比這個更重要 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個人出現了 , 艾倫•圖靈 , 1936年 , 再次發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , 巴布奇的機器是完全機械的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全是理論上的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個人都是從數學的角度來的 , 但turing告訴我們一件很重要的事情 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 說: 「 不論你如何製造電腦 , 都不重要 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不論你電腦的機械裝置 , 像babbage的裝置 , 或像現今的電子裝置 , 或也許在未來的電腦、細胞 , 或一旦我們進入奈米科技 , 再也不重要了 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變小 。 所有這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種意義上是計算的本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這被稱為教會引發論文 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你就會得到這個連結 , 你說這個東西babbage真的是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到現今我們用電腦所做的事 , 只有很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	給你一個概念:它有多慢 , 有1k的記憶力 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用的是打孔卡 , 被餵食 , 用了大約一萬倍的速度 , 第一個zx81 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一組電池 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要的話 , 你可以加上額外的記憶體 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 這帶給我們什麼呢 ?
so there are plans .	所以 , 有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞典 , 科學博物館的檔案中 , 有數以百計的計劃和數以千計的筆記 , 由charlesbabbage所寫 , 關於這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一個計畫是一組我們稱之為計劃28計劃的計劃 , 這也是我一開始的一個慈善機構的名字 , 他是科學博物館的策展人 , 還有開這計劃來建造不同的引擎的人 , 我們的計劃就是建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯辛頓這裡 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案有很多部件 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	一是巴貝奇的檔案掃描 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二個是研究所有計畫的研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是這台機器的電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是在科學博物館實體建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建造出來時 , 你終於能了解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為你面前的不是一片小晶片 , 你必須看著這個美妙的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶在運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽見它運作 。 我可能聞它 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這之間 , 我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	巴貝奇自己寫信 , 一旦分析引擎就會引導未來的科學課程 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有打造它 , 因為他總是用新的計畫 , 但當它真的被建造出來時 , 當然 , 在1940年代 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我來稍微嚐一下它在動作上的樣子 , 用一段影片來說明它的運作方式 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這只是三組cogs , 它會加上 。 這是加入更多的機制 , 所以你想像這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代之前 , 我們會得到它 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝各位 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個影像填充的演說中 , 雅倫•亞瑟•伯特展出了他最近三項關於人性的計畫 , 我們的棲息地拍攝了他一系列的 「 天文攝影 」 , 來自世界各地的個人訪談 , 來自他網路上的 「 六十億人 」 , 他很快就放棄了電影 , 「 家 」 , 透過呼吸影片來記錄人類對環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人類、人類、媒體、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	雅諾•亞瑟伯特蘭在廣闊的角度捕捉了脆弱的地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 可以通過飛機來這裡旅行 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中釋放出九噸的二氧化碳 , 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談到生態學 , 一年內我將二氧化碳當作法國人 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回家時 , 我得要殺一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須以另一種方式來做我的碳排泄 , 就像我每次都要做 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的工作是展現我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些我去年拍過的照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	阿伯達沙油 , 很多的污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	大家都知道問題 ; 我們不想相信我們所知道的事 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在阿爾伯達人工作非op24小時 , 七個小時便盡可能提煉出多少石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的盡頭 。
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油沙不是長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用的石油量比我們每年都多三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的東西 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	新克萊尼亞的珊瑚礁 。
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	百分之百的珊瑚可能因為全球暖化而消失 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 對海洋的生物多樣性非常重要 。
north pole . i've done this picture last summer .	北極 , 去年夏天我拍了這張照片 。
it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	15年前 , 這張照片是不可能做到的 。
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	現在 , 大西洋和太平洋之間有新的開放方式 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	自從1960年以來 , 北極的厚度減少了40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	沒有冰的kilimanjaro有新的面孔 。
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	它失去了80%的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家的說法 , 在一百年內 , 所有的山冰都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上的生命很重要 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	就像艾爾•高爾所說的 , 二十億人住在喜馬拉雅冰河裡 。
return of fish men .	回到漁人身上 。
one fifth of human kind depend on fish to live .	五分之一的人類是依靠魚來生存的 。
today now 70 percent of the fish stock are overexploited .	現今 , 70%的魚股被過度開發 。
according to fao , if we don't change our system of fishing the main sea resources will be gone in 2050 .	根據fao的說法 , 如果我們不改變漁業系統 , 2050年就會消失 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的東西 。
the beautiful picture , by [unclear] in africa .	美麗的照片 , 在非洲 。
one human of six have not enough to eat in the world .	六個人中的一個人不夠吃東西 。
one billion people have not enough to eat .	十億人不夠吃東西 。
in africa , corn is one of the main foods in many places .	在非洲 , 玉米是許多地方的主要食物之一 。
here in america , 90 percent of the corn cultivated is used to feed animals or to do oil .	在美國這裡 , 有90%的玉米耕種被用來餵養動物或做石油 。
palm tree plantation in borneo .	在婆羅 , 棕櫚樹種 。
every year we lose 50 thousand square miles in deforestation .	每年我們損失了五萬平方英里的森林砍伐 。
refugee camp in darfur .	達佛難民營 。

according to the u . n . , we speak about 250 million refugees in 2050 .	根據聯合國 , 我們在2050年提到大約2億5千萬難民 。
i always show my pictures in the street .	我總是在街上展示我的照片 。

just as that woman tried to kiss my feet when we were taking her sons .	正如那位女士試著親吻我的腳 , 我們在照顧她的兒子 。
and i feel humbled by their strength .	我對他們的力量感到謙卑 。
and i will forever feel a need to make reparations to iraq .	我永遠覺得需要對伊拉克做出回應 。

at the moment , my family is very poor , my life here in shenzhen is just about showing myself that i can earn more and to let my parents stay and have something to live on .	此刻 , 我的家人非常貧窮 , 我的人生在深圳 , 只是為了證明我能賺得更多 , 讓我的父母留下來 , 能活得更久 。

now i am going to speak to you about my movie .	現在我要跟各位談我的電影 。
for the last three years , i was shooting the earth for the movie .	過去三年 , 我為電影拍攝地球 。
the name of the movie is " home " " maison . "	電影的名字是《家》 。
it is about the state of the planet .	重點在於地球的狀態 。

video: this earth is four and a half billion years old .	影片:地球有四十五億年的歷史 。
these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物 , 已經有幾億年了 。
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	我們人類已經直立行走了20萬年 。
we've managed to adapt , and have conquered the whole planet .	我們成功地適應了整個星球 。
for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	數世代以來 , 我們都在養育我們的孩子 , 不像其他數百萬種的物種住在我們旁邊 。
for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去30年來 , 我親眼目睹地球和它的居民 , 遠離天空 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生命與地球的福祉有關 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們依賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕魚、繁殖 , 農業仍然是世界上最先進的人類佔領 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	把我們結合在一起的遠遠遠遠比分裂我們的東西還要大 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都對地球的禮物有同樣的需求 , 希望能超越我們自己 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們帶著牆壁來讓我們分開 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	現今 , 我們最大的戰役是要保護地球的天然資源 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	不到50年 , 我們徹底改變了它 , 遠遠超過人類歷史的所有歷史 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界一半的森林消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源很低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集農業正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源並不是永續的 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在危及自己 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善我們的生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距越來越大 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們尚未明白 , 我們的速度比地球能維持的速度還要快 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道解決方案今天是可用的 。
we all have the power to change this trend for the better .	我們都有能力改變這個趨勢 。
so what are we waiting for ?	所以 , 我們在等什麼 ?

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston的演講中 , 理查德•雷斯尼克的談話中 , 說明了將便宜且快速的基因序列轉移到健康照護的一邊 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、醫療、科學、科技、科技、
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查.雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因革命中 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我向你們展示人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大x染色體的複製品 ; 男性有x , 當然 , 是y的小複製品 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	對不起的男孩 , 這只是個小東西 , 讓你變得不一樣 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以 , 如果你放大這個基因組 , 你就會看到這個雙螺旋結構 , 生命的密碼是用這四個化學字母拼出來的 , 或者我們稱它們為基礎:a、c、g、t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 三十億 。
is that a big number ?	這是一個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以拋出大數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我把這1280年的每一個像素放到800個解析度螢幕上 , 我們需要3 , 000個螢幕來看看基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	這真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	或許是因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 順便一提 , y染色體決定要將它定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	實際上 , 十五年後 , 大約四十億美金後 , 基因組被排序並發表 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	在2003年 , 最後的版本被出版 , 他們一直在努力 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	全部都在一個像這樣的機器上完成 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每個鹼基的成本都很慢 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	現在我們把基因組做成50個複製品 , 我們把這些複製品切成50base閱讀 , 然後我們將它們定序 , 大規模平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把它帶到軟體中 , 我們重新組合起來 , 告訴你們故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	所以 , 給各位看這張圖片 , 人類基因組計畫:3gabases , 沒錯 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	其中一台機器:一週內有200個gabases 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天的2000年將會改變到600年 , 這種速度的速度沒有任何跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 根據基礎序列的價格下降了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這相當於你在1998年用氣體填滿車子 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開車去木星和後面兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc地點、所有醫療文獻、摩爾定律的檔案檔案、舊的方式 , 還有新的東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是一個物流層面 , 通常你不會看到這樣的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 全世界定序人類基因組的能力是今年大約五萬到十萬的人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們知道這個基於被安置的機器 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	這預期會是雙倍、三倍或四倍 , 年復一年 , 預期未來會是可預見的 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 特別有一間實驗室 , 代表所有能力的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做 「 北京基因研究所 」 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	順便說一下 , 中國人對新月球的贏家絕對贏得了這場比賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學有什麼意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以 , 一個女人年紀37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她呈現的是第2期的雌激素受體乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和輻射治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她恢復了三階段的卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用手術和化療治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她在42歲時就回來了 , 有更多卵巢癌 , 更多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她帶著急性骨髓性白血病回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸衰竭 , 八天後就死了 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	所以 , 首先 , 這個女人被治療的方式 , 在短短的10年內 , 看起來就像血液輸血一樣 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	正是因為像我的同事 , 瑞克威爾森 , 在華盛頓大學的基因組研究所 , 他決定看看這位婦女的後期 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他定序了皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚和癌症骨髓 , 在幾週內 , 他定序了兩者的基因組 , 沒有什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	然後他把這兩個基因組拿來做比較 , 在軟體中 , 他發現 , 在其他東西中 , 是一個耗損 , 一個在三十億個鹼基中 , 一個叫做tp53的基因 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因中有突變 , 你就有90%的可能性會得癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這沒有幫助這位女士 , 但如果你願意的話 , 它的確有嚴重的、深遠的影響 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 他們得到了這種基因測試 , 他們就會了解它 , 那麼他們就可以定期篩檢 , 他們可以早期發現癌症 , 並且可能活得更長壽 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我向你們介紹beery雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時被診斷出腦震盪 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的媽媽是一位非常勇敢的女人 , 她不相信症狀沒有匹配 , 透過一些英雄的努力 , 和許多網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們有別的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的就是多餘的染料 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了dopa , 他們的症狀確實改善了 , 但他們沒有完全症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	這張照片裡的男生叫joebeery , 他很幸運能成為一家叫做生命科技的公司 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	他們是兩家公司之一 , 製造出大量的基因組定序工具 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	所以他做的是讓他的孩子順序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現一系列突變發生在一個叫做spr的基因中 , 它負責產生血清素 , 其它東西 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以在杜托邦的頂端 , 他們給了這些孩子一種血清素先驅的藥 , 現在他們很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	沒有完整的基因序列 , 這絕對不會發生 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	在幾年前 , 它花費了10萬美金 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	現在是一萬美金 。 明年是一千美金 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	之後的一年是100美元 , 給予或花一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這就是移動的速度 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有小小的尼克喜歡蝙蝠俠和松鼠槍
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果發現 , 尼克出現在兒童醫院裡 , 帶著這種不友善的肚子 , 就像一個飢荒的受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	並不是說他沒有吃東西 , 而是當他吃東西時 , 他的腸道基本上會打開、排泄到他的腸子裡 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	一百個手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽媽 , 請禱告我 , 我很痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生剛好在臨床遺傳學背景 , 他完全不知道發生了什麼事 , 但他說: 「 讓這個孩子的基因序列 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現一個基因突變 , 負責控制細胞死亡的基因 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	理論是他對食物產生了一些免疫反應 , 基本上 , 這是自然反應 , 造成了一些程式化的細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但調節下降的基因已經破壞了 。

and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	骨髓其實是我們用來拯救數萬名病人的生命 , 大部分患有先進的惡性腫瘤 , 如白血病、淋巴瘤和其他疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	所以 , 幾年前 , 我在史丹佛移植我的移植研究人員 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室 。 我們這裡有bob , 他是志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國 , 以拯救白血病的孩子 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何收割骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.團隊 , 廣泛麻醉、護士 , 還有另一位醫生從我身上穿過 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	鮑勃站在桌子上 , 我們用這種小針 , 你知道的 , 不是太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	基本上 , 我們的方法是將它放在軟組織中 , 將它插入硬骨頭 , 進入tuchus , 每一次 , 針筒就會有十個骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後把它交給護士 。 她把它放進一個tin 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把手交給我 , 再做一次 。
about 200 times usually .	通常是兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	最後 , 我的手臂是索索爾 , 我手上有個電話 , 更不用說bob , 他的屁股看起來更像這樣 , 像是瑞士起士 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道 , 這種手術在40年內沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	可能有更好的方法來做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到一個極少入侵的方法 , 我們稱之為 「 骨髓礦工 」 的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓礦工 , 它的運作方式在這裡顯示 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準的子宮頸病患 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨骼幾十次 , 我們只是進入一次 , 進入髖骨或髖骨的前面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有彈性、強大的導管 , 帶有特殊的迴圈 , 它會留在棉花的一部分 , 遵守髖骨的輪廓 , 當它移動時 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以 , 它能讓你非常迅速地靈活 , 或吸食豐富的骨髓 , 迅速地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以通過相同的入口多次通過 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快的 , 鮑勃就能拿到刺穿、當地的麻醉 , 並把收穫當作門診 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了幾個原型 。 我在史丹佛得到了一個小獎金 。
and played around with this a little bit .	稍微玩一下 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最終我們有兩個大型動物和豬的研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們很驚訝地發現 , 我們不僅把骨髓拿出來 , 我們還得到了10倍的幹細胞活動 , 相較於一般的裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置是去年fda核准的 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這裡是活體病患 。 你可以看到它跟著靈活的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	在同一個病人身上 , 會有兩條路線 , 同一個洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在當地的麻醉劑下完成的 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	同樣的 , 我們得到的幹細胞比一般病人的標準方法多了三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	你為什麼要在乎 ? 骨髓是非常豐富的成人幹細胞來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞在我們的身體中 , 包括骨髓中的血液幹細胞 , 我們用這種方式來當幹細胞療法 , 已經超過40年 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年間 , 骨髓幹細胞被用來治療病人其他疾病 , 比如心臟病、血管疾病、組織工程 , 甚至神經系統 , 來治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出櫃 , 我們正在商業化 , 今年 , 第2.0位礦工 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望它能吸收更多幹細胞 , 使它轉化成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人簽署 , 成為潛在救命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能讓你在更年輕、更健康的將來 , 可以在未來使用你自己的骨髓幹細胞 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這張照片是我們骨髓移植的倖存者 , 他們每年都在史丹佛聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來有更多這些倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪lisi提出一個有爭議性的宇宙模型 , 可能可以回答所有大問題 。 如果沒有其他東西 , 它是你所見過最美麗的18度空間粒子和力量的模型 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技、科技、物理、物理、科學、科技 。
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garretlitlisi理論上所有事物的理論
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	喔 , 老兄 。 看看那些殺手方程式 。 甜 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 在接下來的18分鐘 , 我會盡我所能地描述粒子物理的美麗 , 沒有方程式 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們能從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是一種非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每一個珊瑚都有上千個不同的珊瑚蟲 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些多氯聯苯不斷地累積 , 分成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是一個超級智慧的珊瑚 , 我們可以把一個個體拼出來 , 然後問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他在這個特定的地點 , 與他的鄰居相比 , 如果只是機會 , 或命運 , 或什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們調整溫度太高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全是愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以說是很有意義的 , 我有衝浪來證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這個聚合劑會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居很明顯是一樣的複製品 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在所有其他的地點中 , 體驗到他們是獨立的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 超級智慧的珊瑚 , 會特別準備去了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常精確地描述我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實不斷地分裂成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	這對我們人類來說是一件奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能體驗一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子怪異首先被薛丁格和他的貓描述 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓比較喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設置中 , 薛丁格在一個放射性樣本中 , 由量子力學的定律 , 分成一個放射性和一個沒有放射性狀態的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在這個範圍中 , 樣本的輻射會引發一種觸發 , 釋放出毒藥和薛丁格死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一邊 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些現實被每個人分開體驗 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	儘管如此 , 另一個也不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說是很怪異的 , 因為我們每個人只經歷一個個體存在 , 我們也無法看見其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	彷彿我們每一個人 , 像schrordinger , 是種珊瑚分裂成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們 , 世界是如此微小的 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以用一個句子來總結:所有可能發生的事 , 都可以 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示每件事都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理則是描述可能發生什麼事 , 以及什麼事都無法解釋 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們 , 所有的東西都歸功於幾何學 , 以及基本粒子的互動 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有這些互動是完全平衡的 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我要描述我們對這些粒子的了解 , 它們是什麼 , 以及平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這台機器中 , 一道質子和反質子的束縛會加速到接近光速 , 並聚集在一起 , 產生出一股純能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子 , 用探測器和電腦來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這個巨大的機器 , 位在日內瓦的歐洲核子對撞機有一個十七英里的圓圈 , 當它在運作時 , 比蒙特利市的電力高出五倍 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法明確地預測任何個體碰撞中產生的粒子 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性都被發現了 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理告訴我們哪些粒子可以產生 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量必須跟質子和反質子一樣多 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何粒子的質量比這個能量限制的質量都沒有產生 , 而對我們來說仍然是隱形的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新粒子加速器這麼令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它會把這個能量的限制推到前所未有的七倍之外 , 所以我們很快就會看到一些新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能看到什麼之前 , 讓我描述一下我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一大堆亞原子粒子 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人對電子很熟悉 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這房間裡的很多人 , 過得很好 , 把他們推過來 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有中性夥伴 , 叫做中子 , 沒有電荷 , 和非常小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 由上而下的夸克有很大的質量 , 三的結合 , 讓質子和中子在原子裡製造 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都出現在左右手的品種中 , 有反粒子的伴侶攜帶著相反的載荷 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也有較少熟悉的第二代和第三代 , 相同的載荷和第一代相同 , 但有較高的質量 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子都會和不同力粒子互動 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力通過光子的粒子 , 與電荷相互作用
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種很弱的力量 , 非常不想像地 , 較弱的力量 , 只和左撇子物質相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用 , 帶有一種不同的載荷 , 叫做顏色載荷 , 以三種不同的品種:紅、綠、藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygellmann的名字 , 他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 引力的作用 , 透過質量和旋轉 , 產生物質的作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 每種力都有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力與物質相互作用 , 根據每個粒子有的電荷所產生的物質交互作用 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個尚未被看見的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 它會給所有其他粒子質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是看到希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎確定它會 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最神秘的是我們還能看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我將向你們展示一個美麗的可能性 , 朝這場演說結束 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	如果我們用不同的旋轉和載荷來算出這些不同的粒子 , 就會有226個粒子 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	這是很多粒子用來追蹤的 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然會有這麼多基本粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據它們的載荷來描繪它們 , 有些美麗的圖案就會浮現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的電荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 負電荷 , 夸克三分之一有電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個夸克和一個下夸克結合成一個質子 , 它就有一連串的電荷 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 有相反的電荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷實際上是另外兩個載荷的組合:超荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超荷和弱荷分開 , 在這個二維載荷空間中 , 粒子的載荷 , 電荷是這些粒子沿垂直方向的位置 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力相互作用 , 根據它們的超連結和弱電荷 , 產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這就是所謂的 「 聯合選舉萊克 」 模型 , 它在1967年被組合起來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們之所以熟悉電荷 , 是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯有很大的質量 , 打破了這個划船模式的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它使弱力變得非常虛弱 , 使得微弱的粒子變成大質量 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	因為這個巨大的希格斯坐在地平線的方向上 , 電磁力的光子仍然沒有質量 , 與電荷垂直方向的電荷相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力的描述是用二維空間中的粒子載荷的模式 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以將強力推向它的兩個載荷方向 , 並在這些方向繪製出夸克力粒子的載荷 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以被標在四維空間中 , 投射到像這樣的二維空間 , 這樣我們就能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子交互作用 , 自然就會讓物體在四個載荷方向的完美平衡 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果一顆粒子和反粒子碰撞 , 它就會產生能量 , 以及四個載荷方向的總電荷 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時此刻 , 任何東西都可以產生 , 只要它有相同的能量 , 且能維持一個完全零的載荷 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 指控必須保持平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個微弱的粒子可以腐爛成一個電子 , 一個反中子 , 這三個粒子仍然是零電荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些載荷的模式並不只是漂亮的 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們哪些互動是可以發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四維空間中旋轉這個載荷空間 , 來更好地觀察強相互作用 , 強相互作用 , 它有著很棒的長方形對稱 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強烈的交互作用中 , 強力粒子 , 比如這個 , 和顏色的夸克互動 , 比如這個綠色的夸克 , 給夸克一個不同顏色的夸克這個紅色的粒子 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強烈的互動每秒發生數百萬次 , 發生在我們身體的每個原子 , 將原子核結合在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個載荷對應三種力並不是故事的結局 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以再加上兩個載荷對應到重力 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們把它們納入其中 , 每一個粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉載荷 , 旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們全部都分開 , 在六度載荷空間中給一個美好的模式 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看到它很漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	此時此刻 , 這個模式符合我們目前對於大自然如何在這些基本粒子的微小規模內建構出最好的知識 。
this is what we know for certain .	這就是我們所知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子是極限的 , 是我們能在實驗中找到的 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式中 , 我們已經知道這些微小尺度的粒子物理 。 宇宙的運作方式非常美麗 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些關於我們尚未知道的新舊想法 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要用數學來擴展這個模式 , 看看我們能不能把手放在整個香田上 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到所有組成宇宙的粒子和力量 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想要用這張照片來預測新的粒子 , 我們會看到什麼時候實驗達到更高的能量 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	在粒子物理學中有一個舊的想法 , 這種已知的載荷模式 , 不對稱 , 可以從一個更完美的模式中產生 , 和希格斯粒子如何突破電磁性 , 產生電磁性 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要引進新的力量 , 引進新的載荷方向 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們介紹一個新的方向時 , 我們會猜測粒子在這個方向上有哪些載荷 , 然後我們可以將它和其他粒子旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們明智地猜測 , 我們可以建構出標準載荷的標準載荷 , 作為七個載荷空間中最完美的對稱 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	在1973年 , 帕蒂和薩姆在1973年引入了一項大統一理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看這個新的統一模式時 , 我們可以看到一些空隙 , 有些粒子似乎缺少了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這就是統一理論的運作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家尋找更大、更對稱的模式 , 包括以子集的形式 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測從來沒有看過的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這種統一模型預測了這兩種新的力粒子存在 , 它的作用應該很像弱力 , 只是弱力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七維空間中旋轉這組載荷 , 考慮到關於物質粒子的奇怪事實:物質的第二代和第三代物質在六維載荷空間中有完全相同的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並非獨一無二的被六載荷辨識出來 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準載荷空間的上面 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 我們就可以分配出獨一無二的新載荷給每個粒子 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整個模式是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代 , 與第一代的對稱性有關 , 叫做 「 試驗 」 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	這種八度空間的載荷模式其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大的例外謊言群體 , e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是平滑的曲線形狀 , 有248個維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	每一個點都與這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀相對對應 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這個e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦普遍相對論的曲線時間 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	與量子力學結合 , 這個形狀的幾何形狀可以描述宇宙在最小的尺度運作的一切 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀的模式在八度載荷空間中是非常美麗的 , 它總結了成千上萬個基本粒子之間的互動 , 每一個都只是這種複雜形狀的表面 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉它時 , 我們可以看到許多其他複雜的圖形在這個上面 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	有了特定的旋轉 , 我們就能在八度空間中觀察這個模式 , 同時看到所有粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物體 , 如同任何一個單一物件 , 我們可以看到一些孔 , 以這種模式所需要的新粒子 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	有20個空隙 , 在那裡 , 新粒子應該有二個被巴黎粒子填滿 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從它們的位置來看 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該是像希格斯粒子 , 但它們有色荷 , 和強力相互作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子 , 完成了這個模式 , 給予我們全e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8模式有非常深的數學根 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這種偉大的數學美麗的物體能描述粒子相互作用的真相 , 可以用最小規模的想像來描述 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	大自然被數學描述的這個想法完全不是新的想法 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略寫了這句話: 「 大自然的大自然的大書 , 不斷地對我們的凝視 , 寫在數學的語言中 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形、其他幾何形狀 , 沒有人類無法理解它的單一字 ; 沒有這些字 , 一個在黑暗的迷宮中漫遊 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我試著跟著伽利略的指南描述粒子物理學的數學 , 只用三角形、圓和其他幾何數字 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我研究這個東西時 , 數學會和黑暗迷宮相似 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但這個數學的核心是純粹的 , 美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學結合 , 這個數學描述了我們的宇宙 , 作為一個生長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在各種可能的地點互相交互作用 , 根據一個美麗的模式 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著愈來愈多的圖案使用像大型強子對撞機的新機器 , 我們也許能看到大自然是否使用這種e8圖案或另一個圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現的過程 , 是個很棒的冒險旅程 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合e8模式的粒子 , 那會非常酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc找到新的粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 那會很有趣 , 但對e8理論來說卻不好 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人來說是不好的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會有多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 差不多 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然是非常危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這種理論和其他類似的理論是很長的 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人做了很多辛苦的工作 , 知道這些想法可能最終不會實現大自然 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣的:有很多的野生動物 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論很像新創公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	和任何大型投資一樣 , 要放棄一行不通的研究方式 , 情緒上是很困難的 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學中 , 如果不成功的話 , 你得要把它弄出來 , 嘗試其他的東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	要保持清潔和幸福的唯一方法就是保持平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我嘗試過最好的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡物理、愛和衝浪我自己的三項載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	如此一來 , 就算我研究的物理成就無所不在 , 我仍然知道我過著良好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著住在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年 , 我住在毛伊島 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在 , 宇宙中最大的謎團之一是我的父母 , 我如何能在沒有全職工作中生存下來的情況下生存下來 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要告訴你們這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊家辦公室的照片 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到這些美麗的觀點是相似的 , 但在一些不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在毛伊的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一個非常不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心租金 , 讓我能花時間做我愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	有時 , 過著遊牧的存在是艱難的 , 但它讓我能住在美麗的地方 , 在我的生活中保持平衡 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我可以花很多時間和高智能珊瑚結合在一起 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級智慧的人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	我很高興能邀請來到ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概理解了百分之二 , 但我仍然很喜歡 。 所以我會聽起來很笨 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的所有事物理論:我習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克里斯:是的 , 沒錯 , 有幾個人至少會感到興奮 , 因為 , 如果你是對的 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以你有沒有說我們應該考慮宇宙 , 心臟裡最小的東西 , 像是e8的可能性 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度 , 還是......
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	格林:現在我給你們看的圖案 , 與我們所知的基本粒子物理學有關 , 這些圖案已經對應到一個非常美麗的圖形 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這就是我所說的我們肯定知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這種形狀有很明顯的相似性 , 和它融入e8圖像的方式 , 可能是圖片的其他部分 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看的這些點的圖案 , 實際上代表著這種高維物體的對稱性 , 會在我們體驗的時空中扭曲、移動、跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就是我們所見到的基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克里斯:但弦理論家 , 如我所知 , 用較小的弦震動來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該怎麼把電子和e8有關 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	格林:不 , 這會是e8形狀的對稱性 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當它的形狀在時空移動時 , 它在扭轉 。 當它移動時 , 它的方向就是我們所看到的粒子 。 克里斯:e8形狀的大小 , 和電子有什麼關係 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	它比較大嗎 ? 比較小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	理查德:嗯 , 就我們所知的電子是指點粒子 , 所以這會降到最小的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 在量子場理論中 , 這些東西被解釋的方式是 , 所有可能同時在擴展和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我使用珊瑚的比喻 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8的來源就是它的形狀會在時空中附著 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說的 , 形狀扭轉了方向 , 形狀在轉動時扭轉著 , 轉動的表面就是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	透過量子場理論 , 它們自身呈現是指點 , 並以這種方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能否更清楚一點 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這並不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它喚起了一種奇妙的感覺 , 我當然想要了解更多 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	非常謝謝你們來了 。 這真的很吸引人 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇的黑猩猩研究員珍.古拉爾談到塔瑞和她的其他社區計畫 , 協助非洲的城市居民 , 住在受威脅的動物旁邊 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學、科學等 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍•古拉爾幫助人類和動物一起生活在一起 ,
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們能去 , 賈莫 , 納登 , 波諾 , 但我們也可以 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 , 哦 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這就是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺之前所接到的電話 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一邊傳到另一邊 , 從一群的巢穴傳到下一處 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	我今天晚上想跟你們分享我昨天的zeray離開的地方 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個奇妙又三歲的奧斯洛皮克斯小時候 , 塞拉姆 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過人類的歷史、家譜、人類透過基因檔案 , 聽過人類的歷史 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	這是一位古生物學家 , 已故的路易斯•萊西 , 他讓我踏上研究黑猩猩的路上 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	當時是非常不凡的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	這有點常見 , 但他的論點是因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	從化石看來 , 可說是非常糟糕的 , 從肌肉依附的形狀 , 你可以看出它們是如何與它們共存的 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但 , 她們的行為如何呢 ? 那是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化解 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張 , 現在是一個相當常見的理論 , 如果我們在最接近的生物親戚、大猩猩 , 和人類中發現了類似的行為模式 , 那麼 , 也許這些行為在七百萬年前就出現了 , 人類的祖先 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們把這些特徵從古老、古老的過去帶給了我們 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你現在在教科書上看到處理人類的演化 , 你通常會發現人們在推測早期人類的行為 , 根據黑猩猩的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	牠們比較像我們 , 比任何其他生物 , 在ted大會中 , 我們都聽過 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 我一直在評論黑猩猩和我們很相似的行為方式 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每一隻黑猩猩都有牠或牠自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我會給他們名字 。 他們可以活到六十年左右 , 儘管我們認為大部分的人可能不會在野外60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	女生在11或12歲時 , 她的第一個寶寶 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她只有一個嬰兒 , 每五到六年 , 就有一個很長的童年依賴 , 當嬰兒在護理 , 晚上和媽媽一起睡 , 背上騎著 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信 , 長久以來的幼兒期對黑猩猩很重要 , 就如同對我們而言 , 與學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同形式的動物演化過程中變得更複雜 , 所以我們發現 , 學習在一個人的生命史中扮演著更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間看他們的長輩做的事 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道牠們有能力模仿牠們所看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 這種方式 , 現今在所有不同的黑猩猩族群中被看見的各種不同的工具行為 , 透過觀察、模仿、練習 , 來描述這些行為 , 來形容這些行為是原始的文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語 , 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	他們確實有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 當中有許多是相似的 , 甚至是相似的 , 在相同的情境中形成 。 打招呼黑猩猩擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	牠們也親吻、握手、拍手 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	牠們會搖擺 , 扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現許多關於同情心的例子 , 對於愛和真正利他主義的前兆 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 牠們和我們一樣 , 對牠們的本質有黑暗的一面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有能力極度殘酷 , 甚至是一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	這些極具侵略性的行為 , 大部分的情況下 , 都被指導對抗鄰近社群的個體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	牠們非常激進 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	我相信 , 除了其他生物 , 黑猩猩都能協助我們了解 , 畢竟 , 人類和其他動物王國之間沒有尖銳的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這條線非常模糊 , 每當我們做更多的觀察時 , 它就會變得更模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我在1960年開始的研究仍然持續著 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些黑猩猩 , 活在野外的複雜社交生活 , 比其它東西更有幫助 , 讓我們了解到我們是其中的一部分 , 而不是和我們共享的地球的神奇動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	很遺憾 , 發現黑猩猩 , 就像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 正在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張從空中拍攝的照片 , 它顯示了戈柏的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	那時 , 我飛越整個區域 , 大約16年前 , 我發現 , 在公園之外 , 這片森林 , 在1960年時 , 幾乎沒有破裂 , 沿著東岸的坦尼卡湖岸 , 也就是那小小的三十平方的山羊國家公園的地方 , 這個問題來了我的腦海 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些知名的黑猩猩 ? 當居住在國家公園附近的人掙扎生存時 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	更多人住在那裏 , 比那塊地還多的人可能支持 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民從緬甸湧入的數量增加 , 以及剛果湖邊的數量 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人負擔不起從別處購買食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 塔瑞 」 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是一種非常全面的方式來改善人們生活在公園附近的村莊 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從12個村莊開始 , 現在已經24歲了 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入研究 , 包括樹木護士 , 最適合耕種的方法 , 如今幾乎是沙漠一樣落地在這些山上 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制的方式 , 預防土壤的侵蝕 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	再利用過度使用的農田 , 這樣兩年後才會再有生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	努力協助村民取得乾淨的水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建造一些學校房子 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和小群體合作 , 提供她們機會給微型貸款 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	我們有95%的貸款回報 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦權女性 , 與教育工作 , 提供女孩們獎學金 , 讓他們能完成中學 , 明確地說 , 在全世界 , 身為女性的教育改善 , 家庭尺寸會下降 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供關於家庭規劃的資訊 , 以及關於愛滋病/愛滋病 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計畫 , 有些事正在進行保育 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育的情況是 , 住在這24個村莊的農民 , 與其把我們當成一群白人來研究一群猴子 , 順便一提 , 許多的員工現在是坦尚尼亞 , 但當我們開始了坦尚尼亞的計畫時 , 是一個坦尚尼亞團隊進入村莊 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一位坦尚尼亞團隊和村民談話 , 問他們對什麼感興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們有興趣保育嗎 ? 絕對沒有 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康感興趣 ; 他們對教育感興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 隨著他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更了解保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 隨著山丘的上層是樹木 , 所以你有很糟的土壤侵蝕和泥沼 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展所謂的更大的山羊生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是國家公園以外的地方 , 延伸到這些非常退化的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落有更好的生命標準時 , 他們其實同意將百分之十和二十的土地放到一邊 , 所以 , 當樹木長回來時 , 黑猩猩就會有葉線走廊 , 讓它們能夠在國家公園以外的遺傳群體中和其他遺傳群體互動 。
so tacare is a success .	所以 , 坦卡爾是成功的 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲其它地方複製它 , 在其他地方 , 面對極端人口壓力的野外區域 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 正如我們一直在討論ted的前幾天 , 都是主要的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有很大的貧窮 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你收集大量住在土地上的人 , 那不是肥沃 , 尤其是當你砍掉樹木 , 留下土壤被侵蝕的風 , 因為絕望的人口減少了越來越多樹木 , 所以他們可以試著為自己和家人種植食物 , 會發生什麼事 ?
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	除了非洲 , 其他的問題 , 還有開發中國家的其他問題 , 不論在哪裡 , 我們在地球上做什麼 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道 , 著名的科學家e.o.wilson說 , 如果這個星球上每一個人都能維持平均歐洲人或美國人的平均生活水準 , 我們需要三個新的星球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	現今 , 他們說的是四個 。 但我們沒有 。 我們只有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	到底發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 問題來了 , 我們是最聰明的生物 , 牠們走過地球 , 帶著非凡的腦袋 , 能夠看到這些ted大會的技術 , 但我們卻在破壞我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做出重大的決策之前 , 常常常坐下來問自己: 「 這個決策如何影響我們前面的七個世代 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 主要的決策 , 我不是特別在談非洲 , 而是已開發國家的主要決策 , 包含了數百萬美金 , 數百萬人 , 通常基於 「 這會如何影響下一個股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決定影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲四處旅行 , 談到黑猩猩所面臨的問題 , 以及消失的森林問題 , 我越來越了解到 , 非洲過去殖民地剝削的門上有多少問題可以被解決 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲外面旅行 , 在歐洲 , 說話 , 說話在美國 , 去亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你知道我在說什麼 。 我在說的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水水可能是我們這世紀所面臨的最關鍵的議題之一 , 到處都被農業、工業和家庭污染 , 這些化學物質仍然被噴灑在世界各地 , 似乎無法從過去的經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 ; 海嘯的效應變得更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們談過土壤侵蝕 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們有無數燃燒的化石燃料和其他溫室氣體等燃料 , 稱為氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 全世界的人開始相信氣候有問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都被混合在一起 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	影響較嚴重的窮人 。
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經受到影響了 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱變得更糟了 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨來臨時 , 通常會導致洪水、加上苦難 , 以及貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	住在一個土地無法支援的地區 , 他們太貧窮 , 無法購買食物 , 因為整片土地被破壞了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會得到沙漠化、攪拌、攪拌 , 成為樹木的最後一部分 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種事不只發生在非洲 , 全世界都有 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇見了許多年輕人 , 他們似乎失去了希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為在這個非專業聰明的大腦中 , 會有什麼差異 ? ted的科技會被大眾化 , 而人類的心 ? 以科學的角度來說 , 愛和同情的角度來說 , 會有什麼差距嗎 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	這些年輕人 , 當我跟他們說話時 , 他們不是沮喪、冷漠、憤怒 , 他們說出更多或少了同樣的話: 「 我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 我們沒有辦法去做 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每當我看著他們 , 我想我們是如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 我感受到這個絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這導致了這個計畫 , 我們稱之為根源和芽 , 它從坦尚尼亞開始 , 現在已經擴散到全世界的97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它是象徵性的 。 根是建立一間公司基金會 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射擊看起來很小 ; 為了到達太陽 , 它們可以穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆看成我們在地球上所面臨的所有問題 , 環境和社會問題 。 這是希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	全世界有數十萬名年輕人可以打破這個世界 , 讓這個世界變得更美好 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的最重要的訊息:我們每一個人都能做出改變 , 每天都有 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在這個房間裡的每一個人 , 我們都有選擇 , 我們想要做出什麼樣的改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	非常貧窮的人沒有選擇權 。 取決於我們要改變事情 , 讓窮人也有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽團體都選擇了三個專案 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	取決於他們有多老 , 哪個國家 , 不論他們在城市或鄉村 , 或在哪些計畫中 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在已經從幼稚園到大學 , 越來越多的成人開始自己的根和槍擊團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體選擇 , 在他們之間 , 三個不同的項目 , 讓這個世界變得更美好 , 認知到 , 所有這些不同的問題都是相互關聯的 , 互相影響 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	其中一項計畫就是幫助他們自己的社區 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	如果他們能夠的話 , 他們可能會籌錢協助世界其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一項計畫是幫助動物 , 不只是野生動物 , 還有家畜 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	其中一項計畫就是協助大家共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	在這一切當中 , 推動的是學習如何在我們自己、我們的家庭、我們的社區、文化、宗教和自然世界之間生活的和諧 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然世界 。 我們不能以我們速度破壞它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有比這個星球還多 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	在非洲這裡 , 有一兩項項項計畫 , 根部和芽團體正在進行 , 一或兩項專案在坦尚尼亞、南非、肯亞、南非、剛果、獅子山共和國、喀麥隆 , 以及其他團體 。 如我所說 , 它在97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們種植樹木 , 種植有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 雞和賣掉一些錢 , 或只用它們來餵飽他們的家人 , 感到自豪和有權 , 因為它們不再是無助的 , 且要靠它們的蔬菜和雞 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理協助 , 來展現士兵 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做像這樣的計畫 , 讓它們自己脫離了 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是社會中有用的成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有時間讓更多的根源和芽 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病毒/愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	這是根與芽的重要要素 , 年長的孩子和年輕人談話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	不想懷孕之類的 , 年輕人會傾聽其他年輕人的聲音 , 而非成人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 這就是我在世界各地被問到的問題: 「 珍 , 你見過太多可怕的事 , 你見過你的黑猩猩數量減少了大約一百萬 , 在本世紀後 , 到現在都不超過十五萬 , 其他的動物也一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失了 , 曾經是森林的沙漠 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 」 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能參加像ted這樣的會議 , 沒有希望 , 你能嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 一個是人類的神奇大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想科技 。
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	最後 , 我很興奮 , 最後 , 來談談堆肥式廁所 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	它是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們只是把所有的水沖到火車上 , 很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著談到再生能源 , 極其重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們關心地球的孩子嗎 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	有多少人有小孩或孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們關心他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們 , 身為世界各地的菁英 , 我們可以做點什麼 。 我們可以做出選擇 , 來當我們每天的生活 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買了什麼 , 穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用問題來做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周圍的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	在他長大後 , 它會如何影響我孩子的生命 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或我的孫子 , 或其他的 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的大腦和人類的心情結合在一起 , 我們加入了全世界的手 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	ted就是這樣幫助我們 , 谷歌幫助我們 , esri也幫助我們繪製gombe國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有我們能使用的科技 。
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們連結它們 , 開始發生了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	你在下午聽說過這件事 , 開始發生 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 。 若我們關心未來 , 我們必須有所改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	希望大自然的下一個理由非常有彈性 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以把一個完全被摧毀的區域 , 隨時間 , 或許有些幫助它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	其中一個例子是塔爾計劃 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴各位 , 看似死掉的樹木 , 如果你停止砍伐它們 , 你不需要砍伐它們 , 因為你有樹木木 , 那麼五年後 , 你就能有一棵30英呎樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	動物幾乎在滅絕的邊緣 , 可以給予第二次機會 。 這是我下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	這很鼓舞人心 。 這帶我到了最後一個希望的類別 , 我們在過去的兩天中聽到了很多這樣的聲音:這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 這個決心 , 人類精神的韌性 , 讓那些你認為會被貧困或疾病所打擊的人 , 或其他的 , 都可以用手伸出手 , 把他們的部分帶到社會中 , 改變世界 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想一、兩位真正鼓舞人心的人 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出很長的清單 , 但顯然尼爾森•曼德拉的名單從十七年的辛苦勞工 , 23年的監禁 , 帶著這個令人驚訝的寬恕的能力 , 讓他能帶領他的國家走出種族隔離的邪惡政權 , 沒有血戰 。
