ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	在奈及利亞 , 肯薩萊瓦 , 他採用了巨型的石油公司 , 雖然全世界的人都嘗試了他們最好的嘗試 , 卻被處決 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人非常鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人 , 是我們年輕非洲人所需要的榜樣 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環保的榜樣 , 我今天也聽到了一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以 , 我很感激這個機會 , 能再次和ted的所有人分享這個訊息 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中有人能聚在一起討論這些事 , 特別是根與芽計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後一個詞是那個經營這整個會議中心的年輕女士 , 我今天認識了她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她很興奮 , 得到了她的證書 。 她是根與芽 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她是達爾薩萊姆的領導人 。
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說 , 這協助她做她正在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對於我來說 , 很興奮地見到她 , 看到年輕人是如何被賦權的一個例子 , 因為他們有機會採取行動 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 真正是我們明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家黛安娜柯恩在海洋和我們的生活中 , 分享了一些艱難的事實 , 關於塑膠的塑膠垃圾 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、任務藍色、海洋、塑膠等 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	黛安娜柯恩:對塑膠污染的艱難事實 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直跟塑膠袋一起工作 , 過去20年 , 我剪斷並縫縫合成我作品的主要材料 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成二、三維的碎片、雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	在與塑膠合作 , 大約八年後 , 我的工作開始分裂 , 分解成更小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太棒了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	和我們一樣是短暫的 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	在我更進一步教育塑膠時 , 我發現這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	不好的是 , 塑膠會分解成更小的部分 , 因為它總是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 很多東西都在海洋環境中 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 在過去幾年 , 我學到關於太平洋垃圾和健身 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我最初的反應和我認為這是很多人第一次對它的反應: 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們必須走出去 , 把這個東西清乾淨 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以 , 我提出了一個提案 , 要搭乘貨櫃 , 和兩艘被丟棄的漁船拖船 , 一台吊車 , 一台晶片機 , 和一台冷冰的機器 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的目的是去健身房 , 提高大家對這個議題的認知 , 並開始將塑膠放入一點點 , 把它冷到一些磚塊中 , 讓它可能被用來做為社區內的材料 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和那些真的去過健身房的人談話 , 並在海洋環境中研究塑膠問題 , 我意識到 , 清潔是非常小的一滴 , 相對來說 , 每天在世界各地產生多少 , 實際上我需要回頭看看更大的照片 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的圖片是:我們需要找到一種方法來關掉水龍頭 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切割使用者和可用塑膠的位置 , 每天都要進入海洋環境 , 以全球規模 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 仔細看 , 我也發現我真的很憤怒 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只在乎塑膠 , 你在太平洋中期想出來 , 我發現現在有十一個環節 , 在世界上五個大洋裡 , 可能有十一個塑膠 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不光是那種我關心的塑膠 , 它是超市裡的塑膠 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 所有的食物都是塑膠包裝 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都是塑膠包裝 , 甚至在健康食品市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也擔心冰箱裡的塑膠 , 我擔心塑膠和毒素 , 會從塑膠滲透到我們體內 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群人聚集在一起 , 他們都在研究這個議題 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有很多計畫正在進行 , 但其中有些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	第一:如果我們在海洋中發現的80%到90%的海洋碎片是塑膠 , 那我們為什麼不稱它為 「 海洋 」 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收每個人的書 , 都是關於永續發展和綠化 , 都包含回收的概念 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把東西放在一個垃圾桶裡 , 你不需要再想一次 。
what is the reality of that ?	這是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 只有不到7%的塑膠回收 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你仔細觀察 , 特別是談到塑膠瓶 , 大部份只會被低收回收 , 或被刺激 , 或運送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它的循環被轉換成比較少的東西 , 玻璃瓶可以是玻璃瓶 , 或也可以再次使用塑膠瓶 , 絕對不會是塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件我們正在看的東西 , 請大家思考的是 , 我們把第四個r加到 「 減少、再利用、回收 」 的前面 , 三個r就拒絕了 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	無論何時可能 , 都拒絕使用單一和可用的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 ; 有些則是很古老的學齡 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我自己現在在收集這些冷酷的pyrex容器 , 用這些裝置 , 而不是glad和tuperware的容器來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我對自己和我的家人做了一個服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	很容易拿起一瓶不穩定的酒瓶或玻璃瓶 , 如果你在旅行 , 你忘了把你的不穩定的酒瓶裝滿水或過濾水 , 或購買塑膠瓶裝水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我想我想要告訴在座的每一個人 , 我知道你們對這個問題的了解是 , 這在海洋中是個大問題 , 但身為消費者 , 我們所造成的是一個大問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以解決這個問題 , 藉由提高人們對問題的意識 , 並教導人們選擇替代品 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 每當可能有機會選擇使用單一塑膠的替代品 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這條線切割成海洋 , 這樣一來 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的地球 , 拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	來自麻省理工學院的pattiemaes實驗室的示範 , 是由pranviburtry所引發的 , 是ted的buzz 。 它是一個可以穿戴的裝置 , 用這個投影機來描繪我們和環境的互動 。 想像一下 , " 少數性報告 " 再加上一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	demo , 設計 , 介面設計 , 技術 , 科技 。
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	pattiemaes和panav錯過了第六個感應器 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我對這個問題很有興趣:我們能否進化或發展出第六感 , 讓人們可以輕鬆地取得無縫的資訊 , 或簡單地取得資料 , 或可能存在的資訊 , 可以協助我們做出正確的決定 , 關於我們所面對的一切 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	有些人可能會認為 , 現今的手機已經不行了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted認識某個人 , 這當然是最頂尖的網絡地點 , 你不會握手 , 然後說: 「 你能拿出手機 , google嗎 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或者當你去超市 , 你站在那一大堆不同的馬桶文件裡 , 你不會拿出你的手機 , 打開一個瀏覽器 , 試著去決定哪個不同的馬桶文件是最環保的購買 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以我們並不容易取得相關的資訊 , 只能協助我們做出最佳的決定 , 關於下一步該怎麼做 , 以及該採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究小組開發了一系列的發明 , 讓我們能以一種簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 而不需要使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡是為了揭露我們最新的努力 , 目前為止 , 最成功的努力 , 目前還在處理過程中仍是非常重要的工作 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	我現在正戴著這個裝置 , 我們把它和架上的零件混合在一起 , 順便一提 , 目前的成本只有350美元 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我戴著照相機 , 只是個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜式的電池投影系統 , 用鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件跟我口袋裡的手機溝通 , 它是溝通和計算裝置 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生帕納•密特瑞 , 他真的是導入和設計整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統讓他走到任何表面 , 開始用他的手來和他面前投影的資訊互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統追蹤了四隻手指 。
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他戴著你可能認出的簡單標記帽 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要更風格的版本 , 你也可以用不同顏色畫出你的指甲 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	基本上 , 攝影機會追蹤這四隻手指並辨識出他製作的任何手勢 , 例如 , 一個長沙的地圖 , 放大 , 等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	系統也能辨識出像 「 拍照 」 的指標手勢 , 然後拍一張你面前的任何東西 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以直接走到任何一面牆上 , 投射所有他拍攝的照片 , 把它們整理 , 再次重組 , 再次使用所有自然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	有些人可能在兩年前就在這裡看到jefhan或你們之中有人會想: 「 嗯 , 這不像微軟的表面桌子嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也用天然手勢來互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但不同的是 , 你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西可以用 , 和這個投影資料互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是可攜式的 , 可以是......
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	所以 , 有一個很重要的差別是 , 它完全是行動的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的差別是 , 在大量生產中 , 這不會比現今的手機更耗費 , 也不會是更大的包裝 , 會比我在脖子上穿的版本更為風格 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但 , 除了讓你們之外 , 在《少數報告》中 , 湯姆•克魯斯的幻想 , 我們之所以對這個裝置感到很興奮 , 是因為它可以扮演第六感的裝置之一 , 讓你有相關的資訊 , 讓你知道在你面前的任何東西 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	我們看到帕納走進超市 , 他正在購買一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起產品時 , 系統能辨識出他所拿的產品 , 用的是影像辨識或標記技術 , 給他綠光或橘色光 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以要求額外的資訊 。
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以這個特別的選擇 , 在他個人的標準下 , 是一個特別好的選擇 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	在座可能有人會希望廁所紙 , 上面有最多的白化紙 , 而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他就可以拿到亞馬遜的評分 , 它就會被投影在書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是胡安的書 , 我們先前的演講者 , 順便說一下 , 在亞馬遜 , 得到了很大的評價 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕納翻了書的頁面 , 再看看書讀者留言的額外資訊 , 可能是他的最愛評論者的資訊 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他轉向某個特定的頁面 , 他可能會發現一個我們朋友的註解 , 給他一些關於那個頁面上的資訊 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙 , 它永遠不會被過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以在你閱讀的事件中得到最新的體育分數 。
this is a more controversial one .	這更具爭議性 。
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你和ted的某人互動 , 也許你會看到標籤的雲 , 和那個人在他們的部落格和個人網頁裡的字詞 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個例子中 , 學生對攝影機很感興趣 , 等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你去機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機證 , 它可以告訴你 , 你的航班延遲了 , 大門已經改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道目前的情況 , 就跟手臂上的手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	這就是我們目前正在發展的第六感 , 讓我們無縫接觸到關於我們可能發生的事情的相關資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕拉夫 , 她真的 , 像我說的 , 背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他的確值得很多掌聲 , 因為我不認為他在過去三個月就睡得太多了 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女友也可能對他也不滿意 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但它還不完美 , 它在進步中非常多 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道 , 或許在接下來的十年 , 我們將會與第六次的大腦植入 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲利斯•羅德里格茲和艾瑞莎•艾瓦菲有強大的友誼 , 來自世界貿易中心的兒子 , 在2001年9月11日被殺害 ; 伊爾瓦菲的兒子撒沙歐被定罪在那些襲擊中 , 被定罪了 , 希望能找到和平 , 這兩位母親希望能互相了解和尊重 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治、政治、
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	9/11的療癒:那些發現寬恕、友誼、友誼的母親 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	菲利斯•羅德里格茲:我們今天在這裡 , 是因為我們有大部分人認為非凡的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 我們現在感覺很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次發現我兒子在世界貿易中心在2001年9月11日早上 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否死了 , 直到三十六個小時之後 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道它是政治性的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家會怎麼做 , 以我們兒子的名字 , 奧蘭多 , 我和我的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它時 , 很震驚的是 , 我們的生命中糟糕的爆炸 , 真的是 , 我們沒有被復仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾個禮拜後 , zacariasussaoui被指控為六個數量的陰謀 , 致命恐怖主義 , 而美國政府要求為他致命 , 如果定罪了 , 我的丈夫和我的先生在公開場合發聲 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過人權團體 , 我們和許多其他受害者的家人聚集在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到艾妮莎 , 她兒子被指控 , 我心想: 「 什麼是勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 當我更強壯的時候 , 我想要和那個女人見面 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我仍然在深深的悲慟中 ; 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道我有一天會找到她 , 或我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我兒子是受害者時 , 我立刻得到了同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她的兒子被指控了什麼 , 她沒有得到那同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的苦難和我一樣 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	我們在2002年11月認識了 , 艾icha現在會告訴你這怎麼來的 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:下午 , 各位先生女士 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariassaoui的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我請人權組織讓我聯絡受害者的父母 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我到五個家庭 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到phyllis , 我看著她 。
she was the only mother in the group .	她是群體中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他人則是兄弟姊妹 。
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我在她的眼中看到她是個母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	我身為母親 , 遭受許多苦難 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我14歲時結婚 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 那時我十六歲 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	zacaria的故事實在太多了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	我仍然受苦 , 因為我的兒子就像活著一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為她的兒子哭了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我兒子不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 , 我不知道他是不是被虐待 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	所以 , 這就是為什麼我決定要說我的故事 , 所以我的痛苦對其他女性來說是正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對於所有婦女 , 所有給予生命的媽媽 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	取決於我們女性 , 因為我們是女性 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們必須親手合作 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不反對女性 , 而是為了我們 , 為我們女性 , 為我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我反對暴力 , 反對恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校和年輕的穆斯林女孩談 , 這樣她們就不接受婚姻 , 她們的意願很年輕 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一個女孩 , 避免她們結婚 , 和我一樣受苦 , 嗯 , 這是好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是為什麼我會站在你們面前 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	pr:我想說我從aicha身上學到很多 , 從那天起 , 我們第一次和其他家庭成員見面 , 那是一個非常私人的會議 , 因為那是2002年11月 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕那個國家的超級病菌 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都非常緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 為什麼她想要認識我們 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	然後她又緊張了 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 我們為什麼要見她 ? 」
what did we want from each other ?	我們想要對方的是什麼 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們認識彼此的名字之前 , 或任何東西之前 , 我們都擁抱和哭泣了 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	然後我們坐在一個圓圈裡 , 帶著幫助 , 從人們體驗到這種和解 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子是否有罪惡感或無辜 , 但我想告訴各位 , 我對你的家庭發生的狀況有多麼遺憾 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道那就是要受苦 , 我覺得如果有犯罪 , 一個人應該要被公平的審判和懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她用那樣的方式向我們伸出援手 , 我想要說 , 那是個冰鞋 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接下來發生的是 , 我們都說了我們的故事 , 我們都是人類的連結 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	下午就結束了 , 午餐後的三小時 , 我們覺得好像已經認識彼此了 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的是 , 一個女人 , 不僅是如此慷慨 , 在這些現況下 , 以及當時的狀況 , 以及她兒子所做的 , 還有她所擁有的人生 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇見過這麼艱困的人 , 來自完全不同的文化和環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一個特別的連結 , 我非常重視 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我想這全是為了要害怕另一個人 , 但要踏出那一步 , 然後意識到: 「 嘿 , 這一點都不困難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能和誰見面 , 我不知道 , 或我和誰很不一樣 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , 阿icha , 你有幾個字要做結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	aw:我想說我們必須試著認識他人 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須慷慨 , 你的心一定是慷慨的 , 你的心一定是慷慨的 。
you must be tolerant .	你一定是寬容的 。
you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。
and i hope that someday we'll all live together in peace and respecting each other .	我希望有一天我們會一起生活在和平中 , 互相尊重 。
this is what i wanted to say .	這是我想要說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	太多世界缺乏乾淨飲用水的管道工程師麥可•普林特發明了可攜帶的生物過濾器 , 可以在2009年tedglobal的一個令人驚訝的示範 。
business , demo , design , global issues , invention , technology , water	商業、示範、設計、全球議題、發明、科技、水、水、水、
michael pritchard's water filter turns filthy water drinkable	麥可•普林特的水過濾器 , 會讓骯髒的水飲用 , 變成可飲用的水 。
i'd like to talk about a couple of things today .	今天我想談談幾件事 。
the first thing is water .	第一件事是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都在享受這次會議提供的水 , 在過去幾天你們都在享受 。
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得這是安全的來源 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果不是呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果它是來自這樣的源頭呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	接著 , 統計數字會說你們當中有一半的人現在會遭受腹瀉的苦難 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	過去我常常談到統計數字 , 提供安全飲用水給所有人 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但他們似乎不會穿透 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我已經知道為什麼了 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	因為 , 使用目前的思考 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 無法解決 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們關掉:我們、政府和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	今天 , 我想用不同的角度來說明 , 問題已經解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順便一提 , 自從我談話以來 , 世界各地有一萬三千人受痢疾所苦 。
and four children have just died .	四個孩子剛過世了 。
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了生命安全瓶 , 因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和你們大部分人一樣 , 在2004年的聖誕節那天 , 我看著亞洲海嘯的令人沮喪消息 , 因為它在電視上播放 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的幾週 , 人們逃到山上 , 被迫喝下污染的水或死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	這真的困擾了我 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	接著 , 幾個月後 , 颶風卡崔娜陷入美國邊 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 , 」 我心想: 「 這是第一個世界國家 , 咱們來看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道要花五天才能把水送到超級中嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上為電視設置和水拍攝彼此 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那時我決定要做點什麼 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	現在我花了很多時間在我的車庫裡 , 在接下來的幾週、幾個月 , 在廚房裡 , 我太太太的不滿 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 在幾次失敗的原型之後 , 我終於想到了這個 , 救命的瓶子 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好 , 現在來談科學 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在救命者之前 , 最好的手過濾器只能過濾大約200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以一個200奈米的細菌會穿過一個200奈米的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以這絕對會穿過那200奈米的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	救命者池塘是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 沒有任何東西能穿透 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好吧 , 我來示範一下 。
would you like to see that ?	你想要看到嗎 ?
i spent all the time setting this up , so i guess i should .	我花了很多時間把這些設定好 , 我想我應該這樣做 。
we're in the fine city of oxford .	我們在牛津的最好城市 。
so someone's done that up .	有人已經完成了 。
fine city of oxford , so what i've done is i've gone and got some water from the river cherwell , and the river thames , that flow through here . and this is the water .	牛津的好城市 , 所以我做的是從河流中取得一些水 , 還有河流的山姆 , 流過這裡 。 這就是水 。
but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我想 , 如果我們在孟加拉的洪水區中央 , 水就不會像這樣 。
so i've gone and got some stuff to add into it .	所以 , 我做了一些東西來加入它 。
and this is from my pond .	這是我的池塘 。
have a smell of that , mister cameraman .	聞一下 , 攝影師先生 。
we're just going to pour that in there .	我們只會把它倒進去 。
michael pritchard: okay . we've got some runoff from a sewage plant farm .	michaelpritchard:好的 , 我們有一些從污水處理廠跑來的 。
so i'm just going to put that in there .	所以我就把它放進去 。
put that in there . there we go .	把它放進去 , 就這樣 。
and some other bits and pieces , chuck that in there .	還有一些碎片 , 把它蓋在裡面 。
and i've got a gift here from a friend of mine's rabbit .	我這裡有個禮物 , 來自我的朋友的兔子 。
so we're just going to put that in there as well .	所以 , 我們也要把它放進去 。
the lifesaver bottle works really simply .	救生員的瓶子很簡單 。
you just scoop the water up .	你只要把水放上去 。
today i'm going to use a jug just to show you all . let's get a bit of that poo in there .	今天我要用一個評斷來給你們看 。 讓我們看看裡面的一些小馬 。
that's not dirty enough . let's just stir that up a little bit .	這還不夠髒 。 讓我們稍微攪拌一下 。
okay , so i'm going to take this really filthy water , and put it in here . do you want a drink yet ?	好吧 , 我要把這個非常骯髒的水放進去 。 你還想要喝醉了嗎 ?
okay . there we go .	好了 , 來了 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給它一些幫浦 。 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	這些都是必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一旦我打開茶 , 無菌的飲用水就會出現 。
i've got to be quick . okay , ready ?	我必須很快 。 好 , 準備好了嗎 ?
there we go . mind the electrics .	來了 。 請注意電 。
that is safe , sterile drinking water .	那是安全的、無菌的飲用水 。
there you go chris .	這裡是克里斯 。
what's it taste of ?	牠嚐到什麼 ?
let's see chris's program throughout the rest of the show . okay ?	咱們來看看克里斯在其餘的節目 。 好嗎 ?
okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好 , 世界各地數以千計的人使用了救命瓶 。
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	它會維持6 , 000公升 。
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	當它被啟發時 , 使用失敗的技術 , 系統會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	把車禍趕出去 , 打進去 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	這對六千公升來說是好的 。
so let's look at the applications .	咱們來看看應用程式 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	幾個禮拜後 , 我們設立營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫進入營地 , 以取得安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在營地時 , 會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病散播 。 需要更多的資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題就變成自我繁殖 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但藉由不同的思考 , 運送這些資訊 , 人們就可以留在上面 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自己製造無菌飲用水 , 開始重建家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	這並不需要自然災害才能運作 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	使用舊的想法 , 國家基礎建設和管子工作太貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你在計算機上運算時 , 你就會跑出去 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這裡是 「 思考不同 」 的部分 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	不是運送水 , 而是用人造的過程來做 , 讓我們用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡拿起水 , 免費地將水淡化 , 運送到那裡 , 把它丟到山上 , 河流 , 河流 。
and where do people live ? near water .	人們住在哪裡 ? 附近的水 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們要做的就是讓它變得無菌 。 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	嗯 , 我們可以用 「 救命奶瓶 」 。
or we could use one of these .	或者我們可以使用其中一種 。
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的技術 , 在吉利的罐子裡 。
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這會處理25 , 000公升的水 ; 這足夠給四個家庭 , 三年之久 。
and how much does it cost ?	它要花多少錢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	一天大概半美分 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 用不同的方式思考 , 處理用水 , 母親和孩子不再需要每天走四個小時來收集他們的水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的來源取得它 。
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	所以 , 只要花八十億美金 , 我們就能達到千禧目標 , 目標是要在沒有安全飲用水的情況下 , 把人數減少 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	把這些數據歸納為背景 , 英國政府每年花費大約一百二十億英鎊給外國援助 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼要停下來 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	只要兩百億美金 , 每個人都能取得安全的飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	因此 , 每年有三百五十億人遭受苦難 , 而每年死亡的兩百萬個孩子 , 會活下來 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	paddyashown聲稱我們現在生活在歷史上 , 權力正在改變 , 以往從來沒有的方式改變 。 在tedxbrussel的演講中 , 他指出他所看到的三個重大全球變遷 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策、全球議題、政治、世界文化、文化、
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	paddyashown:全球權力轉移 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	在19世紀末 , 有一首非常有名的英文詩人寫的詩 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	有人說 , 在1930年代 , 教堂的大腦會回響 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩寫著: 「 在夏天的伊德山丘上 , 帶著溪流的懶惰 , 哈克我聽到一個遙遠的鼓聲 , 像在夢境中的聲音 , 遙遠、低沉 , 越來越大聲在地球的道路上 , 親愛的朋友和食物到粉末 , 士兵遊行 , 很快就死了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩感興趣的人 , 這首詩是 「 鯊魚夏的老人 」 , 由霍斯曼寫的 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但housman了解的 , 你也聽到尼爾森的交響聲 , 就是19世紀長、炎熱、silvan夏天的穩定性已經近了 , 我們即將進入歷史中最可怕的時代之一 , 當權力改變時 , 我們即將進入一個可怕的時代 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	女士們先生們 , 這些經常伴隨著亂流 , 經常被血液吸收 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	而我要告訴你們的訊息是 , 我相信我們被譴責 , 如果你喜歡 , 我們只能生活在歷史上的那些時刻 , 那時 , 權力的基礎已經開始改變 , 世界的新力量 , 已經開始形成 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	今天我們很清楚地看到 , 幾乎總是高頻的亂流 , 極度困難的時光 , 且常常常是非常血腥的時代 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順便說一下 , 每一世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會認為 , 上次發生的事件 , 休士曼的感受也即將來臨 , 教堂的感覺也一樣 , 當權力從舊國家通過 , 歐洲的舊勢力 , 橫跨大西洋 , 到美國的新興勢力 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在真空中 , 以前的歐洲權力被用在上個世紀的兩個血腥災難中 , 第一部份和第二部分是:兩次世界大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經稱他們為歐洲內戰 , 可能是更精確的描述他們的方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	女士們先生們 , 我們生活在其中之一 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天要談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	首先 , 這兩者的第一件事 , 是關於權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個則是關於一些新的維度我想提一下 , 它從來沒有發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但讓我們來談談發生在世界的權力轉變 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的事 , 在某種意義上 , 很恐怖 , 因為它從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經看到希臘傳遞給羅馬的權力轉移 , 以及在歐洲文明中發生的權力轉移 , 但我們卻看到一些不一樣的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力不只是從國家到國家的後續發展 。
it's also moving vertically .	它的垂直移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今正在發生的是 , 被監控的權力 , 被拘留在法律的法則上 , 在國家國家的制度中 , 已經大幅地移民到全球舞台 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	我們談到全球化的權力 , 其實是真正的權力 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層級 , 權力被迫要負責法律的法則 , 在國際舞台上 , 它不是 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球舞台現在權力充足:網路的力量、衛星廣播的力量 , 金錢改變了這個巨大的金錢轉動了三十二倍 , 交易的金額 , 該有金錢去補助金轉變者 , 假如你喜歡 , 金融推測者將我們所有人帶到我們膝蓋的金融推動力 , 最近 , 跨國企業的金融預算 , 通常比起大規模發展 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個完全沒有規範的全球空間裡 , 而不是受到法律規範 , 而在這樣的環境下 , 人們就不會受到限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在 , 這套裝置強大到一瞬間 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	總是適用於那些擁有最權力的人 , 不受限制的限制 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 很快地 , 不受規範的法律限制 , 不只被你想要的國際貿易、網路等等 。 還有你不想要的國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	9/11的啟示是 , 即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 那些住在那空間的人 , 仍然可以攻擊你最具代表性的城市──一個九月的早晨 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 被帶到911事件的四百萬美金中 , 大約有60%通過雙胞胎大樓 , 911事件摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	我們的敵人也使用這個空間 , 大眾旅行、網路、衛星廣播公司 , 來繞過他們的毒品 , 重點是要摧毀我們的系統和我們的方式 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	很快的 , 不久後 , 歷史的規則就是權力統治的目的必須跟隨著 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	所以 , 正如我所說的 , 正如我所說的 , 我們這個時代的一種現象是全球化的權力 , 那麼我們這個時代的挑戰之一就是把治理帶到全球空間 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 未來的幾十年 , 我們將成為更大或更少的亂流 , 我們愈能達成這個目標:把治理帶到全球空間 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	請注意 , 我不是在談政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在談建立一些全球民主制度 。
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順帶一提 , 我自己的看法是 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們 , 女士們不太可能通過擴散更多聯合國機構來做 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際論壇 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一個可以合法化的國際行動的手段 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但 , 談到全球空間的治理 , 我想這不會發生在聯合國機構的創造中 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	它會發生 , 是因為強大的力量聚集在一起 , 建立以條約為基礎的系統 , 合約的協議 , 來管理這個全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看的話 , 你可以看到它們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:以條約為基礎的組織 , 完全以條約為基礎 , 強大的力量 , 能夠容納最強大、最強大的美國 , 如果有必要的話 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	kyoto:努力努力創造出一個條約性的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	g20:我們現在知道我們必須組合一個機構 , 能夠把治理帶到金融空間給金融的猜想 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	而這就是g20所謂的 「 合約的機構 」 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有個問題 , 我們等一下會再回來談 , 如果你把最強大的權力集合起來 , 用以條約為基礎的機構來制定規則 , 填補那個治理空間 , 那弱勢人會怎麼辦 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個很大的問題 , 我們只要一秒鐘就能回報 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個訊息是 , 如果你要傳遞這些亂流的次數 , 那麼 , 我們的成功程度就大致上取決於我們的能力 , 把合理的治理帶到全球空間 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著它開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要跟這樣的觀眾談這件事 , 但權力不只垂直轉移 , 同時也在地平線轉變 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會認為 , 人類文明的歷史一直被文明聚集在海洋附近 , 在地中海周圍 , 最近在大西洋的力量下 , 越是近期 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	對我來說 , 我們現在看到的似乎是權力轉變的基本轉變 , 廣泛地說 , 從大西洋的國家聚集在一起 , 到太平洋的國家 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這從經濟力量開始 , 但這一直是這樣開始的 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外交政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增 , 發生在世界上其他成長的力量 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為 , 這並不是西方國家轉移到東邊 , 有些不同的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 美國在接下來的十年 , 十五年 , 仍然是地球上最強大的國家 , 但她掌握權力的背景 , 現在已經徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們已經走出50年 , 最不尋常的歷史 , 在這個歷史中 , 我們有一個完全獨立的單一世界 , 在這個世界中 , 每一個同伴都必須被它的位置所指出 , 一個由一個巨人所組成的世界 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這在歷史上並不常見 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在出現的是更正常的歷史案例 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到多極化世界的出現 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	目前為止 , 美國一直是我們世界的主流特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	它們會維持最強大的國家 , 但它們會是越來越多極化的世界中最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	而你會開始看到在中國建立權力的替代中心 , 當然 , 但我自己的猜測是 , 中國的高興不是平滑的 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	當中國在自由化經濟後 , 將開始民主化她的社會 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但這是個不同的討論 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到印度、巴西 。
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你現在看到的其實是歐洲人的樣子 , 更像是19世紀的歐洲人 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	十九世紀 , 歐洲是一名英國外交部長 , 總統 , 常被描述為 「 歐洲權力協會 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一個平衡 , 五面體的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是在平衡中演奏 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林結合 , 英國和維也納和羅馬合作 , 來提供平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在這個由單一世界所主導的時期 , 你已經修復了北約聯盟 , 巴薩•帕特 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	一個固定的權力的兩極代表著固定的盟友 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但多重權力的兩極意味著改變和改變盟友 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們正在進入的世界 , 我們會漸漸看到我們的聯盟並沒有固定 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	大英外交秘書曾說: 「 英國有共同的利益 , 但沒有常見的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會發現 , 即使我們在西方國家都能伸出援手 , 必須伸出援手 , 超越大西洋力量之外的舒適圈 , 才能和其他人聯盟 , 如果我們想要讓事情在世界上完成 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 西方國家並不夠好 ; 我們必須把其他人帶進來 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	在這個例子中 , 我們得帶入阿拉伯聯盟 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗是西方試圖自己做這件事的最後一次 , 我們還沒成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是400年底 , 我說是400年底 , 因為它是西方權力、西方制度和西方價值觀的終結 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家團結起來 , 它可以在世界的每一個角落提出並消除 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不對了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以第二次世界大戰後最後的金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方國家集合了布雷頓森林機構 , 世界銀行 , 國際貨幣基金 , 問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須打電話給別人 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造g20 。
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須超越西方朋友的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為你做個預測 , 這可能更令人驚訝 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我猜我們已經達到400年的終點了 , 西方國家的權力已經足夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國人 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會參與到和平的活動 , 全世界的多邊和平組織 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	喔 , 為什麼不呢 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色的貝雷下服役 , 在藍旗下服役 , 在聯合國指令下服役 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	多少美國人 ? 11人 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	什麼是最大的海軍陸戰隊處理索馬利海盜議題 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國海軍聯盟 。
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是商業主義者 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想要讓海道開放 。
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和那些我們不分享價值的人做生意 , 但 , 在當下 , 我們有共同的興趣 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一個全新的觀點 , 看這個正在興起的世界 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素是完全不同的 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	現今 , 在我們的現代世界裡 , 由於網路 , 因為人們在這裡所談論的東西 , 所有東西都被連結在一起 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是互相依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在被交織 , 作為一個國家 , 作為一個個體 , 一個從來沒有發生過的案例 , 從來沒有發生過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國家的關聯性總是存在 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交的重點是要管理國家之間的關聯 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們密切關在一起 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥得到豬流感 , 這個問題在24小時後 , 查爾斯•德•高爾機場是個問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟會下降 , 整體的崩潰 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯的步驟有火災 , 非洲的食物暴動 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深深地相互連結著 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著一個國家單獨行動的概念 , 而不是與他人連結 , 也不是與他人合作 , 也不再是一個可行的提議 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為國家的動作既不被限制 , 也不足以控制國家本身 , 來控制自己的領土 , 因為國家之外的影響已經開始影響他們 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是英國帝國戰爭的年輕士兵 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	當時 , 我國家的防禦是一件事 , 唯一的一件事:我們的軍隊有多強大 , 我們的空軍有多強大 , 我們的海軍有多強大 , 我們的盟友有多強壯 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那時候敵人就在牆外 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在敵人在牆壁裡 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	如果我想要談談我國家的防禦 , 我必須和健康部談 , 因為流行病對我的安全有威脅 , 我必須和農業部長談 , 因為食物安全對我的安全有威脅 , 我必須和產業的部長談談 , 因為我們希臘基礎建設的脆弱是對我們的敵人 , 如我們從網路戰爭到我所看到的 , 我們的敵人 , 直接在我的國家 , 因為在家裡 , 被我們所影響的房子裡 , 被迫害 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	再也不是一個國家的安全對其士兵和國防部而言是很重要的 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它是將其制度結合在一起的能力 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴你們一件非常重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直建構 , 建立在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 垂直層級制度 , 專業任務 , 指令結構完全錯了 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在商業界 , 你知道我們這個時代的典範結構 , 各位先生們 , 是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	它是你網路的能力 , 無論在你的政府或外部都很重要 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	下面是第三法則 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順便說一下 , 不要問我 「 崩潰 」 的第一法律和第二定律 , 因為我還沒發明這些法律 ; 如果有第三條法律的話 , 聽起來比較好 , 對吧 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	第三條法則是 , 在現代時代 , 一切都和一切有關 , 最重要的事就是你能做的是你能和他人做的事 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的一點是你是政府 , 不論你是軍隊註冊 , 不論你是企業 , 都是你和他人的間接點 , 你和他人建立網路的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你明白這一點在產業 , 政府不了解 。
but now one final thing .	但最後一件事情 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣 , 各位先生女士 , 我們現在被困在一種以前從來沒有相同的方式 , 那也是我們彼此的命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 第一次 , 集體防禦 , 主宰了我們國家的概念 , 已經不夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前的情況是 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我是安全的 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我是安全的 ; 我的聯盟 , 像是nato , 比他們的盟友更強大 , 我是安全的 。
it is no longer the case .	已經不再是這樣了 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	相互關聯的出現 , 以及大規模毀滅的武器 , 意味著 , 漸漸地 , 我和敵人分享了一個命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我是外交官 , 在1970年代 , 我和日內瓦的蘇聯談判 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們了解我們和他們分享了命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全不夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為兩邊都知道 , 零和遊戲無法運作 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人分享命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	在中東 , 和平的大障礙之一就是以色列和巴勒斯坦人都不了解他們有共同的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 女士們先生們 , 過去的願景和詩人 , 都變成了我們必須認真看待的公共政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 我會用一首詩來結束 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐妮的偉大詩 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 送給誰鈴 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 " 沒有人是一座島 " 。
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	內容是: 「 每個人的死亡都會影響我 , 因為我參與的人 , 不要去問鐘響 , 要為你賺錢 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對於約翰•唐納 , 道德的建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	我認為 , 對我們來說 , 方程式的一部分是為了生存 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽、健康、丹•布希特納和團隊 , 研究世界的 「 藍色區域 」 , 他們的長者和vim一起生活 , 在tedxtc , 記錄了九項常見的飲食和生活習慣 , 讓他們能撐過一百歲 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學、科學、科學、科學、
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuettner:要如何活到100+ 。
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	丹麥雙胞胎研究指出 , 在某些生物限制下 , 平均壽命只有百分之十 , 是由我們的基因決定 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外百分之九十是由我們的生活方式所主宰 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍色區塊的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能想出一個真正的公式來長壽 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般的美國人長壽的最佳公式 , 他們可能不會告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽過南海灘飲食 , 或墨水飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國食品金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲醫生告訴我們 ,
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 對於真正幫助我們活得更好的事物 , 有很多疑惑 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜伽 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉還是應該吃豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到補給品時 , 你應該拿它們嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	那麼這些荷爾蒙或逆向劑呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的是否有目的 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性 ? 那麼我們如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們找到長壽的方法是和國家地理頻道合作 , 國家老化研究所 , 找出四個人口統計區域 , 地理學界定的區域 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	把一組專家帶進來 , 用方法來處理這些人所做的事 , 來分析跨文化的干擾 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴各位這是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但 , 首先 , 我想要破除一些常見的迷思 , 談到長壽 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你真的努力 , 你就能活到100歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國大約有五千人當中只有一人活到一百歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機率很低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	雖然美國人口成長最快 , 但卻很難達到100 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們並不是為了長壽而編寫的 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被設計為一種叫做 「 繁榮成功 」 的東西 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它讓我想起我大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱之為 「 繁衍成功 」 , 意思是你有孩子的年齡 , 接著是另一個世代 , 當你的孩子有小孩時 , 年齡會變老 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在那之後 , 演化的效應完全消失了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是一隻哺乳動物 , 如果你是一隻老鼠或一隻大象 , 或人 , 在兩者之間 , 則是相同的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 要讓它變成一百歲 , 你不但得要有很好的生活方式 , 你也得要贏得基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療可以協助減緩、逆轉 , 甚至阻止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	想想看 , 有9件事情可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要幾分鐘 , 那些腦細胞就會死亡 , 它們就不會回來了 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	打網球太硬 , 在你的膝蓋上 , 磨損你的軟骨 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈會堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用白斑點連接 , 我們就能得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情要出錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 用 「 t 」 來表示國家債務數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	這些細胞每八年一次一次就轉一次一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們轉到那裡 , 就會造成一些損害 。 損害就會增加 。
and it builds up exponentially .	它以指數型的方式建造 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像是當我們有披頭四的專輯或老鷹專輯時 , 我們會在錄音帶上複製 , 讓朋友在錄音錄音帶上複製 , 很快地 , 錄音帶的成功世代聽起來像垃圾 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼65歲的人老化速度比12歲的人快125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果你沒有辦法減緩老化或阻止老化 , 我在這裡幹什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	事實上 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人類身體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約是90年 , 對女性來說 , 有些更多 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家 , 平均壽命只有78 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以在這條線上 , 我們離開了大約十二年 , 在桌上 。
these are years that we could get .	這些是我們能得到的年份 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 這些年來 , 幾乎沒有慢性疾病、心臟疾病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 要消失這些年份最好的方法就是看看全世界的文化 , 實際上正在經歷的文化 , 在那裡 , 人們生活的比例比我們年齡一百倍 , 比我們多出十幾年的壽命 , 中年的死亡率是美國的一小部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們在義大利海岸找到第一條藍色地帶大約125英里 , 在薩丁尼亞島上 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	而不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有1400萬人 , 但只有在高地 , 一個叫做nuoro省的區域 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡我們有這個區域 , 男人的壽命最長 , 大約比美國這裡的百歲人多十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不只達到100歲 , 還能用非凡的處女做這件事 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	在那裡 , 102歲的老人仍然騎腳踏車去工作 , 蕭邦 , 打敗一個比他們年輕60歲的人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史回溯到基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	它實際上是一個被隔離的銅時代文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為這塊土地很有推論性 , 它們大多是牧羊 , 偶爾 , 體力較低的活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食主要是以植物為主 , 主要是以食物為主 , 他們可以帶到田野中 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出了一種未釋放的全麥麵包 , 叫做carta音樂 , 用小麥做成的一種乳酪 , 來自草動物 , 所以乳酪在omega-3脂肪酸 , 而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 來自玉米的動物 , 還有一種葡萄酒 , 比世界上任何葡萄酒都要高三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但真正的秘密在於他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會中最強烈的元素之一就是他們對待老人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你曾注意到 , 在美國 , 社會平等似乎在24歲時達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞這裡 , 你的年紀越平等 , 你就越有智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧 , 而不是看到運動畫面上的游泳日曆 , 你看到月曆的百歲人 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 這不僅對你的老父母來說是好事 , 讓他們和家人更接近 , 平均壽命只有四到六年的研究顯示 , 對那些家庭的孩子來說 , 死亡率較低 , 疾病的比例也較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這就是所謂的祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一側發現了第二個藍色區域 , 位於東京的南方約800英哩 , 位在okinawa的亞吉拉契島 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在主島的北部 , 這是世界長壽的零地 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這個地方是最老的女性族群被發現的地方 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	在那裡 , 人們有世界上最長的殘疾壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	牠們活了很長一段時間 , 通常在牠們的睡眠中死亡 , 很快 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性愛之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們的平均壽命比美國人多了七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國有五倍的百歲人 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	美國有五分之一的蟻群和乳癌 , 大型殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的第六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實上 , 這種文化已經證實了這些數字 , 強烈地表示它們有東西可以教我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 以植物為基礎的飲食 , 裡面滿是蔬菜 , 裡面有很多顏色 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們和美國人吃大約八倍的豆腐 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃的東西更重要 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略來避免濫用 , 如你所知 , 這在美國是一個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:牠們吃掉較小的盤子 , 所以牠們通常在每一隻坐著時都少吃熱量 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其提供家庭風格 , 當你在談話時 , 你可以不經意地吃東西 , 他們會在櫃台上服務 , 把食物送走 , 然後把它送到桌上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	牠們還有3000歲的年紀 , 我認為這是史上最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由混合物所發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食就是所謂的 「 哈拉、哈特、哈特、伯食 」 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單來說 , 這些人在吃飯之前會說 , 要提醒他們在胃部滿是80%時停止飲食 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	要花上半個小時才能從肚子傳到大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住要停止80% , 它能協助你避免做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 像薩丁尼亞 , okinawa有一些社會結構 , 可以讓我們聯想到長壽 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會致命 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前 , 美國平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在只剩下一半 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你幸運生於奧金納瓦 , 你就生在一個系統裡 , 你自動生了半個朋友 , 和你一輩子的朋友 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為moai 。 如果你遇到運氣時 , 預期會有機會分享 , 如果不好的話 , 孩子就會生病 , 父母會死 , 你總是會有一個有你的背 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這位特殊的moai女士 , 九十七年來 ,
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成人的生活分成兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作生活 , 我們有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這意味著對簡單的椅子退休 , 或是去亞利桑那州打高爾夫球 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在okinawan語中 , 甚至連退休的詞都沒有 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之的是 , 整個人生都會有一個字 , 那個字是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大約是翻譯的意思是 「 你早上醒來的理由 。 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	在這102歲的凱爾特大師 , 他的ikigai帶著這件武術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	為了這位百歲的漁民 , 牠持續捕魚 , 每週三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 。 國家老化研究所給了我們一個問卷 , 給這些百歲人 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們是文化上很巧妙的 , 那些提出問題的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上起床 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對於這位102歲的老婦人 , 她的ikigai就只是她的曾曾曾曾曾曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩位女孩在101歲半之間分開 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 手上拿著曾曾曾祖母的感覺是什麼 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把她的頭放在後面 , 她說: 「 感覺就像跳上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得這是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我的地理編輯希望我找到美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一段時間 , 我們研究明尼蘇達的草原 , 事實上 , 百歲人的比例很高 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們又轉向數據了 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現 , 美國最長壽的一群人 , 在加州的第七天冒險家中 , 都聚集在洛馬林達 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	冒險家是保守派的方法論者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在週五日的日落慶祝他們的休息日 ,
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	一個 「 時間24小時的庇護所 」 , 他們稱之為 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 比較非凡的長壽 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均婦女平均壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一位先知的女性來說 , 他們的平均壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	差異在於男性之間 , 比起美國人的比例 , 比起美國人的比例 , 比起美國人的壽命還要高11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史特林研究 。 我認為它最能說明這個藍色區域計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異性戀的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	它是白人、黑人、西班牙人、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共通點 , 是一組非常小的生活習慣 , 他們大部分時間都遵循著儀式生活 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中取得飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	金恩:第一章 , 詩句是29種 。 上帝談到傳言和種子 , 再加上關於綠色植物的史丹扎 , 很明顯地 , 沒有肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真地看待這個庇護所 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週有24小時 , 不論他們多忙 , 工作壓力多大 , 孩子需要開車 , 他們會停止一切 , 專注在他們的神、他們的社交網路 , 然後 , 在宗教裡 , 大自然會走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這種力量的力量並不是偶爾完成 , 權力是每週一次完成一生 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	沒有任何一個很難 。 沒有一個成本 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	冒險家也傾向與其他冒險家相處 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一場冒險派對 , 你不會看到人們在吉姆姆姆姆光燈或開一個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	取而代之的是他們談到下一大自然走路、交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們會以深刻且可測量的方式影響彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化讓埃爾斯•沃爾森產生了伊麗莎 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	伊爾瑟•沃麗姆九十七歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是數百萬富翁 , 但當包商想要六千美金來建造隱私圍籬時 , 他說: 「 為了我自己去做這些錢 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天 , 他出去打擊水泥 , 繞過水面 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可想而知 , 也許在第四天 , 他最後到達了手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是那個在桌上的人 ; 做開心手術的人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	97歲時 , 他每個月仍然做了20次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•盧林斯現在已經有103歲了 , 一個活躍的牛仔 , 早晨就開始了游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡戴上板子 , 丟棄了羅斯特的尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在這兩個城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她從她的日子開始 , 帶著升重 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎著腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她在1994年的凱迪克賽維爾上車 , 淚流下了聖柏納迪諾高速公路 , 在那裡 , 她仍然志願七個不同的組織 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我經歷過19次重度探險 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是你遇見的唯一一個人 , 他騎腳踏車穿越撒哈拉沙漠 , 卻沒有防曬霜 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有冒險比起騎著馬gedeton的騎士更加沉重 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 這三種文化中的共同點是什麼 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們所做的事是什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功地把它歸還為九個 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 自從這之後 , 我們已經做了兩次藍色的探險 , 這些常見的探險人員就成真了 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我將要說清楚 , 沒有運動 , 至少我們對運動的看法 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們建立了自己的生命 , 讓他們不斷地被推進到實體活動中 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的okinawan女人站在地上 , 每天30到40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 樓梯上上下 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次旅行到商店 , 或教會或朋友家 , 都會去散步 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何便利 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕 , 來做yard工作或家庭工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們會用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	那種燃燒卡路里就像跑步機一樣 。
