when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做刻意的身體活動時 , 是他們喜愛的事物 , 他們傾向於走路 , 唯一證明的方式就是脫離認知的衰退 , 而他們都傾向有花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何用正確的方式生活 , 所以他們有正確的外觀 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一個文化都需要時間減少 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人禱告 。 第七天的冒險家祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawans有這樣的祖先揭露 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你在急促或緊張時 , 會觸發出一種叫做發炎反應的東西 , 和阿茲海默症的一切有關 , 到心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你每天放慢15分鐘 , 你就會把那發炎狀態轉為更反炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們的字彙有目的、ikigai , 像okinawannns 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 你退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道自己的目的 , 他們活躍在自己的人生中 , 這價值約七年的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	取而代之的是 , 這些人每天喝一點點酒 , 而不是賣給美國人 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們傾向於吃植物的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	並不是說牠們不吃肉 , 而是很多豆類和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略可以避免濫用 , 小東西在對的時間將它們推離桌子 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	這一切的基礎是他們如何連結的 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人首先關注 , 照顧他們的孩子 , 及老化的父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都傾向屬於信仰型的社區 , 值4到14年的預期壽命 , 如果你每個月做四次 ,
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是它們也屬於對的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生來就是活躍地圍繞著對的人 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從弗蘭罕姆研究得知 , 如果三個最好的朋友是肥胖的 , 會有50%的機率會過胖 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人住在一起 , 隨著時間 , 會有很大的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	取而代之 , 如果你的朋友對於娛樂的概念是實體活動 , 弓弦樂 , 或是彈奏曲棍球或花園 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點點 , 但他們吃的不太多 , 而且他們很投入 , 信任和值得信賴 , 這將會隨著時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食是行不通的 。 在歷史上 , 沒有飲食可以用在超過2%的人口上 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常是從一月開始的 ; 通常是十月份完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	當談到長壽時 , 沒有短期修復藥丸或其他藥品 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你仔細想想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許是你能做的最重要的事 , 多年來你的生活 。 非常謝謝你們 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	這種導電力的墨水 ; 一扇窗 , 從清晰轉換到開關 ; 一顆讓音樂產生的水母 。 所有的東西都存在 。 卡崔娜•莫塔說:該是播放的時候了 。 莫塔帶領我們參觀了驚喜且酷炫的新材料 , 建議我們找出他們對實驗的好處 , 重新做實驗 , 重新玩樂的方式 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力 , 設計 , 科技 , 科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:玩智能材料的玩樂 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一個在葡萄牙的朋友 , 他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機建造一輛車 , 讓他能運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他買不起一輛車 , 同時也因為他知道如何建造一輛車 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾有一段時間 , 我們明白事情是如何運作的 , 以及如何做出來的 , 這樣我們就能建造並修復它們 , 或是最少有知情的決策 , 來決定要買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在20世紀後半葉 , 許多這些獨裁的做法都消失了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造者和開源模型將這些知識帶入我們的生活中 , 我相信我們需要把這些知識帶到下一個層級 , 到構成的層級 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的情況下 , 我們仍然知道傳統的材料 , 像是紙和紡織品 , 還有它們是如何產生的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些奇妙的、具體的複合材料塑膠 , 會改變形狀、會導電、會改變顏色、會發光的顏色 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	導電墨水能讓我們繪製電路 , 而不是使用傳統印刷電路板或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	以我手上的這個小例子 , 我們用它來製造觸摸感測器 , 藉由啟動這個小光來對我的皮膚做出反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	導電墨水是藝術家用的 , 但近期的發展顯示 , 我們很快就能把它用在雷射印表機和筆上 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這是加入無色光傳輸粒子的水晶片 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然一般的阿克萊利亞只能在邊緣散射光線 , 但當我開燈時 , 整個表面照亮 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這種材料的兩種應用包括內部設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	而在特定溫度下 , 溫度會改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以我要把這個放在一個熱板上 , 它的溫度只比環境溫度稍高 , 你可以看到發生了什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	這種材料的原理之一是 , 在嬰兒瓶上 , 嬰兒瓶上 , 它會指出 , 當內容物夠酷的時候 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是一般所謂的智慧材料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們將成為我們每天使用的物體和技術 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛天車科幻小說給我們保證 , 但我們可以有一面牆來改變顏色 , 依照溫度 , 鍵盤 , 再捲起來 , 窗戶就會變成開關的不透明 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是一名社會科學家 , 為什麼我今天要談談智慧材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事情是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何製造的 , 同時也因為我相信我們應該更深入地了解構成我們世界的元件 , 而現在 , 我們對於這些高科技合成的未來不夠了解 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧材料很難在小量中取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何資訊可以用在如何使用它們 , 很少人會說它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 主要在貿易秘密和專利領域 , 只有大學和企業能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	所以 , 三年前 , kirsty男孩和我成立了一個專案 , 我們稱之為開放材料 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是一個網站 , 我們和任何想要加入我們的人 , 分享實驗、發表資訊 , 鼓勵其他人在任何時候都能做出貢獻 , 集體的資源 , 像是研究論文 , 和教學 , 由像我們一樣的創作者來 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為一個大型集體產生的資料庫 , 用智慧型材料來發送自身資訊 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但我們為什麼要在乎智慧型材料的運作 , 以及它們的組成是什麼 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的東西 , 我們不了解的東西 , 最終使用的東西會塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品、衣服、我們居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要生活在一個由智慧材料組成的世界 , 我們應該要知道並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新總是由tinker推動 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 不是專家 , 都是發明家 , 從山腳踏車到半導體 , 個人電腦 , 飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 物質科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但不見得都是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學的兩位科學家了解這一點 , 當他們發表了一個更簡單的方法 , 來製造導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker在那時完全沒有化學經驗 , 直到當時 , 他讀了這篇論文 , 用現成的物質和工具來進行實驗 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱 , 甚至用他自己的蒸氣混合器 , 基於另一位科學家/maker的導師 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	喬登後來在網路上發表他的結果 , 包括他嘗試過的所有事情 , 沒有用 , 其他人可以研究並複製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	約旦的主要創新形式是將一個在智能實驗室裡創造出來的實驗 , 並在芝加哥的車庫裡重建 , 只用便宜的材料和工具 , 讓他自己成為自己 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在他發表了這項工作 , 其他人可以找到他離開的地方 , 甚至設計更簡單的過程和改進 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個例子 , 我想提一下她的專案計畫的目標 , 就是強調材料的表現特質 , 同時把焦點放在建造者的創意和技能上 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子設備非常強大 , 他們教導我們事物是如何運作的 , 但在設計中 , 規則是以我們學習的方式來影響 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面 , 漢娜的做法是建立一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物體 , 藉由教導我們材料本身 , 來解放我們特定的限制 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜的許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	我們現在看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有銅膠貼在mp3和磁鐵上 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工學院的馬塞羅•柯爾研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的紙喇叭 , 從簡單的銅膠帶到導電布料 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他製造家漢娜發表了她的食譜 , 讓任何人都可以複製並複製它們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子設備是材料科學中最有前景的一分之一 , 讓我們能創造出更便宜且有彈性的電子產品 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	漢娜的工藝作品 , 以及她分享她的發現 , 打開門給一系列新的可能性 , 這兩者都是美感和創新 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	製造家有趣的事是 , 我們從熱情和好奇心中創造出來 , 我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們常常從不尋常的角度來處理問題 , 在這個過程中 , 我們會發現其他的 , 或甚至更好的方法來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以越多人實驗材料 , 研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 製造他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出真正適合我們所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得有點像是tednelson在1970年代初 , 他寫道: 「 你現在必須要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	當時 , 電腦是這些大型的主體 , 只有科學家在乎 , 沒有人夢想要在家裡有一個 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	我站在這裡有點奇怪 , 說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 取得新興科技的知識 , 最好的方式就是確保我們能在我們的未來發聲 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入玻璃泡 , 鎖住門 , 按住加速器 , 依賴我們的眼睛 , 來引導我們 , 即使我們只能看到前面的幾輛車子後面的車子 。 但如果車子可以和彼此分享他們的位置和速度 , 並使用預測模型 , 來計算路上每個人的安全路線 ?
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛•海利:如果車子能說話 , 意外可能會是可避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	讓我們面對現實:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的一件事 , 但事實是宗教的象徵和好的運氣魅力 , 出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背後的事實是我們知道這是真的 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國十六到十九歲人死亡的主要原因 , 這些事故中有百分之七十五的意外與毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒人可以肯定地說 , 但我記得我第一個意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我在高速公路上是個年輕的司機 , 在我面前的車上 , 我看到了煞車燈 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 這傢伙慢了下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙不會慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這個人在高速公路上停下來 , 停下來 , 停在高速公路 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只剩65到零 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我踩煞車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我覺得abck開始了 , 車子仍然不會停止 , 我知道它不會停止 , 空氣袋部署 , 車子很幸運 , 沒有人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全不知道車子停止了 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以轉變開車的經驗 , 讓車子彼此交談 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是想讓你們想想開車的經歷 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	上你的車 , 關上門 , 你在玻璃泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感知你身邊的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你被任務處理 , 任務是將它導向一部分看不到的道路 , 在另一塊金屬巨人之間 , 以超人的速度 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只要指引你是你的雙眼 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這就是你所擁有的 , 不是為了這個任務而設計的眼睛 , 但人們會要求你做像這樣的事 , 你想要做一場車道改變 , 問你第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從馬路上拿走 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	別再看你要去哪裡 , 轉身 , 看看你的盲點 , 然後開車走下去 , 不看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是安全的驅動方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做呢 ? 因為我們必須做選擇 , 我們必須做選擇 , 看看這裡還是我看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做一個很棒的工作 , 選擇我們在路上做的事 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們忽略了某樣東西 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾 , 我們會覺得出錯或太遲了 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	無數的意外 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它來了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信 。 我相信 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看太多了 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在的科技已經存在 , 可以協助我們改善它 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 車子彼此交換資料 , 我們不僅能看到前面的三輛車 , 還有三輛車 , 到右邊 , 同時 , 鳥瞰視角 , 我們還能看到這些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能夠看到前面的車速 , 看看那傢伙的前面有多快或停止 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個人去零 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	有了計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為這是不可能的 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	事實上 , 不 , 車子是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是三維的物體 , 有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們走在路上 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會依照原本出版的路線旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	很難做出合理的預測 , 很難在不久的將來 , 預測汽車會在哪裡 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使 , 當你在車裡的時候 , 有些摩托車人過來了 ! 每小時85英哩 , 我知道你有過這個經驗 , 那個人沒有 「 出去 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那個人在路上大概在過去半個小時了 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對嗎 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10、20、30英哩後 , 有人看過那個人 , 只要一輛車看到那個人 , 把他放在地圖上 , 他的位置、速度 , 估計他會每小時跑85英哩 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你們會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為其他的車會在他的耳朵大聲說: 「 順便說一句 , 馬達克斯 , 看一下 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以對汽車的行為做出合理的預測 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 他們是牛頓的物品 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說是很棒的 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何達成目標 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的東西開始 , 就像分享車子間的位置 , 分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我在車子裡有gps和攝影機 , 我有一個很精確的概念 , 知道我在哪裡、我要走多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我身邊的車在哪裡 , 有點像是 , 還有它們的方向 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車子也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以有一個精確的概念 , 說明他們在哪裡 , 有點模糊 , 知道其他車子在哪裡 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果有兩輛車共享那數據 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 說明了當模擬模擬結果時 , 即便在輕流量中 , 當車子共用gps資料時 , 我們將這項研究從電腦模擬中移到機器人上 , 進行實際的感測器 , 這些感測器現在就在這些機器人身上:streoreoreo、gps、gps , 以及2d的雷射雷射雷射處理器 , 這些是系統中常見的 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也附著一個特定的短距通訊無線電 , 機器人彼此交流 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人彼此聚集時 , 它們會追蹤彼此的位置 , 且它們能避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在正在把更多的機器人加入混合中 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當你收到太多章節時 , 很難處理所有的封包 , 所以你必須優先考慮 , 那就是預測模式能協助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車都在追蹤預測軌跡 , 你就不會注意那些包 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你把這個看似有點偏離的傢伙的優先順序排序 。
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他會走上路 , 你知道怎麼做 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	你知道你需要警告哪位司機才能離開 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想要怎麼警告每個人 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子怎麼可能會說: 「 你需要走出路 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	這取決於兩件事:一、車的能力 , 第二 , 駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人擁有很棒的車子 , 但他們在他們的手機上 , 或者 , 做點什麼 , 他們可能就不會在緊急情況下做出最好的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始了一項分開的研究 , 做司機國家模式 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用一系列的三台攝影機 , 我們可以偵測到如果駕駛向前、向下看、看著手機 , 或喝一杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外事故 , 我們可以預測誰 , 哪輛車 , 最好的位置是要走出路去計算每個人最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術是現今存在的 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自願分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我想這是個令人不安的概念 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 跟其他的車子談 , 我們會走在一片八卦的大道上 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以用一種方式來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車 , 我並不知道你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看一下你的車牌號碼 , 我並不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信 , 我們的車子可以在我們的背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是一件好事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我想請各位花點時間想想 , 如果你真的不想要那些分心的青少年 , 知道你在煞車 , 你即將到達一個死路 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過自願地分享我們的資料 , 我們就能為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的汽車八卦一下你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路變得更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	金融創辦人彼得•戴曼迪斯談到他如何協助史蒂芬•霍金實現夢想 , 透過一起飛進大氣層 , 並在零g中體驗無重 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、短談、空間、科技、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	史蒂芬•霍金的彼得•戴曼迪斯在0g中 , 獨立了史蒂芬•霍金 。
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人都知道我對打開太空前線有多有熱情 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給全世界的重力專家--無重力的體驗 , 真是令人難以置信 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴各位這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我初次見到他是基因組學獎得主 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所持有的競爭 , 第二個xprize , 讓第一個團隊在十天內將人類基因組定序 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有所謂的 「 基因組一百個個個體 」 , 我們將它定序為其中的一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特事件 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是進入太空 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你到那裡 , 但我可以帶你進入無重力的狀態 , 帶你進入零 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	唯一能體驗地球零度的方法 , 就是用反彈式飛行 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你搭飛機 , 飛越頂部 , 重量是25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回來 , 你的體重是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你一而再而三地做 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8、10分鐘的無重力 , 美國太空總署長久以來訓練他們的太空人 。
we set out to do this .	我們打算這麼做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始運營 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣佈我們要飛史蒂芬霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一間政府機關 , 一間公司飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 別這樣做 , 你就要殺了那個傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	他想要去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有的許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們坐在甘迺迪太空中心 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們有一場記者會 , 我們宣佈我們目的要做一個零平行 , 給他25秒的零 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果一切順利 , 我們可能會做出三個拋物鏡 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	我們問他為什麼他要上去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他所說的 , 對我來說 , 非常感人 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命是不斷增加的風險 , 被災難摧毀......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為 , 如果沒有進入太空 , 人類就不會有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	所以我想鼓勵公眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們把他帶到甘迺迪太空中心 , 在太空總署的車內 , 帶到零號飛機的後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約二十個人捐款給十五萬美金給與我們一起飛行的兒童慈善機構 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個ted人 。
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了一個整間急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生和兩位護士登上飛機 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們監測他的血液、心跳速率、血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們有所有的一切 , 例如緊急狀況 ; 神知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落設施起飛 , 太空梭起飛、降落 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我的另一半是lichtenberg , 我小心地把他暫停成零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那裡 , 我們就讓他體驗到無重力是真正的 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在第一次的拋物線飛行之後 , 醫生說 , 一切都很棒 。 他微笑 , 我們說了 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線鏡 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們實際上漂浮在牛頓爵士的homage , 因為艾薩克•牛頓教授在劍橋舉辦了相同的椅子 , 艾薩克•牛頓 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四次、第五次和第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	第七次和第八次 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像65歲的輪椅人 。
he was so happy .	他很開心 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們生活在珍貴的珠寶上 , 在我們有生之年 , 我們正從這個星球移走 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們這個史詩般的冒險 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫療動畫大衛•布林斯基在3分鐘內展現出令人震驚的動畫 , 顯示細胞內的忙碌生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、醫療、科學、技術、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插圖師 , 我來自一個稍微不同的觀點 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我長大以來 , 我一直在看真與美的表情在科學中表達真與美 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然兩者都很美好 , 但它們都有很棒的東西 , 能為它們帶來很棒的真相和美 , 作為科學和數學的理想 , 幾乎就像是科學家想約會的理想雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是真相的表達 , 作為令人敬畏的事物 , 意味著它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是強而有力的理想 。 它們是不可誘人的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 , 有時是有用的 , 通常是事實後的一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	各位現在可以放一些照片 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美 , 通常對不在科學領域的人來說是不一樣的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用來描述美麗的東西 , 通常只能在你了解語言和語言的同步 , 研究真相和美的主題時 , 才被描述出來 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看宇宙常數 , 有一個人類理想 , 在那裡你會發現生命必須從描述宇宙的數字進化 , 這些都是很難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我被教導為醫學插畫家的訓練之後 , 我就試著做些什麼 , 我從父親身上學到了動畫 , 他是雕塑家 , 以及我的視覺導師 , 我想要找出方法 , 幫助人們了解生物科學的真與美 , 利用動畫 , 說故事 , 讓人們不見得有證據可以被引導 , 並且可以被教導 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今 , 學生通常被沉浸在一個環境中 , 她們學到的是有真和美的主題 , 但她們被教導的方式卻被拿來比較 , 被吸引到事實和美麗的地方 , 並不總是顯而易見 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	就像你煮雞湯的那一古老的食譜 , 直到味道消失了 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對我們的學生那樣做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我在哈佛大學的robertlue打來電話給我 , 在幾年前的分子和細胞生物系中 , 他問我 , 如果我的團隊和我願意真正改變哈佛大學的醫學和科學教育 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始了一項計畫 , 探索細胞 , 探索分子和細胞生物學的真與美 , 讓學生能了解更大的圖片 , 讓它們能吸收所有這些事實 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可能有一塊由微機組成的大型巴士、大型複雜的城市 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微機械的確是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 是世界各地的奈米技術人員 , 都是自動導向、強大、精確、精確的裝置 , 由氨基酸組成 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微機械能強化細胞如何移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們能驅動細胞複製的方式 。 它們能驅動我們的心 。
they power our minds .	它們會影響我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想做的是找出我們要如何把這個故事變成一個動畫 , 它會是哈佛的生態照顧中心 , 它是哈佛大學為它的分子和細胞生物學生所設立的網站 , 除了所有的文字 , 以外 , 所有的做法都被視覺化 , 這樣這些學生就可以內化出細胞的真相和美麗 , 並且能夠研究這個觀點 , 以此來 , 我就能發現它們的全新的生命 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 也就是說 , 你的巨噬細胞在微血管下流動 , 它們正在觸碰微血管壁的表面 , 它們從微血管壁上接收到的細胞 , 它們被賦予了這些資訊 , 外面有發炎 , 在那裡 , 它們看不見和感官 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的資訊會讓它們停止 , 讓它們內化 , 讓它們需要做出各種零件 , 讓它們能夠改變它們的形狀 , 試著擺脫這種微小的狀況 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達 , 我們必須和哈佛的科學家和資料庫模型合作 , 用原子精確的分子 , 找出它們是如何移動的 , 找出它們的行為 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想辦法以一種真誠的方式來做這件事 , 讓事情發生了 , 但不太真實 , 細胞裡的緊密群體會阻止病毒發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給你們看的是一個三分鐘的讀者的消化版本 , 是我們製作的這部影片的第一部分 。 這是一個正在進行的計畫 , 將要花四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們能看到細胞製造這些小步行的機器的路徑 , 它們被稱為kinesin , 將這些巨大的負荷帶到相對大小的螞蟻身上 。
run the movie , please .	請播放這部電影 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些能驅動細胞內部的機器是相當驚人的 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為這些機器都能彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	它們彼此傳遞訊息 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會導致細胞內發生不同的事 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造果蠅需要的部件 , 從細胞核中帶出的資訊 , 以讀取基因的分子 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每個人 , 如果沒有這些微機械的話 , 就有可能做到 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 克里斯的出席率很高 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex遞送人員 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做 「 kinesin 」 , 他把一堆全新的製造蛋白質帶到細胞所需的任何地方 , 不論是細胞膜 , 不論是用來製造或修復某樣東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人都有大約十萬個這種東西在周圍運行 , 在你100兆個細胞中 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你有多懶惰 , 你本質上什麼都不做 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以當你回家時 , 我希望你去思考這件事 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想我們所學到的細胞機制 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞懂了所有正在發生的事情 , 相信我 , 我們就知道一旦知道發生了什麼事的百分之百 , 我們就真的能夠控制我們對健康的影響 , 和我們未來的世代所做的事 , 以及我們將要活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用它來發現更多的真相 , 還有更多的美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但 , 這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 真的很驚人 , 足以察覺細胞所需的作用 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們一起工作 。 它們讓細胞做它需要做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起工作 , 幫助我們身體巨大的實體 , 他們永遠不會看到正常的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受剩下的表演 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布蘭頓計劃要住在她的車裡一年 , 看到她的國家 , 但當憂鬱落入 , 她的自由工作結束時 , 她的露營變成無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述她經歷到她成為美國無家可歸的無家可歸者 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、人生、個人成長、貧窮、社會改變、社會、說故事、說故事、說故事、說故事、說故事、說故事、社會、社會、社會、社會、說故事、
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪•布蘭頓:那一年我無家可歸的那一年 , 我無家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是一位作家 , 一位記者 , 我也是個瘋狂好奇的人 , 所以 , 在22年來 , 我作為記者 , 我學會了很多新的東西 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到的一件事就是變得隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為工作無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭掉了報紙編輯的工作 , 那是我父親同年二月去世的時候 , 我決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡對我來說很困難 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	在我這麼做時 , 我想要感受到和處理很多事情 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都在露營 。 我決定住在一輛車裡 , 要做這件事 , 就好像一趟漫長的露營旅程 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以 , 我把貓、腐爛的貓和露營的裝備裝在1975年的雪檔車上 , 開車到日落 , 完全沒有意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會等同於永久的結構 , 甚至是緊縮 , 和人的價值有關 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒有意識到 , 別人的負面感知會如何快速影響我們的現實 , 如果我們讓它實現的話 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒有意識到無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在車裡是很棒的 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在校園裡淋浴 。 我經常吃掉 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但之後 , 我父親的死亡造成的憤怒和沮喪 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 , 我得要有全職的工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	剛剛的溫泉會變成一個悲慘的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	在任何地方 , 都不可能停在任何地方 , 很明顯地我有隻貓和一隻狗 , 真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓跑過車窗 , 穿過車窗 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗狗去做產卵日照顧 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能用辦公室大樓的員工淋浴 , 卡車停止 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或我在公共房間洗衣 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間的車體溫很少會降到華氏80度以下 , 讓它難以入睡 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中腐爛 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰層在我的胸腔融化了好幾個小時 , 真的很痛苦 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我負擔不起公寓 , 或買不起公寓 , 讓我可以擁有公寓和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄 , 所以我待在車裡 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當暖氣使我無法走過50英尺 , 到我車外的公共廁所 , 我用桶和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天氣候聚集時 , 溫度降到冰凍之下 , 牠們留在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了一整套新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都停著不同的地點 , 這樣我才能避免被警察察察察察察察察察察察察察察察察察察覺 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但 , 我卻無法控制我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道發生了什麼時候或事情 , 但我從一個有才華的作家和記者變成一個無家可歸的女人 , 住在車裡 , 把我的呼吸帶走了 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我還沒改變 。 我的智商還沒下學 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華、我的完整性、我的價值觀 , 所有關於我的東西都一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但不知怎麼的 , 我改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我深深深地深入憂鬱 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我稱為無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 。 我三天沒有洗澡 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排隊中的任何人一樣沮喪和沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是不喝酒或喝酒 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當幾個無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸的 。 你為什麼會在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人沒有把我視為無家可歸的人 , 但我確實這麼做了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	然後教授聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所的反應讓我感到憂鬱 , 讓我自殺了 。 我記得當時在想: 「 如果我殺了我 , 沒人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久後 , 一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•羅斯特 , 他是全國知名的記者 , 他一直在談論我在國際電視 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫了一篇關於我父親的文章 , 在他死前的那一年 , 是在提姆的新書裡 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他正在進行這場演說電路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我了解到timrussert時 , 《見報》的前主持人談到我的寫作 , 同時我在walmart停車場 , 我開始笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑 , 因為這已經到了我是作家 , 還是我是無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	於是我走進書店 , 找到提姆的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 重新讀了我的文章 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是一位作家 。
i was a writer .	我是一位作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久 , 我搬回田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友一起住在貨車裡 , 和沙發上 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始寫作了 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	隔年夏天 , 我是一名工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得獎項 。 我住在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再被看不見了 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人全職工作 , 兼職工作 , 住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續把生活在車上或街頭的犯罪化和罪犯化 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家可歸的無家可歸 , 主要是看不見的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇見他們 , 讓他們參與 , 鼓勵他們 , 並提供他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服任何事情 , 如果它有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我來這裡並不是為無家可歸的海報女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來鼓勵你們把錢捐給下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我來這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 大家不是他們住的地方 , 不論他們在哪裡睡覺 , 或是他們在任何時間生活的狀況 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在一輛沃爾瑪市場停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望永遠都能找到方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的 「 保險套 」 , mechaiviravaida , 帶我們走過全國的大膽計劃 , 以提升生活水準 , 從1970年代開始 。 第一步 , 人口控制 。 這意味著很多法蘭克 , 很有趣 , 且非常有效的談論保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、科學、科學、
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	克塔伊維瓦里達:保險套如何讓泰國成為一個更好的地方 , 一個更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	40年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常非常非常貧窮 , 有許多人生活在貧窮之中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定採取行動 , 但我們並不是從福利計畫開始 , 或減少貧窮計畫 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從家庭平台開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的孕產婦健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以基本上 , 沒有人能接受他們的家庭規劃 , 如果他們的孩子沒有存活下來 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	第一步:去找孩子 , 去找媽媽 , 然後跟著家人規劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是兒童死亡 , 你還需要家庭規劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	讓我帶各位回來 , 為何我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭的孩童的成長率是3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要減少人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女人說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會用藥 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥 。 」 我們很少有醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們不把 「 不 」 視為答案 ; 我們不把 「 不 」 視為一個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去了護士和助產士 , 他們也是女性 , 做了一個很棒的工作 , 解釋如何使用藥丸 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那很棒 , 但它只覆蓋了百分之二十的國家 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為其他80%的人做了什麼 , 讓他們孤獨 , 說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定再做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去了普通人群 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	其實 , 在那黃色標誌下面 , 我希望他們沒看到這個 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	當時我們比可口可樂還要大很多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選的人是我們選的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很熟悉 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們很棒 , 他們自己練習家庭規劃 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各地提供藥丸和保險套 , 在每個村落 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們就在那裡 。 我們去找被視為是解決問題的人們 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論有哪些人 , 都會看到女人的船 , 賣東西是漂浮的市場賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 不論你在泰國找到哪裡 , 都會找到避孕品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為什麼不上宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教教會非常強壯 , 泰國人是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我在那裏是藍色的 , 不是黃色的黃色 , 拿著一碗聖水 , 讓僧侶在吃藥和保險套上灑灑水 , 讓家人的聖潔水 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片在全國各地被寄來 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	有些村莊的僧人自己也在做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女人說: 「 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	它是有福的 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的認知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們去找老師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每個人參與嘗試提供任何讓人類更美好的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去找老師 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過25萬人被教導家庭規劃 , 用新的字母a、出生、保險套、吸毒、吸血管切除 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	接著 , 我們有一隻蛇和梯子遊戲 , 讓你丟掉骰子 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你登陸熟悉的規劃 , 你就會往前走 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	比如: 「 媽媽每晚都會吃藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 媽媽 , 繼續前進 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買保險套 , 很好 , 叔叔 , 繼續前進 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝醉 , 不用保險套 , 回來 , 再開始 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣地 , 教育和娛樂 。
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在學校做這件事 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們有保險套的相關種族 , 我們有孩子的保險套冠軍 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久之後 , 保險套就被稱為女生最好的朋友 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人來說 , 鑽石不會把它做成這樣保險套就是女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年推出了第一個微型貸款計畫 , 組織計畫的婦女說: 「 我們只想借錢給婦女 , 練習家庭規劃 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕 , 照顧你的懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你不懷孕 , 你可以從我們身上借錢 。 」
and that was run by them .	那是他們所經營的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	經過35/36年之後 , 它還在進行中 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 , 它不是真正的銀行 , 但它是一項資金微貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來執行 , 由村民自己經營 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能很難看到一個泰國人 , 總是女人、女人、女人、女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	接著 , 我們認為我們會協助美國 , 因為美國一直在協助每個人 , 不論他們是否想要協助 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	這是七月四日 。

and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	飯店給了我們一間很適合的房間 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	既然是午餐時間 , 他們說: 「 好吧 , 我們會給你一些午餐 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 它一定是美國的可樂 。
you get two brands , coke and pepsi .	有兩個品牌、可口可樂和百事可樂 。
and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	然後食物不是漢堡或熱狗 。 」
and i thought a hotdog will be more symbolic .	我以為熱狗會比較象徵性 。
and here is this , then , young man called willy bohm who worked for the usaid .	這裡是一位年輕人 , 名叫威廉的年輕人 , 他為美國國際援助工作 。
obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很明顯地 , 他有他的吸塵器 , 因為他的熱狗有一半吃了 , 他很開心 。
it made a lot of news in america , and it angered some people also .	它在美國製造了很多新聞 , 同時也讓一些人憤怒 。
i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 。 過來 , 我會做很多事 。 」
in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	在這一切中 , 從7個孩子到1.5個孩子 , 人口成長率是3.3到0.5 。
you could call it the cocacola approach if you like it was exactly the same thing .	你可以稱它為可口可樂的方法 , 如果你喜歡它是完全一樣的 。
i'm not sure whether cocacola followed us , or we followed cocacola , but we're good friends .	我不確定可口可樂是否跟隨我們 , 或者我們跟著可口可樂 , 但我們是好朋友 。

then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著 , 愛滋病來到泰國 , 我們必須停止對抗愛滋病的好事 。
but unfortunately , the government was in denial , denial , denial .	但不幸的是 , 政府在否認、否認、否認 。
so our work wasn't affected .	所以我們的工作沒有受到影響 。
so i thought , " well , if you can't go to the government , go to the military . "	所以我想: 「 嗯 , 如果你不能去政府 , 去軍隊 。 」
so i went to the military and asked to borrow 300 radio stations .	所以我去軍方 , 請求借300個無線電站 。

every ministry , even judges , had to be involved in aids education everyone and we said the public , institutions , religious institutions , schools everyone was involved .	每個牧師 , 甚至法官 , 都得要參與愛滋病教育 , 每一個人 , 我們說 , 大眾、機構、宗教機構、所有人都參與 。
and here , every media person had to be trained for hiv .	在這裡 , 每一位媒體人員都必須接受愛滋病的訓練 。
and we gave every station half a minute extra for advertising to earn more money .	我們花了每半分鐘的額外的廣告 , 來賺更多的錢 。

and these are high school kids teaching high school kids .	這些是高中生教導高中生 。

and these girls who go around teaching about safe sex and hiv were known as mother theresa .	這些四周去教導安全性愛滋病的女孩被稱為 「 艾滋病病毒 」 。
and then we went down one more step .	然後我們再往下一步 。
these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些是小學三年級的孩子 , 四年級到村子裡的每個家庭 , 整個泰國的每個家庭 , 給予愛滋病的資訊 , 給每個家庭保險套 , 給這些孩子 。

and they loved him . you need a symbol of something .	他們很愛他 , 你需要一個象徵 。

and also , in traffic , the policemen give you condoms our " cops and rubbers " programs .	此外 , 在交通上 , 警察會給你保險套 , 我們的 「 警察 」 計畫 。

and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	接著 , 我們決定幫助人們脫離貧窮 , 現在愛滋病已經走出這個時代 , 不是單單靠政府 , 而是和商業界合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能和功勞 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	這些都是商業界提供的 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們變成赤腳企業家 , 小企業家 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫貧的唯一方法就是透過企業企業經營 。
so , that was done .	所以 , 這已經完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	這筆錢從公司到村落 , 透過樹木植入 。
it's not a free gift .	這不是免費的禮物 。
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種樹木 , 金錢會進入他們的微型貸款基金 , 我們稱之為村落發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進來 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在你借錢之前 , 你需要被訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信如果你想要協助窮人 , 住在貧窮中的人 , 能夠取得信用 , 就必須是人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	要取得功勞 , 就必須是人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠不會脫離貧窮 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	在貸款之前 , 你必須被訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	這是我們所謂的 「 赤腳mba 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 所以 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就會成功 。

they said , " they should stop making shoes and clothes .	他們說: 「 他們應該停止做鞋子和衣服 。
make these better , because we can afford them . "	把這些做得更好 , 因為我們負擔得起 。 」
and then we have silk , thai silk .	然後我們有絲 , 泰國絲綢 。

so anyone sitting in and watching tv , get in touch with me .	有人坐著看電視 , 跟我聯絡 。

see , starbucks you awake , we keep you awake and alive .	星巴克你醒著 , 我們讓你清醒 , 讓你活著 。

and then now , finally in education , we want to change the school as being underutilized into a place where it's a lifelong learning center for everyone .	現在 , 終於 , 在教育上 , 我們想要改變學校 , 把學校當作不完整的學校 , 讓每個人成為終身學習中心 。
we call this our schoolbased integrated rural development .	我們稱之為我們的學校基礎整合農村發展 。
