your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能感覺像個朋友 , 但一個真正的朋友會給你一個微笑 。 不久前 , 在ted2013 , 克萊納德•羅莫 , 一位智慧型手機驅動機器人 , 可以和你一起走路 , 投影片上 , 一杯咖啡 , 讓你能在桌子上做出可程表情的反應 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	克萊納多:一個迷你機器人 , 是由你的手機驅動的 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	舉手來說 , 在座有多少人家裡都有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	很多人都沒有 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好了 。 實際上 , 如果你不包含室巴 , 在座有多少人家裡有機器人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們在romotive嘗試解決的問題 , 我和其他20位羅斯莫特的老兄們都著迷於解決問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的想要建造一個任何人都可以使用的機器人 , 不論你是8或80歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是一個非常困難的問題 , 因為你必須建造一個小型的可攜式機器人 , 它不僅是可以負擔得起的 , 而且它必須是人們想要帶回家 , 帶著孩子去的地方 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不可能是詭異或不可怕的 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善且可愛的 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是一個用你已經知道且愛你的iphone的裝置 , 用來當作他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由控制iphone處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造一個可以用wi-fi和電腦視覺處理的機器人 , 讓150美元的價格降低 , 這大約是過去機器人所付出的百分之一 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他在生物模式中 。
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他實際上是在用這個裝置上的攝影機來追蹤我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我倒下 , 他會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很溫暖 , 所以他會盯著我看 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來到這裡 , 他就會跟著我走 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我來到這裡 , 他很聰明 。
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就會嚇到像其他生物一樣 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以 , 在很多方面 , romo就像一隻有自己想法的寵物 。
thanks , little guy .	謝謝 , 小傢伙 。
and if i want to explore the world uhoh , romo's tired if i want to explore the world with romo , i can actually connect him from any other ios device .	如果我想要探索這個世界--嗯 , romo已經累了--如果我想要用romo來探索這個世界 , 我可以把他從任何其他ios設備聯繫起來 。
so here's the ipad .	這是ipad 。
and romo will actually stream video to this device .	而romo會把影片串流到這個裝置上 。
so i can see everything that romo sees , and i get a robot'seyeview of the world .	我可以看見romo看到的所有東西 , 我得到一個機器人的世界觀 。
now this is a free app on the app store , so if any of you guys had this app on your phones , we could literally right now share control of the robot and play games together .	這是應用程式商的免費應用程式 , 所以 , 如果你們有人在手機上使用這個應用程式 , 我們現在就能夠共享機器人和玩遊戲的控制 。
so i'll show you really quickly , romo actually he's streaming video , so you can see me and the entire ted audience .	我會很快地給你們看romo , 他正在串流影片 , 所以你們可以看到我和ted的觀眾 。
if i get in front of romo here .	如果我來到romo前面 。
and if i want to control him , i can just drive .	如果我想要控制他 , 我就可以開車 。
so i can drive him around , and i can take pictures of you .	我可以帶他到處開車 , 拍下你們的照片 。
i've always wanted a picture of a 1 , 500person ted audience .	我一直都想要一張1500個ted觀眾的照片 。
so i'll snap a picture .	我會拍張照片 。
and in the same way that you scroll through content on an ipad , i can actually adjust the angle of the camera on the device .	就如同你在ipad上播放內容一樣 , 我可以調整儀器上的相機角 。
so there are all of you through romo's eyes .	所以你們全部都透過romo的眼睛 。
and finally , because romo is an extension of me , i can express myself through his emotions .	最後 , 因為romo是我的延伸 , 我可以透過他的情緒表達自己 。
so i can go in and i can say let's make romo excited .	所以我可以進去 , 我可以說 , 讓我們做romo興奮 。
but the most important thing about romo is that we wanted to create something that was literally completely intuitive .	但romo最重要的是 , 我們想要創造完全直覺的東西 。
you do not have to teach someone how to drive romo .	你不需要教別人如何開romo 。
in fact , who would like to drive a robot ?	事實上 , 誰想開一個機器人 ?
thank you , scott .	謝謝你 , 史考特 。
and even cooler , you actually don't have to be in the same geographic location as the robot to control him .	更酷的是 , 你其實不需要和機器人在相同的地理位置裡來控制他 。
so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他實際上在任何兩個智能設備之間串流了雙向音頻和影片 。
so you can log in through the browser , and it's kind of like skype on wheels .	你可以通過瀏覽器登入 , 有點像是在輪子上的skype 。
so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	我們先來談談遠端論點 , 這是個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	舉例來說 , 你可以想像一個八歲的女孩 , 她有iphone , 她的媽媽買了一個機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 寄電子郵件給祖母 , 住在國家的另一邊 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	祖母可以登入那台機器人 , 和她的孫女玩隱匿號 , 每晚十五分鐘 , 否則 , 她可能只有一年一次或兩次 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	這些是現在romo可以做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想談談我們未來正在努力的東西 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這其實是我們其中一個工程師 , 一個週末建造的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在google開放式的架構上 , 叫做 「 街區 」 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這讓你可以拖著這些語義代碼的積木 , 創造任何你想要的機器人行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何編寫程式 , 為romo創造一個行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你可以在瀏覽器中模擬這種行為 , 左邊是romo在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以下載它到你的機器人上 , 在現實生活中執行程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你對某樣東西感到驕傲 , 你可以和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所有這些無線網路的機器人 , 都能互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以專注於建造人人人都可以訓練的機器人 , 是因為我們認為在個人機器人中最有說服力的用途是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	他們從人轉變為人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為 , 如果你要在你家裡裝一個機器人 , 那機器人應該要是你自己的想像力 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道 , 這不是10年或100億美元 , 也不是一個大型的人類機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它將會取決於小型、敏捷的機器人 , 像是romo , 以及像你們這樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以 , 我們等不及把所有機器人都拿出來 , 我們等不及要看你打造什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和激進主義者會討論女性、創造力、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 還有這場演說的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、女人、世界文化、文化、文化、女性、女性、女性、世界文化、文化、女性、女性、女性、女性、世界文化、文化、
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•艾倫德說過關於熱情的故事 ,
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你們 。 這真的很可怕 , 在這裡 , 最聰明的 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡是要告訴你們幾個關於熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有一個猶太人說我愛 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼比真理更真實 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是一個說故事的人 。 我想傳達一些比我們共同的人性更為真實的東西 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都讓我很感興趣 , 直到我最後寫了它們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們身邊的謎團 , 所以我寫下關於巧合、開幕、情緒、夢想、大自然的力量、魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年 , 我發表了幾本書 , 但直到2006年二月 , 我就住在義大利的奧運會 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這使我成為名人 。 現在人們認出我在馬西的名人 , 而我的孫子認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我告訴你我四分鐘的名聲 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	奧林匹克典禮的組織者之一 , 打電話給我 , 說我被選為國旗調查員之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答 , 這絕對是錯誤的身份 , 因為你能從運動員身上得到的我是這麼遠的 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定我可以走在體育場上 , 不用走路 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是笑事 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧林匹克旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性代表五大洲 , 三位奧林匹克金牌贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說 , 一個制服 , 並且要求我的測量 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我有自己的遠景在流感動脈中 , 看起來就像是michelin男人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月中期 , 我在土耳其 , 那裡充滿熱情的群眾在街上任何80名奧運隊都在歡呼 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了所有比賽的一切 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得贏 , 但還有運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一股雪 , 一英吋的冰 , 風的力量 , 就能判定種族或遊戲的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 比訓練或幸運更重要的是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才會得到黃金獎 。
it is all about passion .	一切都是關於熱情 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	土耳其的街道被紅色海報覆蓋 , 宣佈奧運的口號 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情在這裡 , 不是一直是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心就是驅動我們的東西 , 並決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我書中的角色所需要的東西:熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要馬爾里克、異議人士、冒險家、外人和叛軍 , 他們會問問題、彎曲規則、冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	很有常識的人不會做出有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	它們只會讓前額外的配偶成為好的配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間 , 我碰到其他的旗幟:三位運動員 , 女演員蘇珊蘇珊•沙隆和蘇菲亞•羅倫 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	此外 , 有兩個有熱情的女人:威加里•馬塔伊 , 肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 她種植了三千萬棵樹 。 藉由這麼做 , 她改變了土壤、天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然 , 許多村莊的經濟條件 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	並且 , 一個柬埔寨激進分子 , 他熱衷對抗兒童賣淫 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她14歲時 , 她的祖父賣給妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩強暴的男人 , 相信有年輕的處女可以治癒愛滋病 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	每天有五、十五個客戶被迫接受 , 如果他們反抗 , 他們就會受到折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色的房間 , 我收到了制服 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的衣服 , 但距離我預期的michelin男人穿的衣服不太好 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來就像是冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	除了蘇菲雅羅倫 , 全體美和熱情的象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅七十多歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感 , 很脆弱 , 很高 , 有很深的色彩 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	那麼 , 你要如何有深色的坦承 ? 沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	在電視訪談中 , 問: 「 她怎麼會看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 。 我的背總是直直直直 , 我沒有發出老人的聲音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 這裡有一些免費的建議來自地球上最美麗的女性之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	不 , 不用咳嗽 , 不用咳嗽 , 不用跟自己說話 , 不用說話 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她沒有那麼說 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在午夜的時候 , 我們被召喚到體育場的翅膀 , 聲響者宣佈奧運旗 , 順便一提 , 音樂起始於這裡的愛滋病遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅倫就在我面前 , 她比我高 , 不是在計算毛茸毛髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走路 , 像非洲大草原上的長頸鹿 , 她肩上握著旗子 。 我穿著腳踏在我的伸展手上 , 把旗子放在我的伸展手中 , 所以我的頭其實是在該死的旗子下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有攝影機都是在蘇菲亞 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大部分的媒體照片中 , 我也出現了 , 雖然通常是在蘇菲亞的腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大部分男人都喜歡的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最好的四分鐘就是那些在奧林匹克體育館裡的人 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我先生很冒犯我說這句話雖然我向他解釋說我們在私人領域所做的事通常只花不到四分鐘所以他不該自己去做
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有這四分鐘的記者 , 因為我不想忘記他們 , 老年時摧毀我的大腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想永遠帶著我的心 , 永遠帶著奧林匹克熱情的關鍵字 。
so here's a tale of passion .	這裡有個關於熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	當時是1998年 , 這個地方是剛果的土衛六難民營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順便一提 , 世界上80%的難民和流離失所是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱之為剛果死亡營 , 因為那些沒有殺死的人會死於疾病或飢餓 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕女子 , 蘿絲•地圖 , 還有她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕和寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵強迫她看著她的丈夫被虐待並殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她成功讓七個孩子活著 , 幾個月後 , 她生出了雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子剪下麻痺的皮膚 , 用她自己的頭髮綁起來 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她把營地指揮官的雙胞胎命令命令命令命名 , 用黑色茶餵給他們 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持它們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵在她的牢房中打擊強暴她最老的女兒時 , 她會抓住她並拒絕放手 , 即使他們把槍拿到她的頭上 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家人存活了16個月 , 接著 , 幸運的是 , 一個年輕的美國人 , 薩夏•查諾夫的熱心 , 他成功把她放進美國救援飛機 , 羅斯地圖 , 她的九個孩子在亞利桑那州鳳凰城 , 他們現在住在哪裡 , 成長茁壯 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	在斯瓦希里 , 地圖意味著偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書裡的主角是強壯且有熱情的女性 , 像是羅斯•地圖 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不建議他們 , 不需要這樣做 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處都看到它們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都和女性合作過 。
i know them well .	我很了解他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在一個古老的時代 , 在世界上末期 , 一個天主教和保守家庭 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪在我五歲時 , 我是個憤怒的女權主義者 , 雖然這個詞還沒到智利 , 所以沒人知道我有什麼問題 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 我的自由價格很高 , 且要質疑父權主義 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能支付這筆錢 , 因為每次我收到的金額 , 我都可以遞送二次 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我女兒保羅亞二十多歲時 , 她對我說 , 女權主義已經到了 , 我應該繼續前進 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有不可思議的鬥爭 。 女權主義約會了嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於像我女兒 , 今天在座的所有人 , 特別有特權的女性 , 但對世界上大部分的姊妹來說 , 她們仍然被迫要結婚 , 賣淫 , 強迫勞動 , 她們有不想要的孩子 , 或無法餵飽 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法控制自己的身體或生活 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、毆打 , 有時會被打死 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	現今大部分的西方年輕婦女被稱為女性主義者是種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女性主義從來沒有很性感 , 但讓我向各位保證 , 它從來沒有阻止我調情 , 我也遭受缺乏男性的苦難 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女權主義沒有死去 , 沒有任何意義 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個詞 , 改變它 , 對女神來說 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱之為蚜蟲 , 金星 , 或金星 , 或任何你想要的東西 ; 名字就無所謂 , 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們就支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這裡還有另一個關於熱情的故事 , 這是一個悲傷的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	那個地方是孟加拉村的小婦女診所 。
the year is 2005 .	在2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙醫衛生 , 她在三週假期去診所當志工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備清潔牙齒 , 但當她到那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是一個滿滿蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	外面有一行婦女等了好幾個小時被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人處於極端疼痛 , 因為她有數個腐爛的瘧疾 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮知道唯一的辦法就是拿出不好的牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有執照 ; 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她的風險很大 , 她很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的樂器 , 但幸運的是 , 她帶來了一些諾提琴 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有勇敢且熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她謀殺了一個禱告 , 然後她帶著手術前進 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 鬆了病人親吻她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 衛生學家抽出更多的牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	隔天早上 , 當她再次到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一位病人正在等著她丈夫 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女人的臉看起來像水母 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	腫脹到無法看見眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫、憤怒、威脅要殺美國 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她所做的事感到害怕 , 但翻譯說明病人的狀況和手術無關 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她丈夫打敗她 , 因為她沒有家準備晚餐給他 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬的女性像這樣生活 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是最貧窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	儘管世界上三分之二的婦女在勞工上 , 她們擁有不到百分之一的全世界資產 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水低於同一份工作 , 如果他們有薪水 , 而且他們仍然很脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 他們經常受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實是 , 給予女性教育、工作、控制她們自己的收入、繼承和財產的能力 , 讓社會受益 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦權 , 她的孩子和她的家人就會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村落的人民 , 最終 , 整個國家也一樣 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai去肯亞的一個村莊 。
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和婦女談話 , 解釋說土地是荒蕪的 , 因為他們砍了樹 , 賣掉樹 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女種植新的樹和水 , 掉下去 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	大約五、六年後 , 他們有一片森林 , 土壤被充足 , 村落被拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮、最後退的社會總是會讓女性下降 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	但這個顯而易見的事實卻被政府和慈善機構忽略了 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	給予女性專案的每一塊錢 , 每一塊錢就有20塊錢給男性專案 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性佔人類的51% 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦權讓他們改變一切 , 不僅僅是科技、設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性一起工作 , 連結、有知識 , 和受教育 , 能把和平及繁榮帶到這個被偽造的星球上 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在任何今天的戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡都是平民 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 她們是繼承傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人在世界裡跑 , 看看我們面臨的混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是一個基本的問題 , 大部分人都在問 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序是合理的嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個保存生命的世界 , 而生命的品質是為每個人豐富的 , 不只是為了特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月我看到費南多•波特諾在加州大學柏克萊圖書館的畫作 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	在美國 , 沒有博物館或畫廊除了紐約的畫廊 , 讓波特歐的作品展現出這幅畫 , 因為主題是阿布格拉伯監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是巨大的折磨和濫用權力的畫作 , 用的是大型的波特羅風格 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我無法從我的腦中或我的心中取得這些影像 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的就是權力 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用權力的力量 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個物種中 , 雄性領袖定義現實 , 並強迫其餘的群體接受現實並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則隨時都會改變 , 但他們總是受惠 , 在這個例子中 , 技巧效應並不適用於經濟學 ,
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待從梯子的頂部到底部 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女性和孩子 , 特別是窮人 , 都在最底層 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即便是最有勢的男人也能虐待女人或小孩 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我得到了一些力量 , 透過性別、收入、種族、和階級 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 該是時候了 , 要徹底改變我們的文明 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但對於真正的改變 , 我們需要女性的能量來管理世界 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要幾個關鍵的女性在權力的位置 , 我們需要培養男性的女性能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我說的當然是年輕人 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老人無助 , 我們必須等待他們死去 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很想有蘇菲亞羅倫的長腿和傳奇的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 根據一個選擇 , 我寧願有勇敢的心 , 像是威加利馬塔伊、索瑪利媽、珍妮、羅斯地圖 。
i want to make this world good .	我想要讓這個世界變得更好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是讓它變得更好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不呢 ? 這是可能的 。 看看這個房間裡所有的知識 , 能源 , 天賦和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	咱們先擺脫我們的粉絲 , 捲起袖子 , 去工作 , 熱情地創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦的大小 , 三千萬份餐都是用的 。 但是 , 所有的食物是從哪裡來的 ? 建築師卡林•史特爾討論每天餵食城市的奇蹟 , 顯示了古老的食物路線如何塑造了現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題、全球議題、
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡羅琳•史黛爾:食物如何塑造我們的城市 , 如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵飽一個城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代的一個大問題 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻很少被問過 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們視為理所當然 , 如果我們去一家商店或餐廳 , 或在大約一個小時內 , 就會有食物等著我們 , 神奇地從某處來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為 , 倫敦大小的城市每天都要生產出足夠的食物、運送、購買、購買、購買、吃、丟棄的東西 , 每天都要發生在地球上的每個城市 , 都是很了不起的 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在像這樣的地方 , 彷彿它們是世界上最自然的東西 , 因為我們是動物 , 我們需要吃 , 事實上我們和古老祖先一樣依賴自然界 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們進入城市 , 更多的自然世界被轉變為非凡的地景 , 像我身後的那個 , 它是巴西馬托格羅索的黃豆田 , 目的是要餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非凡的地景 , 但我們很少見到它們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多的景觀 , 不僅僅是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們越往城市進步 , 我們就越多吃肉 , 所以全球每年有三分之一的穀物被餵給動物 , 而不是人類 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由於它需要三倍的穀物 , 實際上是十倍的穀物來餵飽人類 , 如果它是先通過動物的話 , 那不是非常有效率的餵養我們的方法 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	問題也在上升 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	估計到2050年 , 我們的人數將是城市的兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	據估計 , 將有兩倍的肉類和乳製品 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以肉類和都市主義在手上起手 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將會帶來巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	六十億飢餓的肉食品 , 到2050年 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 實際上 , 如果我們繼續走下去 , 這個問題就不太可能解決 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有九千萬公頃的雨林被砍伐 , 創造新的耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	儘管同時我們也失去了相當大量的碳水化合物來鹽和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也很渴望石化燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	大約需要10卡路里才能生產我們西方消耗的食物 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管我們有很大的成本來生產的食物 , 但我們卻不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國生產的一半的食物 , 目前被丟棄了 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	為了結束這一切 , 在這漫長的過程中 , 我們甚至沒有適當的管理來餵飽這個星球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	十億人肥胖 , 同時又有十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	這一點都不合理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為現在全球80%的食物交易只由五間跨國企業所控制 , 這張照片很可怕 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	當我們進入城市時 , 世界也擁抱西方飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 這是一個不穩定的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 要回答這個問題稍微簡單一點 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 這個過程是在古老的東邊 , 稱為 「 肥沃 」 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是最近的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	同時也是肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 有兩種非凡的發明 , 農業和城市化 , 發生在同一個地方 , 同時也發生了 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這並不意外 , 因為農業和城市是相互連結的 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為我們古老祖先第一次發現了一種食物來源 , 足以支撐永久的定居地 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些定居處的樣子 , 我們會看到它們是緊密的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被生產力的農田包圍 , 被大型的寺廟複雜 , 像這個 , 實際上 , 精神化 , 中央食物分配中心所支配 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為那是神殿安排收穫 , 聚集在穀物裡 , 將之送給神 , 然後給予神不吃人的穀物 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你喜歡 , 這些城市的精神和實體生活都是由穀物所支配的 , 以及維持它們的收穫 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部都那麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	名聲著名的是 , 羅馬在第一世紀有大約一百萬個公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市是怎麼回饋的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是我所謂的 「 古老食物哩程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬可以到海裡 , 讓它可以從很遠的地方進口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	在古代世界裡 , 唯一能做到這一點的方法 , 因為在路上運輸食物是非常困難的 , 差不多是如此 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物顯然很快就消失了
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬有效率地鼓勵戰爭 , 像是凱薩和埃及 , 只為了取得他們的穀物保留地 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張是相當長的 , 畫出軍事化的購物圈 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡事實 , 我只需要提一下:羅馬以前是從倫敦進口牡蠣 , 在某個階段我覺得這很特別 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	羅馬透過它的胃口 , 塑造了它的內陸 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 在工業界也發生了另一件事 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀倫敦的地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 來自袋狼 , 沿著地圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場就在城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	路從它們帶到便宜 , 也就是主要市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看那些街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你可以知道300年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 魚也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也是從河流進來的 。 同樣的東西 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 比林斯門是著名的倫敦的魚市場直到1980年代中期才開始運作
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	仔細想想 , 這真的是很了不起的 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他人都在跟手機遊蕩 , 看起來像磚塊 , 有點像是港口的魚 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是城市中的食物:一旦它根入城市的另一樣東西 , 它們很少移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類是完全不同的 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物會走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦大部分的肉都來自西北部 , 來自蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	到達西北部的城市 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦著名的肉市場 ,
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家畜從東加利亞到東北部
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像是氣象婦在做這件事 。 總之 , 鳥類會用腳來保護牠們 , 腳上有小的畫布鞋 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	然後當他們進入廉價的東邊時 , 就會被賣掉 , 這就是為什麼被稱為 「 家禽 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看在工業時代之前的任何城市地圖 , 你可以追蹤食物進來 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何被食物的形狀 , 兩者都透過閱讀街道的名字 , 讓你知道很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在過去的生命中 , 是你在星期五去買你的魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也必須想像它滿是食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一買食物的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年史密菲爾德的影像 , 你可以看到 , 住在像這樣的城市中 , 很難知道你的食物從哪裡來 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 假如你有星期日午餐 , 你的機會就在你的窗外 , 大概三天前就在你的窗外 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是一個有機城市 , 一個有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西部的照片 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 最早的火車乘客是豬和綿羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場了 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被趕出視覺和心智 , 在鄉下某處被屠殺 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們被鐵路接近城市 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 它讓城市能夠第一次成長 , 真正的大小和形狀 , 在任何地方 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去的城市被地理限制 ; 他們以前必須透過非常困難的身體來取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們從地理上被有效地解放 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如同你從倫敦的地圖上所看到的 , 在火車出現的九十年後 , 它從一個很容易餵飽的小區域 , 從動物腳上來到一個很大的海綿 , 要不管是腳上、動物或人類都很難餵飽任何人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 這只是開端 。 火車來了之後 , 真的 , 這個過程結束了 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	這是城市的最後解放 , 完全和大自然之間的關係 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這是那種沒有氣味的城市 , 沒有混亂 , 絕對沒有人 , 因為沒有人會夢想走在這樣的地景中 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們把食物送到車子裡 , 開車到外面的某個地方 , 帶回了一週的購物 , 想知道到底該怎麼做 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	而這正是我們與食物和城市的關係 , 完全改變的時刻 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡 , 我們有食物 , 以前是市中心 , 在周圍的社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	它以前是社交活動 , 買賣和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前煮飯 ; 現在我們加入水或一點蛋 , 只要你做蛋糕或其他東西 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物 , 看看是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只是在包裝上讀到標籤 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們不珍惜食物 , 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再相信它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是去珍視它 , 我們把它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品系統最諷刺的一點是他們承諾要讓生活更加困難 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由讓城市可以在任何地方建造 , 任何地方 , 它們其實遠離了我們最重要的關係 , 那就是我們和大自然 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	此外 , 它們也讓我們依賴它們能傳遞的系統 , 如我們所見 , 它們是不穩定的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那麼 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	500年前 , 湯瑪斯•摩爾曾自問 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他書《烏托邦》的頭條 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	那是一系列半獨立的城市 , 如果聽起來很熟悉的話 , 一天走向彼此 , 每個人基本上都是耕種 , 在他們的後花園裡種植蔬菜 , 一起吃飯等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我認為 , 你可以說食物是烏托邦的基本原則 , 即使從來沒有那樣規劃它 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	還有另一個非常有名的烏托邦人遠景 , 埃布內斯霍華 , 《花園城市》 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的點子:一系列半獨立的城市 , 一小塊大都市的東西 , 帶著土地到處 , 加入鐵路 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	同樣的 , 食物可以被認為是他視覺的訂購原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造出來了 , 但和那個霍華的願景沒有關係 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	而這些烏托邦的點子問題就是他們是烏托邦 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是湯瑪斯•摩爾刻意使用的詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為它的產量是希臘的兩倍 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可能意味著一個好的地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個理想的 , 一個有想像力的東西 。 我們不能擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 身為一個概念性的工具 , 來思考人類居住的深層問題 , 讓它不太能被使用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 來自古希臘語 「 sitos 」 、 「 sitos 」 、 「 topa 」 、 「 topia 」 等地方 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西托邦 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們可以把食物當作一種非常強大的工具 , 一種概念性工具 , 設計工具 , 以不同的方式塑造世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這樣做 , 西托邦看起來會是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我想這看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 。 這只是狗的臉 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	不管怎樣 , 這是食物在生命的中心 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌、享受、人們花時間為它慶祝 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這就是我們社會中糧食應有的地方 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但除非你有這樣的人 , 不可能有這樣的場景 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順便說一下 , 這些也可以是男人 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	人們會想到食物 , 會想到前面的計劃 , 可以盯著一堆原生蔬菜 , 並且認清它們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 。 我們是網路的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這種人 , 我們就不可能有這樣的地點 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	這裡 , 我故意選擇這個 , 因為這是一個人買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網路、市場 , 在那裡 , 食物會在當地生長 。
it's common . it's fresh .	它很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	這是城市社會生活的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為沒有這些 , 你就不能有這樣的地點 , 當地種植的食物 , 同時也是地景的一部分 , 而不只是一個零和的商品 , 在一些看不見的地獄裡 。
cows with a view .	牛的觀點是 。
steaming piles of humus .	大堆的 「 嗡 」 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上就是把整件事結合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多拜訪的一個社區專案 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	它是一個溫室 , 孩子們會告訴所有關於食物的知識 , 並自己種植食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有個叫kevin的植物 , 或者它屬於一個叫kevin的孩子 , 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	總之 , 這些企圖與大自然重新連結的計畫是非常重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 對我來說 , 西托邦是種看法 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 西托邦已經存在於一個小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅是把它們加入 , 用食物當作一種看法 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們就不會把城市看成大型、大都市 , 像這樣無生產力的怪物 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看得更像這樣 , 作為生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 它們無可避免地被連結在一起 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	但當然 , 這也不是很棒的圖像 , 因為我們不需要再創造像這樣的食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要更深入思考永續文化 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張圖片會讓我覺得我們需要做的事 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	這是一種重新概念化的食物如何塑造我們的生活 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最好的圖像是從650年前開始 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	是阿布羅吉歐•羅倫澤蒂的 「 好政府的寓言 」 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	重點是城市和鄉村之間的關係 。
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這個訊息非常明確 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧這個國家 , 這個國家就會照顧這個城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我希望我們現在能問ambrogiolorenzetti , 如果他今天畫出這張照片 , 會是什麼樣子 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天好政府的寓言會是什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	我們得要問這個問題 , 我們得要開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們就是吃什麼的 。
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要了解到 , 世界也是我們所吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採取這個想法 , 我們可以用食物作為強大的工具 , 來改善世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	二十一世紀 , 卡倫•阿姆斯壯發起了幾週後 , 關注宗教的角色:它的教條會分裂我們嗎 ? 或它會為我們共通點嗎 ? 她會檢視這些催化劑 , 驅使世界的信仰重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝 , ted大獎 , 全球議題 , 政治 , 宗教 , tedglobal2009 , 暴力 , 暴力 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們重新審視黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我都覺得很挫折 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我敏銳地意識到同情心在世界各大宗教裡的核心 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個人都演化出了他們自己的黃金法則 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 它出現在正面的版本中 , 「 一直對待所有人 , 只要你自己被治療就好 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是 , 負面的版本 「 不要對別人做你不喜歡的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心 , 發現讓你感到痛苦 , 然後拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 讓你在任何人身上都承受痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調同情的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來很棒 , 也因為它很有用 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施黃金法則時 , 如同混亂所說: 「 整天 , 」 不單只是一個問題 , 問題是你每天都在做 , 回到貪婪和自負的生活 , 卻每天都在做 , 你從世界的中心 , 放下另一個 , 然後你超越自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它帶你到一個名為 「 神 」 的存在 , nirvana , rama , rao , tao 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們所知的自我存在 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你以前從來不知道 , 這對宗教生活是很重要的 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有幾個很棒的例外 , 通常當宗教人聚在一起時 , 宗教領袖會聚集在一起 , 他們會爭論關於廢除教條 , 或是說出仇恨或對同性戀的意見 , 或類似的事情 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們並不真的想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到當我和宗教團體說話時 , 有點像是在表情上交叉 , 因為人們常常想做對 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	那當然會打敗運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我這麼感激ted ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們很溫柔地從我的書籍研究帶我進入二十一世紀 , 讓我能和比我想像中更廣泛的觀眾交談 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到很迫切 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們無法在全球實施黃金法則 , 這樣我們就治療所有人 , 無論何時何地 , 不論他們是誰 , 彷彿他們和我們一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界來交給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 是我們這個時代最偉大的任務 , 就是建立一個全球社會 , 如我所說 , 在那裡 , 人們可以和平共處 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該要做出重大貢獻的宗教 , 卻被視為是問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 不只是宗教人士相信黃金法則 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的來源 , 這種有想像力的同理心的行為 , 把你自己放在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以 , 我們有一個選擇 , 對我來說 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以說服或強調信仰的教條和寬容的面向 , 或者我們可以回到拉比山丘 , 老派的耶穌當代人 , 當他站在一條猶太教義上時 , 他說: 「 這對你的鄰居是有害的 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	那是托拉和其他所有的東西 , 只有評論 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	拉比人和早期教會的父親說過 , 任何對教條的詮釋都是非法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	我們需要恢復這種精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不僅會發生 , 因為愛情的精神會讓我們消失 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須實現這一點 , 而且我們能用ted所推出的現代溝通方式來進行 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對所有伴侶的反應感到極大的鼓舞了 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一組人會用查爾特來治癒分裂 , 最近才出現在新加坡社會 , 國會的一些成員想要在政治上執行 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將會有一場藝術展 , 領導著藝術家會帶領人們、年輕人 , 並展現出慈悲 , 也是所有藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在歐洲 , 穆斯林社區抱持著事件和討論 , 討論同情心在伊斯蘭和所有信仰中的核心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停在那裡 , 它不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教學 , 我們錯了 , 只專注在信仰不信教的教條上 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教學一定會引起行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我打算在我死去的那天工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我想繼續讓我們的夥伴們做兩件事 , 來教育並激發同情心思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育因為我們從同情心中退出 。
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們通常認為這只是對某人感到抱歉的意思 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但當然 , 如果你只是想一想 , 你不會了解同情心 。
you also have to do it .	你也必須這麼做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們能參與其中 , 因為媒體是很重要的 , 要協助消除一些我們對他人的刻板印象 , 讓我們彼此分開 。
the same applies to educators .	教育者也一樣 。
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望青少年能感受到動態、動態和挑戰同情生活方式 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時 , 它也需要急性智能 , 而不只是一種古怪的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想打電話給學者 , 來探索他們自己的同情心 , 在別人的傳統中 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	最重要的是 , 鼓勵對不友善的演講的敏感度 , 如此一來 , 是因為人們有這篇文章 , 不論他們的信仰或缺乏信仰 , 他們覺得被賦予挑戰不友善的言論 , 不友善的宗教領袖、政治領袖 , 以及產業的領袖 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力 。

i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我仍然被困在舊世界裡 , 被一群人坐在一間房間裡 , 還在說另一句話 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted向我介紹一個全新的思考方式和呈現想法 。

and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 問題有時候看起來比較有吸引力 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但最後我想引用一句英國作家的論文 , 他是牛津作家 , 我不太常引用c.s.lewis 。

he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說 , 他分辨愛情的愛情 , 當兩個人凝視、拼字 , 彼此的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他把它和友誼做比較 , 當兩個人站在旁邊 , 如同 , 肩膀肩膀肩膀 , 雙眼固定在共同的目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上彼此 , 但我們能成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信 。

this gives me a chance to suggest to you the structure of the column of marcus aurelius , which is really no more than a pile of quarters high thick quarters . over the piazza of saint ignacio , completely ruining the symmetry , but that aside a spectacular place to visit .	這讓我有機會向各位建議馬克斯•奧里烏斯圓柱的結構 , 這真的不比一堆四分之一厚的石塊還要多 。 在聖賽納西亞的帕薩 , 完全毀了對稱性 , 但除了一個壯觀的地點之外 。

the text here is right side and upside down so that you are forced to turn the book around , and you can see it from ground point of view and from her point of view looking in the hole , getting a different kind of perspective , moving you around the space . particularly appropriate in a building that can contain perfectly a sphere dimensions of the diameter being the same as the distance from the center of the floor to the center of the oculus .	這裡的文字是對的 , 向下的 , 所以你被迫把書翻過來 , 從地面的角度看 , 從她的角度看 , 從洞的角度來看 , 到你周圍有不同的觀點 , 特別是適當的在一個建築裡 , 可以包含一個完全不同的空間 , 直徑是直徑的距離 , 和地面的距離一樣 , 從地面的角度看 , 到oculus的中心 。
unfortunately for her , the anchor line gets tangled around the feet of some boy scouts who are visiting the pantheon , and they are immediately yanked out and given an extraordinary but terrifying tour of some of the domes of rome , which would , from their point of view , naturally be hanging upside down .	不幸的是對她來說 , 連接線被纏住了一些男孩偵查員的腳 , 他們馬上就被拉上去了 , 給了一些奇特但恐怖的旅程 , 一些羅馬的圓頂 , 從他們的角度來看 , 天然就被綁住了 。
they bail out as soon as they get to the top of saint ivo , that little spiral structure you see there .	牠們一旦抵達聖象群的頂端 , 就會保釋出來 , 你看到的小螺旋結構 。

at the end of lunch , they untie the anchor , they set off through the baths of caracalla and over the walls of the city and then an abandoned gatehouse and decide to take one more look at the pyramid of cestius , which has this lightning rod on top .	午餐結束時 , 他們會解開管線 , 穿過卡拉浴場 , 穿過城市的牆壁 , 接著 , 一個廢棄的大門 , 決定再看一眼西斯蒂烏斯金字塔 , 上面有一道閃電線 。
unfortunately , that's a problem: they get a little too close , and when you're in a dirigible you have to be very careful about spikes .	不幸的是 , 那是個問題:它們太靠近了 , 而當你在可怕的情況下 , 你必須非常謹慎地關心這些刺激 。
so that sort of brings her little story to a conclusion .	所以 , 這會讓她的故事得到一個小結論 。
marcello , on the other hand , is sort of a lazy guy , but he's not due at work until about noon .	另一方面 , 馬賽利歐有點懶 , 但他一直都在工作 。

he gets up , leaps onto his scooter , races through the city past the church of santa maria della pace , down the alleys , through the streets that tourists may be wandering through , disturbing the quiet backstreet life of rome at every turn .	他站起來 , 跳到他的摩托車上 , 種族穿越城市 , 超越了聖地亞德拉的教堂 , 穿越了遊客的街道 , 每輪都在打擊羅馬安靜的人生 。
that speed with which he is moving , i hope i have suggested in this little image , which , again , can be turned around and read from both sides because there's text on the bottom and text on the top , one of which is upside down in this image .	他移動的速度 , 我希望我建議這張小小的圖片 , 可以轉過頭來 , 從兩側轉過來 , 因為上面的文字是上面的 , 其中一張是顛倒的圖片 。
so , he keeps on moving , approaching an unsuspecting waiter who is trying to deliver two plates of linguine in a delicate white wine clam sauce to diners who are sitting at a table just outside of a restaurant in the street .	所以 , 他繼續前進 , 接近一個毫無懷疑的服務生 , 他試圖在一個脆弱的白酒杯醬給坐在餐廳外的餐廳外面的餐桌上 。
waiter catches on , but it's too late .	服務生抓住 , 但已經太遲了 。
and marcello keeps moving in his scooter .	馬歇羅繼續前進 。
everything he sees from this point on is slightly affected by the linguine , but keeps on moving because this guy's got a job to do .	他在這個時點所看到的一切都有點受到語言的影響 , 但繼續前進 , 因為這個人有工作要做 。
removes some scaffolding . one of the reasons rome remains the extraordinary place it is that because of scaffolding and the determination to maintain the fabric , it is a city that continues to grow and adapt to the needs of the particular time in which it finds itself , or we find it .	除去一些支架 。 羅馬仍然保留了不平凡的地方 , 因為支架和決心要維護布料 , 一個城市持續成長和適應特定時間的需求 , 或我們發現它自己 。
right through the piazza della rotonda , in front of the pantheon again wreaking havoc and finally getting to work .	穿過pazzzada , 羅頓達 , 在神殿前 , 再次醒來 , 終於開始工作了 。
marcello , as it turns out , is the driver of the number 64 bus , and if you've been on the number 64 bus , you know that it's driven with the same kind of exuberance as marcello demonstrated on his scooter .	結果發現 , 馬賽利歐是64輛巴士的驅動力 , 如果你在64輛巴士上 , 你知道它的驅動力和馬塞羅在他的摩托車上證明了同樣的啟動 。

he's got candles out , he's got flowers in the middle and he's trying to figure out where to put the plates and the glasses .	他把蠟燭拿出來 , 中間有一朵花 , 他試著找出要把盤子和眼鏡放哪裡 。

enters the courtyard and talks to the custodian , who tells him that there's been a disaster in the palazzo ; nobody's tvs are working and there's a big soccer game coming up , and the crowd is getting a little restless and a little nervous .	進入庭院 , 和客戶談話 , 他告訴他 , 在帕拉索有一場災難 ; 沒有人在電視上工作 , 有一場很大的足球比賽出現 , 觀眾有一點點休息 , 有點緊張 。
he goes down to the basement and starts to check the wiring , and then gradually works his way up to the top of the building , apartment by apartment , checking every television , checking every connection , hoping to find out what this problem is .	他走到地下室 , 開始檢查電線 , 然後漸漸把他往上爬到建築的頂端 , 公寓 , 檢查每個電視 , 檢查每一個連結 , 希望找出問題是什麼 。
he works his way up , finally , the grand staircase and then a smaller staircase until he reaches the attic .	他終於成功了 , 大樓梯接著小樓梯 , 直到他抵達閣樓 。
he opens the window of the attic , of course , and there's a tablecloth wrapped around the building's television antenna .	他打開閣樓的窗戶 , 當然 , 有一張桌布包著建築物的電視天線 。
he removes it , the problems are solved , everybody in the palazzo is happy .	他除去了 , 問題解決了 , 在帕拉索的所有人都快樂 。

all he has to do now , with a perfect table , is wait for her to arrive .	他現在只需要用完美的桌子來等她抵達 。
that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是第一次嘗試 , 但似乎還不夠實質 , 來傳達我想要傳達羅馬的內容 。
so i thought , well , i'll just do piazzas , and i'll get inside and underneath and i'll show these things growing and show why they're shaped the way they are and so on .	所以我就想 , 嗯 , 我會做pazzas , 我會進去 , 下面我會展示這些東西 , 顯示出它們的形狀 , 等等 。
and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	然後我想 , 這太複雜了 。 不 , 我會把我最愛的部分和碎片放進萬神廟裡 , 把它們放進去 , 然後放大尺度 , 這樣你就可以看見聖誕節的頂端 , 克斯蒂烏斯的金字塔和巴曼特曼特島的摩托 , 一邊站在這個神奇的空間中 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	這是一張圖 , 所以我想也許是皮蘭西要和escher見面的時候了 。
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你看我已經開始失去控制權了 , 也失去希望 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	有一條非常薄的藍線 , 可以穿過這個東西 , 可以讓它整合在一起 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	然後我想: 「 等等 , 我在幹什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	書不只是收集和儲存資訊的方法 , 它是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一層一層一層一層層一層一層一層一層一層一層一層一層一層一層一層一層一層一層一層一層
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但把它們想成是層疊 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是層層層層的地形層 , 垂直層層 , 我心想 , 只要把一個頁面給你們 , 讓我可以正確地思考 , 讓我可以向你們展示層面的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大部份建築的牆壁都覆蓋著疤痕 ; 這些結構的疤痕已經被改造 , 而不是被撕裂 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一張摺紙 , 讓你把它展開 , 你可以看到我所謂的疤痕組織背後的意思 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到在1635年 , 製造小型的窗戶是必要的 , 因為壞人會來或其他東西 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	所有的適應都被埋在黏土下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以把這個pazzzo的頁面給你們看看裡面發生了什麼事 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但 , 更重要的是 , 我也能讓你們看看在其中一個偉大的建築角落 , 有著巨大的石塊 , 或用磚塊和黏土做的假石塊 , 通常更常是如此 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它變得有點立體 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以帶你們走一條狹窄的街道 , 帶到一條令人驚訝的偏遠圖上 , 用雙重的摺疊頁面 , 如果你跟我一樣 , 小時候讀一本彈性書 , 你希望能把你的頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把你的頭包裹著 , 在那短暫的時間內 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我並沒有做任何比摺疊頁更複雜的事 。
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但接著我就想 , 或許我可以簡單一點 。
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	咱們來看看萬神廟 , 前面的pazzalda 。
here's a book completely wide open .	這是一本全開的書 。
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不打開這本書 , 只要我打開90度 , 我們就在萬神廟的前面 , 我們就在看著上面 , 在廣場上 , 往下看 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我用另一種角度來看這本書 , 我們就在橫跨萬神廟的前方 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊品 , 沒有把戲 , 只是一本不開的書 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這似乎很有前景 。 我想 , 也許我會在裡面做 , 我甚至可以把摺疊品和唯一開放的書結合在一起 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	所以我們進入萬神廟裡 , 它不斷地成長 , 諸如此類 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我在正確的軌道上 , 但它失去了人類的品質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以我回到故事的概念 , 如果你想要讓人們注意書 , 一路上要有好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 震撼了我成為了 「 困境 」 標題 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果是養殖鴿子 , 它會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德賽 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是那段旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果標題有用 , 但那會是一段旅程 , 穿過羅馬 , 展示出我喜歡羅馬的東西 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	這是一隻鴿子坐在教堂的上方 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天就離去 , 做正常的鴿子 。 回來 , 整個地方被支架和綠色蚊帳覆蓋 , 這種鴿子無法回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以 , 現在是無家可歸的鴿子 , 它必須找到另一個住處 , 這讓我可以通過我最愛的目錄 , 我們從高的鴿子開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它得要回去和家人同住 , 那不是件好事 , 但它確實能把鴿子重新帶回來 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點有趣 , 但也許有一個人應該以某種方式參與其中 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老人 , 他一生都在照顧病鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會去任何地方 , 帶著危險的地方 , 帶著這個傢伙 , 學會為他做特技 , 在午餐時間和其他類似的事 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	這片老人和鴿子之間的真實債券 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 他在故事結束時就生病了 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他被教導要拼寫他的名字 , 艾爾多 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	他們在三、四天後出現 , 看不見他 , 他住在這個小小的垃圾桶裡 , 拼了他的名字 , 飛來飛去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於得到足夠的力量 , 把梯子爬到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子 , 一個拉紅氣球 , 在那裡等著他 , 把他帶到城市的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘記提到:每當他失去鴿子時 , 他就會把鴿子放到城市的牆上 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在古老的羅馬習俗中 , 死者從來沒有埋葬在牆上 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這是一個很有趣的故事 。

this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我向我的學生展示的其中一件事 , 因為這是一個完整的基準化 , 一個否認任何的觀點 。

and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你想看到聖地馬利亞德拉的步調 , 這些書真的很有彈性 , 令人難以置信的互動 , 把它轉過來 , 另一方面看 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	穿過巷子 , 我們可以看到紅線的影響 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	然後鳥類在中世紀高塔上 , 把自己拉過來 , 剩下的幾個中世紀大樓之一靠近聖誕老人的教堂 , 繞著圓頂向下 , 向下看 , 我們剛剛提到的 , 看到並流過幾次 ; 那裡是伯尼斯山脈的四條河流 , 然後越過了北京聖誕老公園 , 停止了26英尺長的距離 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	接著我們可以在裡面轉動 , 因為我們在飛行 , 我們不需要擔心重力 , 所以這張圖可以在任何頁面上隨處可見 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu時 , 我們會有點興奮 ; 這並不讓人意外 , 用這種方式來模仿建築 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	經過美好的牆上填滿了我剛剛提到的交叉義肢 ; 美麗的雕像就在尼龍上方的牆上 , 以此類推 。

and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 所以我們完成了這個理解的循環 , 你所要做的就是閱讀這些段落 。

mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院研究者skylarbbits自行組裝出一個想法 , 而不是建造東西 , 我們可以創造一些材料 , 像dnazips一樣 , 這是早期階段的一個大概念 ; tibbits向我們展示了三項隱形的計畫 , 暗示未來的樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	天空的tibbits:我們能製造製造製造自己的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想向你們展示我們製造東西的方式的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快的 , 我們的建築和機器就會自行組裝、複製、修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以我要告訴你們我所相信的 , 是目前製造業的狀態 , 然後將它和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在目前製造業的狀態中 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間 , 五十萬到一百萬個零件 , 相當複雜、令人興奮的新技術 , 在鋼鐵、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人振奮的機器可以帶我們進入太空五年--250萬個零件 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你看自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種蛋白質 , 可以在一萬奈秒內摺疊 , 或用三十億鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一個小時複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的自然系統中有這麼多複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 比我們能建造的任何東西都還要有效率 , 遠遠比我們能建造的任何複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	在能源方面 , 它們的效率更高 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎沒有犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	他們可以修復自己長壽 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 自然系統有很有意思的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以把它轉譯到我們的建設環境中 , 那就有一些令人興奮的潛力 , 可以用來建造東西 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵在於自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要自行組裝在我們的物理環境中 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的東西的複雜性 , 來建造建築和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要把它解碼成簡單的序列 , 基本上就是我們的建築如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編寫的部分 , 可以把這些序列拿來摺疊 , 或重新組合 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量 , 讓它能啟動 , 讓我們的零件能夠從程式中摺疊 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的矯正措施 , 來確保我們成功地建立我們想要的東西 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以 , 我要給你們看一些計畫 , 我的同事和我在麻省理工學院致力於達成這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	第一個是macrobot和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	這些專案是大規模的可重組機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	他們嵌入了機械裝置 , 感應器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你解碼你想要摺疊的是什麼 , 變成一連串的角度 , 負120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 負120 , 類似這樣的東西 ; 所以一連串的角度 , 或轉 , 然後你將這個序列通過弦 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都帶著它的訊息 , 負面120個它轉到那裏 , 檢查一下 , 然後把它傳給鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是聰明的科學家、工程師、設計師 , 都在這個項目上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為它真的會帶來光明:它真的是可以擴展的嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 成千上萬美元 , 製造了這個8英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能把這個放大嗎 ? 我們真的能把機器人放大到每一個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 看看被動的自然 , 或被動的嘗試有重新組合的程式性 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 它嘗試進行實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	基本上 , 它嵌入了計算的最基本組件 , 數位邏輯大門 , 直接嵌入到你的零件中 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是nand蓋茲 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	有一個四面體 , 就是你的電腦運算 , 你有兩個四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是從使用者的輸入 , 如同你正在建造你的磚塊 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一個是從前面的磚塊中放出來的 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	再給你一個3d空間的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	意思是 , 使用者可以開始加入他們想要的磚塊 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它是它之前所做的計算 , 你說它要它做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始往上或往下移動 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	在左手邊 , [1、1]輸入等於0的輸出 , 就會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入是1個輸出值 , 就會上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們所有的資訊都嵌入在其中 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個例子中 , 我稱它為自主複製 , 因為你的結構包含了完全的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都嵌入在上面 , 告訴你如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可能有爬上去閱讀的東西 , 可以在一個東西上輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它直接嵌入 , 沒有外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	我將展示的最後一個專案叫做 「 偏見鏈 」 , 它可能是我們目前被動自我組裝系統中最令人興奮的例子 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以 , 它需要可重組性和可程式性 , 讓它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你有一連串的元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每一個元素都是完全相同的 , 它們有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	每一個鏈 , 或每一個元素 , 都想要轉右轉或左轉 。
