so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈 , 你基本上是在編寫程式 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你要告訴每一個單位是否該轉右轉或左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鏈 , 它就會折疊成任何組合 , 在這個例子中 , 一個螺旋 , 或在這個例子中 , 兩個立方體相鄰 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以基本上你可以程式設計任何三維形狀或維度 , 將二維變成完全被動的鏈 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們未來什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為這告訴我們有新的可能性可以自我組裝、複製、修復、修復我們的實體結構、建築、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分有新的可程式性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從而你有新的計算可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 所有的磚塊都可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是很了不起的平行和分配的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	這對此是令人振奮的 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我在這裡所展示的這些專案只是一個小步 , 邁向這個未來 , 如果我們為一個新的自我組合世界實現這些新技術 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 我們繪製了非洲大陸 , 我們甚至去過海底最深的一點 。 下一代要去探討什麼 ? 生物學家和探險家娜森•沃爾夫提出了這個答案:幾乎每一件事 。 他說 , 以不可思議的小世界 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學、科學、生物學、
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森•沃爾夫:要去探索什麼 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我拜訪威斯康辛州的貝洛特 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡榮耀一個二十世紀偉大的探險家roychapmanandrews 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他在美國自然歷史博物館的時期 , 安德魯領導了一系列的探險 , 來到未知的區域 , 例如這裡的戈壁沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	據說他後來是印第安納瓊斯人的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛特市時 , 我公開演講給一群中學學生 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡要告訴各位 , 如果在ted演講中 , 有任何更親密的東西 , 它會試著注意到一個45分鐘課程的一群人 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	演講結束時 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但從那之後 , 我就發現了一些問題 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一位年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們該去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為 , 我們很多人有一種感覺 , 地球上偉大的探索時代已經結束了 , 對下一代來說 , 他們必須去外太空或深海 , 才能找到重要的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但這真的是事實嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	地球上真的沒有任何東西可以讓我們探索嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我回想起生物學史上最愛的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是一個看不見的世界的探險家 , 馬丁努斯•貝吉尼克 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以beijerinck開始發現煙草病的起因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是從菸草植物中取出的感染毒液 , 他會把它過濾成更小、更小的濾器 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他到了那個時候 , 他覺得一定有某種東西比當時所知最小型的生命形式還要小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的謎團找了名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 的拉丁文 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭開病毒的過程中 , beijerinck為我們開啟了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒是地球上大部分的基因信息 , 遠超過所有其他生命形式的基因信息 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯地 , 已經有很大的實際應用 , 和這個世界有關 , 比如根除天花 , 疫苗的出現是對子宮頸癌的先進 , 我們現在知道 , 大部分是由人類的乳突病毒所造成 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	beijerinck的發現 , 這不是500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前 , beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但我們不知道生命形式是如何構成我們星球上大部份的基因信息 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們可以探索未被察覺的世界 , 像是深度定序 , 讓我們能做得遠遠遠超過表面 , 看看特定物種的個別基因組 , 再看看整個代替的群體 , 在我們身邊的微生物 , 記錄這些物種的基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以把這些技巧應用到從土壤到皮膚中間的一切 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們現在常常這樣做 , 來辨識出爆發的原因 , 完全是造成它們的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓各位了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上都拿了一根鼻子 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常用這種方法來尋找呼吸道病毒 , 比如流感病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先我們會看到的是大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這些遺傳信息 , 我們會看到一些常見的嫌疑惑當然 , 很多人類遺傳信息 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大部分來自你鼻子內完全沒有傷害的事物 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也會看到非常非常令人驚訝的東西 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始研究這些資訊時 , 我們會發現 , 你鼻子裡大約百分之二十的基因信息並不符合任何我們前所未見的植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些研究這些資料的小組 , 我們當中少數人已經開始稱之為生物暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們之前見過的任何東西 ; 它有點像是我們遺傳信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻子中有20%的遺傳信息是很多生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸子 , 高達40%或50%的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對無菌的血液中 , 大約有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質無法被分類 , 不能被輸入或配對我們之前見過的任何東西 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為這可能是人造物 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對比較新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當它們變得越來越準確 , 我們決定了這些信息是生命的一種形式 , 或者至少其中一些是生命的一種形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設只是嬰兒期 , 存在著非常非常令人興奮的可能性:在這個生命中埋藏在這個遺傳信息 , 代表著尚未被辨識生命的存在 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一連串的a、t、c、g , 我們可能會發現一個全新的生命階級 , 例如beijerinck , 將徹底改變我們對生物學的本質 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這或許可以讓我們辨識出癌症的成因 , 或找出我們不熟悉的爆發來源 , 或是製造分子生物學的新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興向大家宣佈 , 和史丹佛大學的同事、加州理工學院和加州理工學院的同事 , 我們目前正在開展一項計畫 , 來探討新的生命形式存在的生物暗物質 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們不知道病毒 , 這種生命形式構成我們星球上大部份的基因信息 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們也許會驚嘆 , 我們可能完全不知道在我們的鼻子底下 , 新的生活階級 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	沒錯 , 我們可能對地球上所有的大陸進行了調查 , 我們可能已經發現了所有外在的哺乳動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的善良為下一代的探險家提供了很重要的一課 , 像是威斯康辛州的貝洛特年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我認為如果我們這樣說的話 , 就會是這樣的:不要假設我們目前認為的一切是全部的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	在你選擇探索的領域中 , 去追求暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊有未知的 , 他們等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇科學家daviddeutsch把理論物理放在後埋葬上 , 討論一個更緊急的物質:人類物種的生存 。 他說 , 第一步是要承認我們有一個問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛.德許在宇宙中的我們位置 , 位在宇宙中 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出肢體 , 說出令人驚訝的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著這樣做 , 但我想要從大家早就知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	事實上 , 首先 , 是歷史上大部分人都知道的 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 太陽系 , 或我們的環境 , 特別適合維持我們的演化或創造 , 就像過去的想法、我們現在的存在 , 以及最重要的 , 未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今這個想法有個戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	想法是 , 在太空船之外 , 宇宙是不可思議的 , 而內部則是我們所仰賴的一切 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們搞砸我們的太空船 , 我們就沒有其他地方可以去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件事 , 大家都早就知道 , 與大部分人類歷史所相信的相反 , 事實上 , 人類並不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	如同史蒂芬霍金所說的 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面的化學雕像 , 繞著一個典型的恆星軌道 , 位在一個典型的銀河系的郊區 , 諸如此類 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	大家都知道的這兩件事的第一件事就是說我們處在一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的服裝等等 , 第二件事是說我們處在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	特別是如果你把這兩個深層的真相視為深層的真理 , 來告知你人生的決定 , 那他們似乎有點衝突彼此 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能阻止他們完全錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是 。 讓我先從第二個例子開始 , 很典型嗎 ? 嗯 , 咱們來看看四周 , 看看隨機方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學氣囊 , 這完全不是典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只要朝同一個方向幾百英里 , 回頭看 , 你就不會看到任何牆或化學雕像 。 如果你更進一步看到太陽、太陽系、恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但那仍然不算典型的宇宙 , 因為星星會出現在星系中 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中大部分的地方 , 一個典型的地方 , 幾乎沒有任何星系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	所以 , 讓我們再往外走 , 直到我們在銀河系外面 , 回頭看 , 是的 , 銀河系有著巨大的銀河系 , 有著螺旋臂在我們面前擺放 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時此刻 , 我們已經有十萬光年了 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但是我們仍然離宇宙中一個典型的地方很近 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地方 , 你必須走一千倍的距離 , 到達一個星系間的空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那看起來是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中典型的地方是什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 在巨大的代價下 , ted已經安排了高解析度的虛擬實境 , 呈現出星系間空間的景象 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們能不能把燈關掉 , 請看 , 這樣我們就能看出來嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美你可以看到 , 在星系間的空間中是完全黑暗的 , 暗的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	如果你看著最近的恆星 , 那顆恆星就會爆炸成超新星 , 你就直接盯著它看 , 當它的光照射到你時 , 你甚至無法看到一個滑翔器 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙就是這麼大 , 又有多暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管事實超新星如此明亮 , 很明顯地 , 它會讓你死於幾年的光年 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星系間的空間 , 到目前為止 , 你甚至不會看到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	外面也很冷 , 比絕對零度低了三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	它是非常空的 。 真空的真空密度比目前地球上最好的科技能創造的更少一百萬倍 。 這就是這個地方的不同之處 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這地方是如此的不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能把燈關掉嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	我們要如何知道一個遙遠的環境 , 如此不同 , 外星人 , 和我們以前習慣的任何環境 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球 , 我們的環境 , 以我們的方式 , 正在創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	那到底是什麼意思 ? 嗯 , 比我們剛從這裡看的更遠一點 , 用望遠鏡 , 你就會看到看起來像星星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為 「 夸薩 」 , 原本是指量子星體 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著看起來有點像星星的東西 。 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 。 數十億年前 , 數十億光年之外 , 星系中心的物質崩塌到超大質量黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後強烈的磁場引導了重力崩塌的部分能量 。 而其中的一些物質 , 以極大的噴射流形式 , 照明了對葉的亮度 , 我認為它是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理幾乎無法像噴射機那樣的物理 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法即時存活下來 。 語言分解 , 試圖描述這些噴射機的情況 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這有點像是體驗超級新星爆炸 , 但在尖端的範圍 , 一次數百萬年 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 那個噴射機在幾十億年後發生 , 在宇宙的另一邊 , 有些化學氣味可以準確地描述、模型 , 和解釋 , 最重要的是 , 你在現實中所發生的事 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含一個精確的運作模式 , 其它的夸薩 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是一張超凡的圖像 , 雖然它包含了它 , 還包含了解釋的模型 , 體現了相同的數學關係 , 以及相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這才是知識 。 如果那還不夠驚人 , 一個結構和另一個結構相似的信念就會隨著時間而增加 。 這就是知識的成長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這種特殊的特殊特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	這種實體的物體 , 與其不同 , 儘管它們可能是一樣的 , 仍然可以體現相同的數學和因果結構 , 且隨著時間而不斷地實現 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是種化學雕塑 , 這種化學雕塑有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含著 , 有著不斷增加的精準度 , 萬物的結構 。 這個位置 , 而非宇宙中的其他位置 , 是一個中心 , 包含了整個物理現實的結構和因果本質 。 到目前為止 , 不論是無知的 , 物理定律允許這個現象 , 或甚至允許它發生 , 是物理世界最重要的事項之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼 , 太陽系和我們的環境 , 如何在我們與宇宙的其他部分取得這種特殊的關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬•霍金的評論中有一點是對的 , 但它是錯誤的強調 。 一件事是 , 它沒有用任何特殊的物理 。 沒有任何奇蹟 。 它只用了我們這裡的三件事情 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中之一是物質 , 因為知識的增長是一種資訊處理 。 資訊處理是計算 , 計算需要一台電腦 , 沒有人知道製造電腦的方法 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能源來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 讓媒體能夠影響我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 比較不具體 , 但對於開放式的知識、解釋來說 , 也是必要的 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境充滿了證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	比方說 , 牛頓重力定律大約在三百年前就發生了 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但是我們過去做過的證據 , 是在地球上每平方米上下降了數十億年前 , 之後的數十億年 , 其它的科學也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	據我們所知 , 要發現所有科學最基本的真理 , 只是為了我們地球而已 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的地點是用證據來滿足的 , 還有物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 這三種為開放式知識創造而設立的設備是最低可能的 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說 , 它是空的 , 它是冷的 , 它是暗的 。 還是嗎 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另一個失誤 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個立方體存在於星際空間 , 跟我們家一樣大 , 太陽系 。 現在這個立方體是人類標準的空缺 , 但這仍然意味著它含有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	舉例來說 , 一百萬噸足以製造一個自給自足的太空站 , 有一群科學家致力於創造一個開放式的知識流 , 等等 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 除了現代科技之外 , 還能收集來自銀河空間的氫氣 , 將其轉化成其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個完整的宇宙中 , 如果某樣東西不被物理定律禁止 , 那麼 , 哪些東西可以阻止我們去做 , 除非知道怎麼做 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 它是知識的問題 , 而非資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能自動提供能源供給 , 因為交通運輸會是核融合反應器和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	同樣的 , 這對人類的感官來說是暗的 。 但你所要做的就是用一個望遠鏡 , 即使是現今的設計 , 向外看 , 像我們從這裡看到的銀河系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	有了更強大的望遠鏡 , 你可以看見恆星 , 行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在這些星系中 , 你可以做天體物理學 , 學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	當地的粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理 , 化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	可能最困難的科學會是生物領域的旅程 , 因為要花上數億年才能到達最近的生命星球 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你們 , 抱歉 , 理查但我從來沒有像生物學場一樣我認為我們每隔幾億年就可以完成一件事
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	事實上 , 星系間的空間包含了所有開放式知識的前提 。 任何這樣的立方體 , 在宇宙的任何地方 , 都可能變成我們現在的中心 , 如果有這樣的知識的話 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以我們不是一個獨特的友善地點 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系空間能夠創造出一個開放的解釋流 , 那幾乎是所有其他的環境 。 地球也是污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	這裡和這裡的限制因素 , 並不是資源 , 因為它們很充足 , 但知識 , 很可怕 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這種以知識為基礎的觀點 , 我認為應該讓我們覺得很特別 。 但它也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著 , 若沒有必要的特定知識 , 我們就無法存活在宇宙的挑戰中 , 我們就不會存活下來 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要一個超新星 , 才能在幾年之外離開 , 我們都會死去 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁雷斯最近寫了一本關於我們脆弱的書 , 從天體物理 , 到科學實驗都出錯了 , 最重要的是 , 大規模毀滅性武器的恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有50%的機率能在這個世紀生存 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他等一下會議上會談到這件事 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為機率是正確的分類來討論這個問題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他這件事 , 我們可以生存下來 , 我們無法存活下來 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這並不取決於偶然 , 而是我們是否創造了相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險完全不是史無前例的物種會隨時滅絕
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終止了 。 絕大多數的物種和文明都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為例外 , 那麼我們唯一的希望就是利用一種區別我們物種的特徵 , 和我們的文明 , 從其它地方來看 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋、新的知識成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 讓我把這個應用到目前的爭議上 , 不是因為我想要提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 而是來說明我所說的 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但根據這個理論 , 我不是正確的物理學家 。 在全球暖化方面 , 我只是一個拉曼 。 一個拉曼人要做的理性是嚴肅地看待科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 它已經太遲了 , 它已經無法避免災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為 , 如果我們現在最好的選項就是阻止二氧化碳排放 , 像是京都議定書 , 它的經濟活動和它極大的成本 , 成千上萬的美金 , 不論是什麼 , 那就已經是個災難了 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	倡導者的行動 , 甚至都沒有在意去解決這個問題 , 僅僅僅只是稍微延後它 。 所以它已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免任何人意識到危險 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	可能已經太晚了 , 在1970年代 , 當最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放即將在數十億的新年內滅亡 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這一切對我來說似乎很明顯 , 我不知道為什麼它沒有公開的辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	我們永遠不會知道 。 當我們知道即將發生的災難 , 以及如何在災難本身的成本下解決這個問題 , 那就不會有太多的爭論了 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預先的預防原則 , 可以避免我們還未預見的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要解決問題的立場 , 不只是問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	是的 , 預防的一盎司就等於一磅解藥 , 但只有我們知道預防什麼 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你曾在鼻子上打過鼻子 , 那麼醫學的科學並不符合教導你避免打擊 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學不再尋求治療方法 , 只專注在預防上 , 那它也無法做到 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	目前世界正在緩和計劃 , 針對所有成本減少氣體排放 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要用計畫來降低溫度 , 用計畫來生活在更高的溫度上 , 而不用花任何成本 , 而是有效率且便宜的 。 有些計畫存在 , 例如在太空中的鏡子 , 將陽光轉移 , 並鼓勵水生生物吃掉更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	目前 , 這些東西都是fringe研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	它們不是人類努力要面對這個問題的核心 , 或一般的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	我們還沒察覺到的問題 , 把正確的能力放在無限的避免 , 不是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩個石板平板 , 刻在上面 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中之一 , 卡夫: 「 問題是可笑的 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一張地毯則是: 「 問題是無可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	如果被困在不好規則的系統中 , 掙扎的國家要如何脫離貧窮 ? 經濟學家保羅•羅默斯揭開了一個大膽的想法: 「 市區 , 城市的行政區是由國家的聯盟所統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	paulromer的想法是基礎的:城市特區城市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們帶來了一個非常吸引人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的機場上做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有電 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特殊的學生 , 但我見過像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉個例子 , 綠色襯衫的那件 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	讓我們給他一個名字:nelson 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我打賭nelson有一支手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這就是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森能取得像手機一樣的尖端技術 , 但無法取得一百歲的科技 , 讓家裡產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	換句話說 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不好的規則可以預防這種雙贏的解決方案 , 當人們能把新科技帶進來 , 讓他們可以用在像尼爾森這樣的人身上 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在一個規則下運行 , 說它必須以非常低、補貼的價格 , 事實上 , 一個價格低到每一單位都需要錢 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以它既不是資源 , 也不是激勵措施 , 連接其他的使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他發現 , 有可能有不同的規則 , 企業賺取小額利潤的規則 , 所以他們有動機去登記更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這類規則是尼爾森公司購買的手機公司 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統知道這些規則是如何運作的 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變用電來定價的規則 , 但從事業和消費者身上 , 他們想要保存現有的補助金率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他陷入困境的規則 , 阻止他讓雙贏的解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森被困在街燈下學習 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是要試著找出我們要如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	我們有沒有可以發展出一些規則來改變規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想說的是 , 我們能做實用抽象的見解 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給予更多選擇的人 , 以及在許多國家的領導者更多的選擇 , 也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 呈現這兩者之間的反對是有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想要給領導人的那種選擇 , 例如給予總統在電力上提高價格 , 消除經濟想要的人們所做的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望選擇繼續消耗補貼的電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只給一邊或另一邊 , 你就會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到更多選擇的方法 , 那就能給我們一套改變規則 , 來讓我們擺脫陷阱 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也能取得網路 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則的損害 , 規則會讓人們留在黑暗中 , 看看美國太空總署的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 跟鄰居的黑洞相比 , 這就像是黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會驚訝地發現北韓的規則讓人們處在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但很重要的是 , 北韓和南韓一開始就有相同的規則 , 從法律和規定的角度來看 , 同時也在更深層的層面上 , 了解、規範、文化、價值觀和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做了選擇 , 導致了非常不同的規則 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們可以改變人類的規則 , 可以改變我們彼此互動的規則 , 讓彼此更好 , 或更糟 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在讓我們來看看另一個加勒比海地區 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 這裡的線上 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也是黑暗的 , 和這裡的鄰居相比 , 多明尼加共和國的居民數目差不多 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家都和波多黎各比較黑暗 , 這裡有一半的居民是海地或多明尼加共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們的是 , 規則是壞的 , 因為政府是弱的 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不單是那些規則是壞事 , 因為政府太強壯、太壓迫了 , 就像北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想用良好的規則來創造環境 , 我們不能只撕下它 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須找出方法來建造 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國顯著證明了與規則相關的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	在這張圖表中 , 中國是世界上高科技領導人 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國的先驅技術 , 如鋼、印刷、槍擊 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從來沒有採用 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則 , 鼓勵這些想法散播出去 , 一種利潤的動機 , 可以鼓勵散播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了規則 , 減緩了創新 , 讓中國遠離世界 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 世界上其他國家創新 , 同時發展新科技 , 也發展出新的規則 , 中文則從這些進步中被切斷 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	那裡的收入一直停滯不前 , 在世界其餘的其他地方 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表比較近期的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它描繪了中國平均收入的百分比美國平均收入的百分比
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50和60年代 , 你可以看到 , 大約佔3% 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但到了70年代末期 , 事情改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	在中國 , 經濟開始起飛 , 中國開始迅速接觸到美國 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你晚上回到地圖 , 就能得到一個線索 , 讓中國的規則大幅改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最明亮的地點 , 如你所看到的 , 就是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀大部分的時候 , 都在一套很不一樣的規則下運作 , 比起其他的中國規則 , 從當時工作市場經濟 , 由英國管理 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是個地方 , 那裡有數百萬人可以從大陸開始 , 開始工作 , 比如縫衣、製作玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了達到增加收入的過程 , 越來越多的技能導致那裡非常快速的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是個典範 , 像香港這樣的領導人可以複製 , 當他們決定把所有的大陸都搬到市場模式上 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到提供他人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫所有人立即轉移到市場模式 , 他們的發展是透過創造一些特殊的區域 , 在某種程度上 , 英國所做的是:讓機會和市場規則合作 , 讓那些想要選擇的人可以選擇 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港附近創建了四個特別的經濟區 , 中國人可以來工作 , 城市很快地長大 ; 也有區塊 , 外國公司可以進來製造東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區域有一座叫做 「 深圳 」 的城市
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡 , 有一間台台灣公司製造了iphone , 在座許多人都有 , 他們用中國人的勞工來做 , 搬到深圳 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以在四個特別區域之後 , 有14個海岸居民在同樣的意義上被打開 , 最終也在這些地方展現出成功 , 讓人們可以選擇 , 因他們提供的優勢而被困住 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	在那裡證實了成功 , 導致了整個經濟模式的共識 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	現在 , 中國的例子顯示了幾點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:保存人們的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:在正確的規模上運作 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變村落的規則 , 你可以這樣做 , 但村落太小了 , 如果你有數百萬人在良好的規則下工作 , 就會得到一些好處 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變國家的規則 , 你不能給一些人一個機會 , 看看事情是怎麼回事 , 讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給了你機會 , 創造新的地點 , 讓人們可以選擇的新規則 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們夠大 , 足以得到我們所能得到的所有利益 , 只要數百萬人在良好的規則下工作 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 我們的提案是構想一個叫做 「 特許城市 」 的概念 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們先從一個調查開始 , 找出所有規則 , 來吸引我們需要建造城市的人們 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者來建造基礎建設──電力系統、道路、港口、機場、建築 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引公司 , 他們會僱用先搬到那裡的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家庭 , 居民來到那裡 , 永久地養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子接受教育 , 並為他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	在這張圖表中 , 人們會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造出來 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一次又一次地做 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要成功 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	這些都是在查特上捕捉的 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	如果我們可以在無人居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 , 那就被建造出來了 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從未居住的領土開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以在新的調查之下生活 , 但沒有人被迫生活在其中 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後 , 我們需要的是領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想要的選項 , 我們想要的領導者 , 讓國家之間的合作可能:國家合作的情況 , 實際上 , 實際上 , 中國和英國合作的方式 , 首先加入市場模式 , 然後擴展到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 不經意地透過它在香港的行動 , 減少了世界貧窮 , 比上個世紀 , 我們所採取的援助計畫還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以 , 如果我們允許這種合作關係再次複製 , 我們就能得到全世界的規模 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到責任的授權 , 一個國家的控制權 , 來接管某些行政的責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我這麼說的時候 , 你們當中有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這會帶來殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是的 。 但很重要的是要了解當我們開始思考這些事情時會產生的那種情緒 , 可以讓我們退一步 , 可以關閉我們的能力 , 並且我們想要探索新點子的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這和殖民主義不一樣 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義是不好的 , 而我們一些援助方案中 , 基本上是不太好的 , 就是它涉及了合作和執行的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是關於選擇 , 無論是領導者 , 還是為了住在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是對抗合作和欺騙的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談這在練習中是如何發揮的 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	我們拿一個特殊的領導人raulcastro , 他是古巴的領導人 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定有機會為古巴做古巴的古巴做事 , 但他在古巴的島上沒有香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	然而 , 他在南方有一點點亮 , 上面有很特殊的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	那裡有一區 , 位在南阿莫灣 , 在那裡 , 條約讓美國政府對一塊土地負責 , 大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚去了加拿大總理 , 說: 「 看 , 雅諾斯有一個很糟的pr問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不去加拿大呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造一個特殊的行政區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓新城市在上面建造 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們在附近有個香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些公民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會回來 。 但這將會是通往現代經濟和現代世界的通道 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這個模型還在哪裡呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	許多人完全得到特殊區域的概念 , 讓人們可以選擇成為一個規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	它是改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新規則的方式 , 讓人們不需要強迫 , 反對 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以對長期投資者做出更可靠的承諾 , 這樣的投資者 , 來建造港口、建造道路 , 在新的城市裡 , 他們可以做出更可靠的承諾 , 如果他們能和另一半國家合作的話 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	甚至在一些安排中 , 有點像是一份核心帳戶 , 把土地放入核心帳戶中 , 伴侶國家負起責任 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	在非洲也有許多土地 , 在那裡 , 新城市可以建造 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我在海岸飛行時拍的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣的土地有很大的延伸 , 在那裡 , 有數億人可以住 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	如果我們概括一下 , 想想看 , 不僅僅是一或二個特區居民 , 還有數十萬個城市 , 為數億城市創造地方 , 甚至數十億人口 , 在未來的世紀 , 將有足夠的土地給他們 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在世界各地 , 如果我們晚上看燈 , 誤導的一件事是 , 視覺上 , 世界大部分都已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我告訴各位 , 為什麼會錯 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以這代表所有土地的代表為例 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個平方 , 代表地球上所有可耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表現在已經被三十億人居住的城市佔據的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把點移到長方形的底部 , 你可以看到 , 現有的城市有三十億居民 , 佔地球上僅佔了百分之三的可耕地 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想要為另外十億人建造城市 , 他們就會像這樣點點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們將從百分之三的可耕地變成百分之四 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大幅減少地球上的人類足跡 , 藉由建造更多的城市 , 讓人們可以移動 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市被良好的規則所管理 , 就能成為城市 , 在那裡 , 人民是安全的 , 不受犯罪、疾病和公共衛生的城市 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會找到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	它們能取得基本的電力 , 像是電力 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要建造第一個特區城市 , 要花多少時間才能建造出更多的城市 ?
it would help to have a manual .	這對手冊有幫助 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授能做的是寫一些細節 , 寫進這個手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們經營城市 , 去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會在野外放學術 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們思考像這樣的問題 , 假設不只是加拿大 , 處理拉爾卡斯特的問題 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	或許巴西是參與者 , 西班牙也可能 。 也許古巴想成為四個聯合公司的夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要怎麼寫條約 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	沒有任何先例 , 但那可以輕鬆地被解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	結果發現 , 新加坡和香港是城市 , 在他們剛開始時 , 土地的價值很大 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地上的收入來支付像警察、法院等的東西 , 但學校系統和醫療系統 , 讓這個地方更吸引人 , 人們的收入更高 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 人們協助建構這個區域的人的動機 , 建立它 , 並設立基本規則 , 朝向正確的方向 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有很多類似的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們怎麼可能有低成本的建築 , 負擔得起第一份工作的人 , 組裝類似iphone的東西 , 讓那些建築物有效率 , 確保它們是安全的 , 所以它們不會掉落地震或颶風 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術上的細節要處理 , 但那些已經開始追求這些事的人 , 已經知道沒有障礙 , 沒有障礙 , 除了想像的失敗之外 , 這種細節讓我們無法實現真正的全球雙贏的解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片來總結 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能如此順利 , 是因為地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和別人分享想法 , 當他們發現這些想法時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀有物品 , 分享的意思是 , 我們的收入越來越少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們就會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用那樣的方式思考想法 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一種想法:管理我們如何互動的規則 ; 例如 , 讓我們有一個計程系統 , 來支持一個研究大學 , 免費提供某種知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	我們有一個系統 , 讓土地能被登記在政府辦公室 , 人民可以承諾承諾是屬於殖民地 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能持續創新我們對規則的空間 , 尤其是創新的概念是改變規則的概念 , 所以我們不會被困在不好的規則 , 那麼我們就能繼續向前進 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 像尼爾森和他的朋友不再需要在街燈下學習 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	遺傳學先驅克萊格•凡特休息了一段時間 , 他的團隊發現了數百萬個基因 , 來繪製海洋生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、企業家、基因、發明、海洋、科學、科技、科技、
craig venter on dna and the sea	克萊格•凡特在dna和海上 , 和海上的克萊格•凡特 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時間 , 我被幾個人問到我對老化辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將會是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者大大勝過悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我18分鐘內 , 我將告訴各位 , 我們將如何從基因編碼轉換到開始寫程式的第一階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	直到十年前 , 我們才出版了第一個自由生存的有機體序列 , 也就是大象流感 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫花了13年到4個月的基因組計畫 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八個小時內做同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	過去十年間 , 大量的基因組被加上:大部份的人類病原體、幾株植物、昆蟲和哺乳類 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	十年前 , 在這個想法的階段 , 基因組學是今年底 , 我們可能有三到五個基因組序列 , 數百個基因組 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	今年我們剛從戈登和貝蒂摩爾基金得到了一百三十個基因組 , 作為環保生物的副方案 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以閱讀基因密碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但 , 正如我們所看到的 , 我們幾乎無法在這個星球上抓到的表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分人都不明白 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物組成約半個地球的生物量 , 而所有生物組成的生物量只有一分之一 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是牛津人不常做的事 , 但如果你把它放到海裡 , 吞下一口海水 , 記住每一毫升就有大約一百萬個細菌 , 和一千萬個病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	不到五千種微生物物種被標記為兩年前 , 所以我們決定採取行動 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開啟了sercer二號探險 , 當時我們是大型的海洋探險 , 嘗試每200英哩的海洋樣本 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始測試 , 然後搬到哈利法克斯 , 沿著美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿過太平洋 , 我們現在正在橫跨印度洋 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這非常困難 ; 我們在帆船上做這件事 , 一部分是要協助刺激年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只用海水過濾它 , 我們用不同的濾器收集不同的大小生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 每24小時就可以排列出一億個基因密碼 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	藉此 , 我們有了驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	例如 , 認為我們眼睛裡的視覺色素 , 只有一到兩種有機體有著同樣的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎所有海洋上半部的生物 , 都有相同的感光器 , 使用陽光 , 和它們的能量和溝通來源一樣 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個網站 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了一百三十萬個新基因 , 和五萬個新物種一樣多 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們現在把它延伸到空中 , 帶著來自sloan基金會的資金 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們測量到我們每天呼吸的病毒和細菌數量 , 特別是在飛機或關閉的會堂上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們通過一些簡單的外表過濾 ; 我們一天從紐約市的一棟大樓上收集了十億微生物 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	我們正處於當代排序的過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	就在資料收集方面 , 我們在加拉帕戈斯所在的地方 , 我們發現幾乎每200英哩的樣本 , 我們在海洋中看到極大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些邏輯上是合理的 , 以不同溫度的梯度來看 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 以紅色表示溫度 , 藍色是溫暖 , 我們發現暖水樣本和冷水樣本之間有很大的差異 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件讓我們吃驚的事是這些光受器偵測不同的光波長 , 我們可以根據它們的氨基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些從各地到各地都很大的不同 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外地 , 在深海 , 大部分是藍色的地方 , 光受器通常會看到藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有很多葉綠素時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們可能更加不同 , 在極端的紅外線和紫外線 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了得到我們的基因複製品的評估 , 我們把所有的資料組合起來 , 包括我們在遠征的所有資料 , 這代表了地球上所有基因資料的一半 , 總共大約兩千九百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些資料放入基因家庭 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們是否只是發現已知家庭的新成員 ? 還是發現新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但我們在環境中採集的每一個新樣本 , 都會加上線性時尚 , 給這些新家人 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以我們正處於這個星球上最早期的發現 , 關於基本基因、元件和生命的發現 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看所謂的進化樹 , 我們就在右上角和動物的右上角 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	在大約兩千九百萬個基因中 , 我們的基因體中只有大約兩萬四千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有動物聚集在一起 , 我們可能有不到三萬個 , 可能有十幾個不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我覺得這些基因不僅僅是進化的設計元素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為在基因中心的觀點 , 也許回到理查德•達金斯的觀點 , 遠遠超過基因中心的觀點 , 這些基因元件的不同 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力 , 在過去十年或二十年間 , dna定序的速度和dna定序的速度有了差不多 , 且很便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們首先想到合成基因組學當我們在1995年重組第二組基因組 , 從墨西哥柏斯的生殖器 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 上面寫著: 「 我是我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	漢氏症有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只會問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 另一個500 , 是否有較小的基因組可以組成最小的營運系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以 , 我們開始進行 「 變性器突變 」 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	翻譯只是隨機插入基因密碼中的小片dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果它們插入基因的中間 , 它們會破壞它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了所有可以接受轉譯植入的基因地圖 , 我們稱之為 「 不必要的基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境是非常關鍵的 , 你只能根據環境中的特質來定義一個必要或不必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用更直接的智力方法和13個相關的生物基因組做比較 , 我們試著比較它們的共通點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們找到了重疊的圓圈 。 我們找到了173個基因 , 所有13個生物都有 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	池塘擴張一點 , 如果我們忽略一個細胞寄生蟲 , 它會擴展得更廣 , 只要我們檢視核心基因的核心組合 , 大約是310組 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴展或收縮基因組 , 取決於你的觀點 , 到大約300到400個基因 , 從最低的500個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法的唯一方法就是建造一個人工染色體 , 裡面有這些基因 , 我們必須在一個以石膏為基礎的時尚中做這件事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現 , 在大片中合成精確的dna是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	漢姆.史密斯和克莉德•赫奇奇森 , 我的同事開發了一種令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能夠合成五千個鹼基對的病毒 , 僅僅是兩週的時間 , 它的序列和它的生物學 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是個令人振奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna注入細菌 , 突然間 , dna開始開車製造病毒粒子 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個合成病毒 , 一個小兒麻痺病毒在一年之前就被製造出來了 , 但它僅僅是活躍的十分之一 , 而且花了三年的時間 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的結構 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是一個軟體製造自己的硬體 , 那就是我們對生物學的觀念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上開始關心生物戰事 , 我最近在參議院委員會前證實 , 美國政府設立了特殊委員會來審查這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 要記住現實是很重要的 , 而不是人們的想像力 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 現今已經有任何基因組的病毒都可以被製造出來 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上就對伊波拉或天花的事物感到害怕 , 但這種生物的dna沒有傳染性 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人製造了天花的基因組 , dna本身也不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	安全部門真正關心的是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 努力創造生物戰事代理人 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這項研究真的被不一致 , 未來就不會有任何的知識來製造設計病毒 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為兩年內就有可能實現單細胞生物 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能在十年內 , 那些我們擁有的真菌細胞 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	我們現在正在製造數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變這個人造染色體的casettes和基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 你要如何把所有其他人都放在一起 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一個同類的重組系統 , 將它們重新組合成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個生物體中衍生出來的 , 分泌無線電 , 可能需要三百萬個輻射 , 且不會被殺害 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆發後 , 它會重新組合出它的基因組 , 大約12到24小時後 , 在它的染色體被拆開之後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上無所不在 , 可能是因為我們的旅途而存在於外太空 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是個半百萬輻射後的杯子 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和裂縫 , 而微生物就在底部變得更快樂、更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這張圖片顯示了一百七十萬個輻射後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體真的會分解 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna自動重新組合了24小時 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	令人驚訝的是 , 這些生物能做到這一點 , 我們可能有數千種 , 如果不是數萬種 , 在這個星球上有能力做到這一點的物種 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合成之後 , 第一步就是移植到沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	因此 , 我們認為合成細胞將會有很大的潛力 , 不僅是了解生物學的基礎 , 還有希望環境和社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們排序的第三種生物中 , 甲烷會生存在沸騰的水溫 ; 它的能量來源是氫 , 它的碳會從環境中捕捉到 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 數千種不同的生物從二氧化碳中存活下來 , 並捕捉到它 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其使用石油合成過程的碳 , 我們有機會使用碳 , 從大氣中捕捉回來 , 將它轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種生物體 , 住在一氧化碳中 , 我們用它來減少水分 , 來產生氫和氧 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 有許多可以改造代謝甲烷的途徑 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦有一個主要的計畫 , 用挪威的雕像來捕捉和轉換加油場的甲烷 , 變成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	在短短的一段時間內 , 我覺得會有一個新的領域叫做 「 組合基因組 」 , 因為這些新的合成能力 , 這些大量的基因庫重組 , 以及同源的組合 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 來製造一百萬個不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 就如同所有的生物學 , 你通過篩選 , 不論你是在篩選氫氣生產 , 或化學生產 , 或單純的可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因的作用 , 會很棒 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用 , 從陽光直接製造氫 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用被氧氣調節 , 我們認為會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也結合了細胞膜 , 分解複雜糖的酵素 , 分解成簡單糖和發酵 , 以產生乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	製藥生產已經在主要實驗室進行了 , 用微生物 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物所產生的化學物質比我們最好的化學家所產生的複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可以是食物的來源 , 希望是能量的來源 , 環保的補救 , 也許還可以取代石化產業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策研究來總結 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在1999年延遲實驗的開端 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理審查 , 來嘗試製造人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要的宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各式各樣的宗教領袖都在用他們的經文作為法律書 , 他們找不到任何東西 , 禁止創造生命 , 所以這必須是沒關係的 。 唯一的重點是生物戰事方面 , 但給了我們前進的研究 , 以我們做這些實驗的原因 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在sloan基金會剛剛資助了一份多個機構研究 , 來找出對社會的風險和利益 , 以及像我這樣的科學團隊應該採用的規則 , 我們正嘗試設立好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的議題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是非常簡單的問題 , 我們是否能設計出清潔能源 , 或許革命 , 讓開發中國家能做些什麼 , 並提供各種簡單的過程 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家philipzimbardo說幸福和成功根植在我們大部分人的遺傳特徵中:我們對過去的方向、現在和未來的方向 。 他建議我們在時間的第一步改善我們的生活 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心智、心理學、科學、科學、科學、
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo開了健康的處方 , 時間很長 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密力量的概念 , 在很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好的 , 開始吧 。 30秒的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	讓它安靜下來 , 安頓下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	時間到了 , 排序 。 一 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10、9、8、7、6、4、3、2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利普•辛巴多:咱們來談談亞當的校長誘惑 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 拜託亞當 , 別太小心了 。 吃點東西 。 」 「 我有 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , 亞當 , 別拋棄eve 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好 , 一一口 。 到底怎麼了 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是誘惑 。 一切都是關於產生、抗拒的 , 是的 , 晚點 , 衝動、反思、焦點 , 以及未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	被保證的美德會落在當下的熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	青少年女孩在婚前宣傳性缺席和處女 , 感謝喬治布什多數 , 60% , 她們在一年之內就對性誘惑產生影響 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	他們大部分都沒有用出生控制 。
so much for promises .	太多的承諾了 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們誘惑四歲的孩子 , 給他們一個治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到實驗者回來 , 他們就可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 它會支付 , 等待 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	三分之二的孩子因誘惑而放棄 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等待 。 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 現在延遲了 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	華特•密歇爾 , 我在史丹佛大學的同事 , 14年後 , 發現那些孩子的不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在許多方面 , 抗拒的孩子和受益的孩子之間有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	那些拒絕分數250分的孩子 , 在座位上比較高 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這很巨大 。 這就像一整組不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有惹上麻煩 。 他們是更好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們是自信且有決心的 。 而今天對我而言 , 關鍵在於 , 他們是被賦予未來的 , 而不是被賦予的 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間的觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間的觀點是研究個體 , 我們所有人 , 將你的經驗分成時間區或時間分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而你會自動做 , 無意識地做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	文化、國家、社會階級、教育水平之間的差異不同 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們會變得有偏見 , 因為你學會了濫用其中的一些 , 並且濫用其他的 。
what determines any decision you make ?	你做了什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你做出一個決定 , 決定你要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對於某些人 , 只有在當下的情況下 , 其他人在做什麼 , 以及你所感受到的 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而這些人 , 當他們做決策時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 簡報 」 , 因為他們的焦點是現在的 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是不相關的 。
