it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是在說: 「 我過去經歷過的這種情況是什麼樣子 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以 , 他們的決策基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們將這些人稱之為 「 過去式 」 , 因為他們專注於什麼 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 也不是現在 , 而是關於未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是關於預期的後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們將稱之為 「 未來 」 。 他們的專注力是 「 未來 」 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想說 , 時間觀點的悖論 , 是影響你所做的每一個決定 , 你完全無法察覺的 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你有這種偏見的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六個方法 。 有兩種方式可以呈現出來 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以遵守 , 兩種方式是未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正向或負面 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是具體化的 , 也就是你專注於生活的喜悅 , 或當下的主義者 , 這無所謂 , 你的生命被控制著 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以有未來的目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超然的未來:生命起源於死亡 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展靈活性 , 讓時間觀點流暢地取決於情況的需求 , 這就是你需要學習的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 最佳時間檔案是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	正面積極高 , 適當的將來 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	和現代主義的調節 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於負面的和當下的利益 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的暫時混合就是你從過去的過去所得到的基礎 , 會讓你的家人、身分和自我聯繫 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來所得到的 , 是翅膀到新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的享樂主義得到的就是能量 , 去探索你自己 , 地方 , 人們 , 感知 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	過多的觀點 , 比正面觀點 , 任何時間的觀點都有更多的負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	成功的未來會有什麼犧牲 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間 , 他們犧牲朋友的時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲有趣的時光 , 犧牲個人的絕緣 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲嗜好 , 犧牲睡眠 , 影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們活下來是為了工作、成就和控制 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我確信這和一些ted人有所共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	它對我產生共鳴 。 我成長為南布朗克斯貧民區的窮孩子 , 一個西西西西里家庭 , 大家過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來這裡是一位未來人 , 走過頂端 , 做這些犧牲 , 是因為老師介入 , 讓我成為未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那塊棉花糖 , 因為如果你等著你會拿到兩顆 , 直到我學會平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了現代主義 , 我把焦點放在過去的思維上 , 所以 , 在76歲時 , 我比以前更活躍 , 更有生產力 , 我比以前更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只想說 , 我們把這個應用到許多世界問題上:改變學校孩子的輟學率 , 結合成癮 , 增加青少年健康 , 用時間隱喻來治療創傷後壓力症候群 , 促進永續發展和保育 , 減少身體復健 , 在那裡有50%的輟學 , 改變了自殺恐怖份子 , 以及改變家庭衝突的時間 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說的是:許多人生的謎題都可以透過了解時間觀和其他人的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果真的很深刻 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	現今的頭條在一百年內會發生什麼事 ? 一百年後 ? kirkcron的 「 長新聞 」 專案收集現今不重要的故事 , 數十年來 , 甚至會有共鳴 。 在ted2010年 , 他強調了未來的可能性頭條 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學、科學、科學、
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcron:現在 , 真正的新聞報導了 。
we are drowning in news .	我們在新聞中淹沒 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是路透社每年就發佈了三百五十萬個新聞 。
that's just one source .	這只是一個源頭 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:長期來看 , 那些故事中有多少會很重要 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是長期新聞的主意 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是一個長期基金會的專案 , 由tedster成立 , 包括凱文凱利和史都華•布蘭德 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們在尋找的新聞故事 , 可能是50到100 , 000年後的新聞故事 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過過濾器看新聞時 , 很多東西會從旁邊掉下來 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	去年 , 為了從a.p.上層的故事 , 這會在十年內發生嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這會在50或100年後產生影響嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 那有點酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但 , 過去一年的上述故事是經濟 , 我打賭 , 很快 , 或後來 , 這個特殊的經濟衰退將會是舊的消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 什麼樣的故事能為未來帶來改變 ?
well , let's take science .	咱們來談談科學 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會穿過我們的血液循環 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是隻老鼠 , 某一天就已經在這裡了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近一些故事:奈米蜜蜂和真蜂毒液的腫瘤 , 它們會把基因傳送到大腦 ; 一個可以爬過人體的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源呢 ? 我們要如何餵飽九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	我們現在有六十億人在吃麻煩 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國人如果沒有基因改造的作物 , 就會餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲已經賭上十億人 。
what about global politics ?	那麼全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界將會變得非常不一樣 , 如果中國設定議程 , 他們可能會 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們超越了美國 , 成為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們超越了德國 , 成為最大的出口者 , 他們開始做dna測試 , 來選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們找到各種方法來推動我們所知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	最近的一些發現:阿根廷有一個蟻群 , 現在已經散播到各大陸 , 但南極洲 ; 有一個自主導導導向的機器人科學家 , 很快就發現了 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 生命也可能不再需要我們了 ; 十二萬年後 , 一個微生物出現了 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	看似沒有我們 , 生命會繼續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但我在去年的長期新聞中發現了這個:在月球上找到的水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	更容易把蜂群放上去 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不這麼做 , 中國可能會 , 或者在座的某個人可能會寫一份大支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長期來看 , 有些新聞比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	地球科學家卡洛琳•波科斯從卡林航行到土星的影像 , 專注在土星上最大的衛星、土衛六、土衛六 , 這看起來像是冰山噴射的照片 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	美國太空總署、設計、探索、科學、太空、科技、宇宙、視覺化、視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	卡羅琳•皮科讓我們飛到土星上 ,
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘 , 我會帶你們踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這趟旅程 , 各位和我已經經歷了很多年 , 它從50年前開始 , 人類第一次離開地球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在那50年裡 , 我們不僅真的在月球上落下了腳 , 我們還把機械太空船送到所有八個行星上 , 我們登陸了小行星 , 在這個時點 , 我們有了一架太空船 , 用來冥王星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械任務都是人類旅程的一部分:一趟旅程 , 去了解某樣東西 , 去了解我們的宇宙 , 去了解我們的起源 , 以及地球 , 我們的地球 , 我們的生命來源 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系的所有地方 , 我們可能會去尋找像這樣的問題的答案 , 這是土星 。 我們去過土星 , 在1980年代早期 , 我們去過土星的調查之後 , 土星的調查已經變得更加深刻 , 因為卡西尼太空船 , 在2004年的夏天 , 穿越了星球 , 穿越了星球 , 在2004年的夏天 , 走到土星的軌道上 , 成為了人類最遙遠的機器人 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是很豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供神秘、科學的洞見 , 顯然超越了這個系統的研究 , 對於宇宙的發展有極大的影響 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是研究環 , 我們就知道很多恆星和氣體的圓盤 , 我們稱之為 「 螺旋星系 」 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這裡有一張anmedanebula的美麗照片 , 是我們最接近、最大的螺旋星系 , 到銀河系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	接著 , 這是漩渦銀河系的美麗部分 , 由哈伯太空望遠鏡拍攝 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程是一部分 , 同時也是一個比喻 , 一個更大的人類旅程 , 來了解我們身邊的所有事物 , 以及人類如何融入這張圖片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我痛苦的是 , 我無法告訴你們我們在卡西尼身上學到的一切 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法給你們看我們過去兩年半所拍攝的美麗照片 , 因為我沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以我將集中在這次重大的探險探險旅程中最令人興奮的兩次 , 我們正在進行土星探索 , 過去兩年半 , 一直都是如此 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星是由非常大且多樣化的衛星所組成 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的尺寸從幾公里長到像美國一樣大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們拍攝土星的大部分美麗的照片 , 事實上 , 土星和它的一些衛星相處 。 這是土星和鑽石的土星 , 然後 , 這裡是土星 , 展示了地表 , 展示了它們的垂直稀薄度 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	現在 , 土星47顆衛星中有兩顆衛星是固定的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛六和土衛二 。 土衛六是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼抵達那裡 , 是太陽系中我們剩下的最大一片未被探索的地形 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	這個身體有很長一段感興趣的人觀看行星 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有一個很大、很厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為比較像是地球上的環境 , 或至少過去 , 比任何其他太陽系的身體都要大 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層主要是氮分子 , 就像你在這個房間裡呼吸一樣 , 除了它的大氣層含有簡單的有機物質 , 比如甲烷、丙烷和乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些分子在土衛六大氣層中被打破 , 它們的產品結合在一起 , 形成了 「 黑色粒子 」 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這隻海鮮無所不在 , 完全是全球性的 , 完全是霸主 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這就是為什麼你不能用眼睛看不見表面 , 用光譜中可見的區域 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些混合的粒子 , 在我們和卡西尼一起到達之前 , 已經有數十億年了 , 溫柔地漂移到表面 , 將表面覆蓋在有機泥中 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	所以 , 就像泰坦 , 油 , 油 , 油 , 或我們不知道的東西 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這就是我們猜想的 。 這些分子 , 特別是甲烷和乙烷 , 可以是土衛六溫度的液體 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是要讓土衛六的水變成地球 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	在大氣層中 , 它是可以被凝聚的 , 所以認知到這個情況 , 帶到一個怪異的世界 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 好 , 在這些雲層上 , 上方有數百公里的霧霾 , 它能防止任何陽光進入表面 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度是攝氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但儘管冰冷 , 你可能會在土衛六表面下雨 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上 , 雨是如何在地球上運作的:它會雕刻吉利 ; 它會形成河流和凱塔 ; 它能創造峽谷 ; 它能在大盆地和隕石中聚集 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把黏液從高山頂上沖下山丘 , 落到低地 。 所以停下來思考一下 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六表面會是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 。 鐵達尼號的高峰 , 和地球上的深度地球一樣黑暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	它很冷 , 很壞 , 很糟糕 , 可能會下雨 , 你可能會站在密西根湖邊邊 , 和油漆薄板一樣 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們和卡西尼一起到達前的土衛六的表面 , 我可以告訴你們 , 我們在土衛六發現的 , 雖然細節不一樣 , 每一點都和那個故事一樣令人著迷 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像卡西尼人──它就像是一名青少年的冒險 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有厚厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這張照片是titan , 背著太陽 , 光環是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	另外一個月球--我甚至不知道它是哪一個 。 它是非常廣闊的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號的儀器可以透過大氣層看到表面 , 我的攝影機系統是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你看到的是明亮又暗的區域 , 大約是它為我們抵達的距離 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這真是太神奇了:我們無法弄清楚我們在泰坦看到的是什麼 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你仔細看這個區域 , 你會開始看到一些我們不知道的無數通道 。 你可以看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	我們後來發現 , 事實上 , 一個隕石坑 , 但土衛六表面上有很少的隕石坑 , 意思是 , 它是個很年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來像是地形 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來就像被拉開一樣 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你在一個星球上看到任何線性 , 就表示已經有破裂 , 像個錯 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以 , 已經在結構上有了改變 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 發生了一件事件 , 許多人認為卡西尼的調查是土衛六的 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那就是呼吸探測器的部署 , 歐洲燃燒的呼吸探測器 , 橫跨太陽系七年 。 我們將它部署到土衛六的大氣層 , 花了2.5個小時 , 才會下降 , 然後它落在地表 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我想強調這個事件有多麼重要 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它第一次登陸在外太陽系 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	在我心中 , 這件事非常顯著 , 這事件應該要和美國和歐洲各個城市的陳述遊行一起慶祝 , 不幸的是 , 這並不是事實 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這是另外一個原因 。 這是國際的使命 , 這事件在歐洲、德國都慶祝 , 而慶祝的簡報是用英語、美國口音、德語、法語、義大利語和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	它是一個關於 「 聯合國 」 所謂的真實聯合體示範的示範:一個真正的聯合國加入一個極為好的努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 它很巨大地在探索一個星球 , 漸漸了解一個行星系統 , 對於所有人類歷史來說 , 這種行星系統是無法接觸的 , 現在人類已經觸過它了 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我開始開始開始談起雞皮疙瘩 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是極大的情感事件 , 我個人永遠不會忘記 , 而你也不應該 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	總之 , 探測器在下沉的路上測量了大氣層 , 它也拍了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 看到探測器表面的第一張圖片 。 這是我們看到的景象 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這真是令人震驚 , 因為我們希望其他的照片都能從軌道上拍下來 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	這是一個不明確的模式 , 一個地質模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是一種只由液體流動而形成的趨勢 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以追蹤這些頻道 , 你可以看到它們的結合 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們把這條通道結合成這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是液體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這是海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里拍的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片是在八公里拍的 , 好嗎 ? 同樣的 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里大概是航空高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要穿越美國的飛機旅行 , 你會飛到這些高度 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是你在泰坦航空的窗戶 , 飛越泰坦的表面 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器在表面留下 , 我要給你們看 , 女士們先生們 , 第一張從外太陽系的月球表面拍的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是冰塊 , 是嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很明顯地 , 它降落在一個平坦、黑暗的區域 , 且它沒有從視覺下沉 。 所以我們降落的不是液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器基本上就是土衛六的平面 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一個沒有安慰的地面 , 充滿了液態甲烷 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是因為這種材料已經從土衛六的高地上沖下 , 穿過我們看到的這些管道 , 已經耗盡了數十億年 , 來填滿低窪的盆地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是呼吸探測器登陸的原因 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但是 , 我們的影像中仍然沒有標誌 , 或甚至充氣的影像 , 任何大型、開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 會變得更困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們在土衛六赤道地區的電影 , 展示這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘高達100公尺 , 被幾公里高 , 它們延伸了幾英里和里程數 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	數百英里的沙丘高達一千到一千兩百英里 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	很顯然 , 這是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或者你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 再次 , 這個問題讓我感到困惑 , 沒有液體 , 直到最後 , 我們在極地看到湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	在泰坦南極地的南極地有一個湖 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大約是安大略湖的大小 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	接著 , 大約一週半前 , 我們飛越了土衛六北極 , 再次發現 , 我們發現了像卡西亞海一樣大的特徵 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	看來這些液體 , 是因為我們不明白的原因 , 至少在這個季節 , 都顯然是在土衛六的極地 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意 , 我們發現泰坦是個很了不起、神秘的地方 。 它很奇怪 , 但卻是外星人 , 但卻有像地球一樣的地質形態 , 和一個很棒的地理多樣性 , 一個很棒的世界 , 在太陽系中 , 只有太陽系的複雜性和豐富性才是地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們去了土衛二 。 土衛二是一顆小月 , 大約是土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以看到在英格蘭旁邊 , 只為了讓你看到它的大小 。 這不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二非常白 , 它非常亮 , 它的表面很明顯地被破裂了 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是一種非常地質活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二發現的母親在南極發現了發現 , 我們正在研究南極 , 在那裡找到了破裂的系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們是被覆蓋的 。 這些碎片是用有機物質覆蓋的 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個區域 , 南極地區 , 都升高了溫度 。 它是地球上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這很奇怪 , 發現地球上的南極比熱帶更熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們拍攝額外的照片時 , 我們發現 , 從這些碎片中 , 會引發好的噴射機 , 冰粒會延伸數百英里到太空 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把這張照片塗上顏色 , 將微弱的光線帶出來 , 我們看到這些噴射會餵飽水平 , 事實上 , 在其他的圖像中 , 將數千英里的距離傳到土衛二上方的太空 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我的團隊和我研究了像這樣的圖片 , 像這張圖片 , 並思考了卡西尼的其他結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到的結論是 , 這些噴射噴射可能從土衛二表面下噴發液態水 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以 , 我們可能有液態水、有機材料和過熱 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能偶然發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 也就是說 , 一個適合生物生存的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我想我不需要告訴你們 , 在我們的太陽系中發現生命 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學影響 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明基因的出現 , 不是一次 , 而是兩次獨立地發生在我們的太陽系中 , 那就意味著 , 根據推論 , 它發生了很驚人的次數 , 遍及宇宙的137億年 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球也是我們所知的唯一一個行星 , 充滿生命 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它是獨一無二的 , 到目前為止 , 我們唯一認識的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們當中有任何人在1960年代時 , 都原諒你 , 如果你不是 , 那你就會記得1968年阿波羅8號太空人拍的這張非常有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次 , 地球是從太空拍攝出來的 , 它對我們在宇宙中的位置有著巨大的影響 , 我們對地球的保護有責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	我們在卡西尼首次拍了一張相當於人眼的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是太陽的全食 , 從土星的另一側看到 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張不太美麗的照片中 , 你可以看到由太陽的主要光環 , 你看到了太陽的折射影像 , 你看到了這個環 , 事實上 , 由土衛二的排放 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但就好像那還不夠厲害 , 我們可以在這個美麗的圖像中發現 , 我們自己的星球 , 在土星光環的手臂上爬行 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有一些深刻的動作 , 深深地影響著我們自己 , 捕捉到我們的小藍色的星球 , 在其他世界的天空中 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而我們從中獲得的這個觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這半個世紀前開始的發現中得到最好的獎賞 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	在2005年 , 只有15%的世界被繪製出來 。 這慢慢地 , 在災難發生後 , 隱藏了未經使用的土地和未知道路的經濟潛力 。 在這短短的演講中 , 谷歌的卡特加德展示地圖 , 全球各地的一群人繪製了地圖來繪製世界的地圖 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、科技、
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	最近的卡特加達:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟體 , 建立經濟體 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	在2008年 , 颶風納利斯遭到毀滅性的緬甸人 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人需要幫助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要趕人和供應到這個區域 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有辦法幫助到cyclone受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看到洛杉磯或倫敦地圖時 , 很難相信到2005年 , 世界上只有15%被描繪成地理細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國對世界多數人面臨的問題:沒有細節地圖 。
but help was coming .	但 , 救援已經來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在谷歌 , 40名義工使用新的軟體來繪製十二萬公里的道路、三千間醫院、物流和救援點 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? google繪圖機 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	google地圖製造商是一項技術 , 讓我們每個人都能繪製我們所知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這種軟體來繪製每樣東西 , 從道路到河流 , 從學校到當地企業 , 影片商店到角落商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名赫南多•蘇托認識到大部分的開發中國家的經濟升遷的關鍵 , 就是利用大量的未知土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	例如 , 僅僅在印度 , 一兆美元的房地產仍然未被過時 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是去年 , 在170個國家 , 數以千計的使用者就繪製了數百萬個資訊 , 創造了一幅細節的地圖 , 從來沒有被認為是可行的 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這使得熱情使用者的力量到處可見 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	現在讓我們看看一些使用者所創造的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 正如我們所說的 , 在170個國家 , 人們正在繪製世界的地圖 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的橋樑 , 剛在塞內加爾畫了一條路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	離家更近 , chalua , 班加羅爾的n.g路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何、手勢辨識、機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以百計城市使用者的勝利 , 一個使用者 , 一次編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是我們未開發的地球70%的邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村落的布德魯斯村落在十個月的非暴力抗議活動中阻止一道障礙 , 橫跨他們的橄欖園 。 你聽說過嗎 ? 巴西的電影製片人朱利亞•巴查查亞問我們為什麼只關注以色列衝突 , 而不是非暴力的領導人 , 有一天會帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	朱利亞巴查亞:注意非暴力的注意 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去八年 , 我致力於記錄以色列和巴勒斯坦人的工作 , 他們試圖用和平的手段來結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我和歐洲及美國的作品一起旅行時 , 總有一個問題出現了:巴勒斯坦的甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我面臨的挑戰是 , 我常常從中東回來 , 在那裡 , 我花了數十個巴勒斯坦人拍攝 , 他們用非暴力來保護他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和定居者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人正試著要打造一個巨大的國家非暴力運動 , 終止職業 , 並在該地區建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 在座大部分的人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種分裂在國外發生的地面和感知之間 , 是我們尚未成功的巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動的關鍵原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	今天我來到這裡 , 談到注意力的力量、注意力的力量、以及非暴力運動在西岸、加薩和其他地方的崛起和發展 , 但今天 , 我的案例研究將成為巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 最少沒有暴力的不是巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力行為 , 而是讓我們開始注意那些已經有的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我用布德魯斯把你帶到這個村莊來說明這個點 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨滅絕 , 因為以色列宣佈它會建造一個隔離障礙 , 其中一部分則會在村落上蓋 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 被包圍 , 所以他們會失去自由 , 到其他的西岸 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地領導者的靈感 , 他們發起了和平的抗爭活動 , 來阻止這種事發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你看一些短片 , 所以你有一種感覺 , 在地面上看起來是什麼樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女人:我們被告知牆會和以色列分開巴勒斯坦 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德魯斯 , 我們發現牆會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列人:柵欄事實上 , 創造出恐怖的解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男人:今天你受邀參加和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被數十個以色列兄弟姊妹加入 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列行動主義者:沒有什麼比非暴力反對者更嚇人 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女人:我們看到男人試圖推動士兵 , 但沒有人能那樣做 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔•派對:我們必須忽略傳統思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯•派對:我們是完整的和諧 , 我們想要把它散播到巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	聊天:聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔、哈馬斯 , 和流行的前面 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞主持人:柵欄的凝塊持續著 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被送去散播群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男人:這些是活的子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就像是費拉雅 , 到處射擊 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列行動主義者:我確信我們都死了 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊 , 還有其他人甚至不喜歡牛 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗議不會阻止暴行 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	蛋白:這是一場和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	溝通:我們能做到 ! 我們能做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱利亞•巴赫亞:我第一次聽到布德魯斯的故事時 , 我很驚訝國際媒體並沒有報導七年前發生的非凡事件 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是 , 布德魯斯成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民 , 經過10個月的和平抗爭 , 說服以色列政府將土地上的障礙移到綠線上 , 也就是國際識別以色列和巴勒斯坦領土之間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德魯斯的抗藥性已經在西岸散播到村莊 , 散播到耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體卻對這些故事保持沉默 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默造成嚴重的後果 , 導致非暴力的可能性成長 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦存活 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭共有的共通點 , 兩者都是一種劇院 , 尋求觀眾的原因 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一不斷地被封鎖並吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦的議題 , 那對非暴力的領導者來說 , 要對他們的社區做出訴訟是可行的選擇 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能不會讓房間裡的父母感到驚訝 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓你的孩子更大聲地投擲你的孩子 , 最好的方式就是讓他第一次關注他丟掉球體 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	蟻巢會變成幼兒心理學家所謂的 「 功能性行為 」 , 因為嬰兒知道他能從中獲得父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以鼓勵或貶低行為 , 只因為給予或讓孩子們注意力 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成人來說也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為會受到影響 , 取決於國際社會選擇專注在哪裡 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 終結中東的衝突 , 帶動和平的核心 , 是要把非暴力行為轉變成一種功能性行為 , 讓現今在地面上更加關注非暴力的領導者 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在我拍攝電影的過程中 , 在西岸、加薩和東耶路撒冷的村莊裡 , 我看到即使是一部紀錄片 , 也會影響到轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫瓦拉賈的村子裡 , 離耶路撒冷很近 , 社區正面臨類似布德魯斯的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被圍繞著 , 失去很多土地 , 沒有機會 , 不論是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	兩年來 , 他們一直在使用非暴力 , 但從沒人注意到他們就越來越不滿了 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了一個螢幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後 , 他們舉辦了最好的示範和示範 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民 , 看著布德魯斯的故事 , 覺得電影中確實有人在追蹤他們所做的事 , 有人在乎 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列 , 有一種新的和平運動叫做索里達里ot , 也就是希伯來的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導人把布德魯斯當作主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告說 , 以色列人從來沒有活躍過 , 看電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	華拉賈和索利達里特運動的例子顯示 , 即使是一部小型的獨立電影 , 也可以扮演一個角色 , 將非暴力轉變成一種功能行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在 , 想像一下 , 大媒體玩家的力量 , 如果他們開始報導每週非暴力的示威 , 在村落發生 , 比如比利、尼林、瓦拉 , 在耶路撒冷的鄰里 , 比如希克•賈拉和史瓦 , 非暴力的領導人會變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效率 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是看不見的 , 就好像它們從來沒有發生過一樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我親眼見識過 , 如果我們能做到 , 他們就會乘上去 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果它們的數量會增加 , 它們的影響力會在以色列巴勒斯坦衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響力終於可以解開這種情況 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人已經證明非暴力是可行的 , 在像布德魯斯這樣的地方 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們把注意力交給他們 , 讓他們可以證明它在任何地方運作 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•桑克有個簡單但有力的領導力的模式 , 全都從黃金圓和 「 為什麼 」 開始 , 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁•路德金 , 以及萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye , 企業 , 企業 , 領導者 , 銷售 , 銷售 , 成功 , 成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	simonsinek:偉大的領導者啟發了行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當事情不像我們假設的那樣 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好的 , 你要如何解釋當其他人能夠實現一些看似反對的假設 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果如此有創意 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們比所有的競爭都更創新 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的才華、相同的機構、相同的顧問、相同的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那麼 , 為什麼他們似乎有不同之處 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁•路德•金恩帶領民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受苦的人 , 他肯定不是一天中唯一的偉大演說者 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能想出控制權 , 強權的人飛行 , 尤其是其他隊伍 , 他們更有資格 , 更有資格......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有完成人類飛行 , 萊特兄弟打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有別的玩法 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前我發現了一項發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這項發現深深地改變了我對世界運作的方式 , 它甚至深深地改變了我運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有的偉大、鼓舞人心的領導人和組織 , 不論是蘋果、馬丁•路德•金、或萊特兄弟 , 他們都認為 , 採取行動 , 以同樣的方式溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	這完全和其他人完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是把它編碼 , 可能是世界上最簡單的點子 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱之為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 什麼 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導人能夠鼓舞其他人不在哪裡 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	地球上每一個人 , 每一個組織都知道自己在做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們是怎麼做到的 , 不論你稱之為 「 分化價值觀 」 、 「 屬性過程 」 或 「 usp 」 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或組織知道他們為什麼要做這些事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	所謂的 「 為什麼 」 , 我指的不是 「 賺錢 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這就是結果 。 結果永遠是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	我指的是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的原因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	你的組織為什麼存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎呢 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	因此 , 我們思考的方式 , 我們行動的方式 , 我們溝通的方式是從外面來的 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很明顯的 , 我們從最清楚的東西到最模糊的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但啟發的領導人和激勵人心的組織不論他們的規模大小 , 不論他們的產業都認為 , 採取行動和溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果是因為它們很容易理解 , 每個人都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果和其他人一樣 , 來自它們的行銷訊息聽起來會像這樣: 「 我們會做出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 很容易使用和使用者友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	大部分的行銷都是這樣做 , 大部分的銷售都是這樣做 , 我們大部分的人交流的人際關係 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們所做的事 , 我們會說我們是如何變得更好 , 我們期待某種行為、購買、投票 , 諸如此類的 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是為我們的客戶做事 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很大的氣體流程 , 它有皮革座位 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果實際上是這樣溝通的 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的方式思考 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是把我們的產品設計得很漂亮 , 簡單的使用和使用者友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛好是用電腦做好事 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不同的是吧 ? 你準備好要從我身上買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的就是反轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明人們不會買你做什麼 , 人們會買你為什麼這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每個人都很舒服從蘋果購買一台電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也很自在地買蘋果的mp3播放器 , 或蘋果的手機 , 或蘋果的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 就像我之前說的 , 蘋果只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼可以區別它們的競爭者 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭對手都一樣有資格去做這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway發表了平面電視 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很明顯可以做平面電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們多年來都在做平面螢幕 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	演員是mp3播放器和pdas , 他們製作了很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以做出完美的設計產品 , 沒有人買 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到這件事 , 我們甚至無法想像從現場購買mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會從電腦公司買mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標並不是要跟你所擁有的所有人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最好的部分是:沒有一個我告訴你的是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	全都在生物學的手段 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學、生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看看人類大腦的交叉處 , 從上往下看 , 你看到的是人類的大腦被分解成三個主要元件 , 與黃金圈完全相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦、我們的智人大腦、我們的新皮層 , 和 「 什麼 」 層面相對應 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層負責我們所有的理性、分析思考和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間的兩個部分構成我們的邊緣大腦 , 我們的邊緣大腦負責我們所有的感受 , 比如信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類行為、所有決策 , 且它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面的溝通 , 是的 , 人們可以了解大量複雜的資訊 , 比如特徵、利益、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它不會驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們從內部傳遞訊息時 , 我們直接對控制行為的大腦說話 , 接著 , 我們允許人們將它合理化 , 用我們所說和做的事 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是腸道決策的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	有時候你會給某人所有的事實和數據 , 他們會說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節都說了什麼 , 但這感覺不對勁 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們要用這個動詞 , 它不會 「 感覺 」 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的大腦部位無法控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們最好能忍受的就是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者有時候你會說你帶著你的心臟 , 或者你帶著你的靈魂 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭把它打破 , 那些不是身體的部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你的邊緣大腦中 , 控制決策而非語言的部分 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道你為什麼要做你所做的事 , 人們會回應你為什麼要做你所做的事 , 那你要如何讓人們投票給你 , 或從你身上買東西 , 更重要的是 , 忠誠 , 想要成為你所做的事的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是要賣給需要你所擁有的人 ; 目標是要賣給那些相信你所相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是僱用需要工作的人 ; 而是僱用相信你所相信的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 如果你聘用人 , 只因為他們能做一份工作 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用你相信的人 , 他們會用血、汗水和淚水來工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有什麼比萊特兄弟更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人都不知道samuelpierpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	在二十世紀早期 , 追求人類飛行的追求 , 就像白天的網路com 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley , 我們假設成功的方案 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我是說 , 即使你現在問人們: 「 你的產品或公司為什麼會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給予你相同的三件事:被大量化、錯誤的人、不好的市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	一直都是相同的三件事 , 讓我們來探討一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley得到了五萬美金 , 由戰爭部門來計算飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	金錢是沒有問題的 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛辦公室工作 , 在史密森尼工作 , 當時他知道所有人的腦袋 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他僱用了最好的思維金錢 , 能找到市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處跟著他 , 每個人都在為拉ngley起源 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼 , 為什麼我們從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英哩遠在俄亥俄州 , 奧維爾和威爾布萊特 , 他們沒有我們認為的成功方法 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 ; 他們用自行車店裡的腳踏車來支付夢想 ; 沒有一個人在萊特兄弟的團隊裡 , 受過大學教育 , 甚至是歐威爾或威爾堡 ; 紐約時報跟著他們走 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別是 , 奧維爾和威爾堡是由一個目標所驅動的 , 由一個目的 , 一個信念驅動 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能找出飛行器 , 就會改變世界的軌跡 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不一樣 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要變得富有 , 他想要有名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他追求富人 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟夢想的人 , 和他們一起工作 , 帶著血、汗水、淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	另外一些人只為付款工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們會說故事 , 每次萊特兄弟出櫃時 , 他們會拿出五組零件 , 因為那是他們會墜機的幾次 , 在他們進來之前 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最終 , 1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟起飛 , 沒有人去體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後我們就發現了 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證明 , 蘭利受到錯誤的動機:那天萊特兄弟去飛 , 他放棄了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可能會說: 「 那真是個驚人的發現 , 各位 , 我會改善你的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一個 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他放棄了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的 , 你就會吸引那些相信你所相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引那些相信你所相信的人是很重要的 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	一種叫做創新的傳播法則 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對知道術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	人口的前2.5%是創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%是早期採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你的早期 , 絕大多數是你的遲到 , 和你們的喉頭 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買到觸控電話的唯一原因是你不再買輪子電話了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在不同時間的不同時間點 , 但創新的散播法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場成功或大眾市場接受這個想法 , 直到你達成了這個臨界點 , 只有15%到18%的市場滲透 , 然後系統就開始 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你對新企業的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡跟你說: 「 喔 , 這大約是10% 。 」 很驕傲的 。
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以超過10%的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們大約有百分之十的人只是 「 了解 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們如何描述它們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	這就像是那種直覺 , 「 喔 , 他們就懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要如何在你做生意之前找到它 , 而不是那些不懂的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以 , 在這裡 , 你必須關閉的這個小差距 , 如同jefreymoore所說的 , 「 過馬峰 」 , 因為 , 你看 , 早期的多數人 , 不會嘗試任何事 , 直到有人先試過 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新者和早期採用者 , 他們很自在地做出這些直覺決策 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更自在地做出那些直覺的決策 , 由他們對世界的信念所驅動 , 而不只是產品可用 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人排隊排了六個小時才買到iphone , 當他們第一次出櫃時 , 你才剛走進店裡 , 然後在店裡買了一個 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人一開始就花了四萬美金在平面電視上 , 雖然這項技術是次等的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便說一下 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為這項技術太棒了 , 他們自己做了 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	那是因為他們想要成為第一位 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 , 你所做的就是證明你所相信的 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做那些證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	前六個小時 , 拿iphone購買iphone的原因 , 排了六個小時 , 是因為他們對這個世界的信念 , 以及他們希望每個人看到的:他們是第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我給你們一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗 , 以及一個有名的成功 , 關於創新的散播法則 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 知名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是一個商業的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	正如我們之前所說的 , 第二 , 成功的食譜是金錢、對的人、對的市場條件 , 對吧 ? 你應該成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從八、九年前 , tivo出版的那天起 , 它們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手下 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們是非常富裕的 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當作動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我總是在垃圾時間華納的dvr上做tivo 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是個商業上的失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺到錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們去ipo時 , 他們的股票是大約30到40美金 , 然後爆炸了 , 而且從來沒有交易過10 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它甚至在六歲以上交易 , 除了幾條小插頭 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有種可以暫停現場電視、滑雪廣告、現場電視的產品 , 記住你的觀看習慣 , 甚至不問你 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	憤世嫉俗大多說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 。 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你害怕我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種喜歡完全控制你生活的人們 , 天哪 , 我們有一項產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場電視、跳過廣告 , 記住你的觀點 , 等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 , 而你所做的就是證明你所相信的 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你們一個成功的例子 , 說明創新的散播法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天 , 有25萬人出現在華盛頓的購物中心 , 去聽金恩博士演講 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有送出任何邀請 , 沒有網站來檢查日期 。
how do you do that ?	該怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	嗯 , 金恩博士不是美國唯一一個偉大的演說員 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是唯一在美國受過早期權利困擾的人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很糟 。
but he had a gift .	但他有個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們在美國需要什麼改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處走動 , 告訴人們他所相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 。 」 他告訴人們 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	相信他所相信的理由的人 , 讓自己成為自己的理想 , 他們告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創造了結構 , 讓更多人知道 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	當時有25萬人出現在對的時間 , 聽他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人來找他 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為自己出席 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們所相信的美國 , 讓他們在巴士旅行了八個小時 , 在八月中時站在華盛頓 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人和白人:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信世上有兩種法律:由高權威組成的 , 以及由人類組成的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	除非所有由人類製造出來的法律 , 都和較高權威制定的法律一致 , 否則我們生活在一個公平的世界裡 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛好 , 公民權利運動是幫助他帶來生命的完美 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們跟著 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順便說一下 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在傾聽政治人物 , 他們的全面12點計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有啟發任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者有權力或權威的位置 , 但領導者鼓舞了我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們遵守領導者 , 不是因為我們必須這麼做 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們追隨那些領導者 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	正是那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 他們有能力鼓舞周圍的人 , 或找到啟發他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你要如何記得你在哪裡停車 ? 你怎麼知道你在正確的方向移動 ? 神經科學家尼爾•尼爾研究我們周圍的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學、科學、科學、科學、
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	尼爾•布爾斯:你的大腦如何告訴你你身在何處 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們停在一個大停車場時 , 我們要如何記住我們車子的位置 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	問題來了荷馬 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們會試著了解他的大腦到底發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬體開始 , 黃色代表記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你在那裡受損 , 比如阿茲海默症 , 你就無法記住一些東西 , 包括你停車的地方 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它的名字是拉丁文的 「 海主 」 , 類似海主的名字 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像大腦的其他部分 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人類的大腦有大約一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元彼此溝通 , 藉由傳送小脈衝或脈衝 , 透過彼此連結來傳遞電訊號 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片細胞組成 , 非常密集的相互連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的藉由記錄老鼠或老鼠的個別神經元在覓食或探索環境中尋找食物
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	想像一下 , 我們從這隻老鼠的海馬體的一個神經元記錄下來 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發電時 , 就會有一個紅點和點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	我們看到的是 , 這個神經元知道當老鼠進入特定的環境時 , 就會知道這個神經元的存在 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它會透過發送電擊傳送到大腦的其他部位訊號 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以我們可以顯示神經元的激發率 , 作為動物所在位置的函數 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從不同神經元中記錄 , 我們會看到不同的神經元在動物的不同部位時 , 會發出不同的神經元 , 比如這個正方形的盒子 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 它們結合在一起 , 為其餘的大腦進行一張地圖 , 不斷地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	在那裡 , 人類也被記錄下來 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時需要腦部監控的電活動
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人在玩電玩遊戲 , 他們開車開車到一個小鎮 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	海馬體內的細胞會被激發 , 會被活躍地發送電脈衝 , 每當它們開車穿過一個特定的小鎮 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 一個位置細胞怎麼知道老鼠或人在其環境裡的位置 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們環境的界線特別重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	所以最上面的那張圖就像是把老鼠的箱子的牆壁打開一樣 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你把盒子擴大時 , 激發的位置就會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的一面 , 每當有一面牆靠近南方 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放在盒子裡 , 細胞就會在兩個位置上開火 , 不論在哪裡 , 都會有一面牆到南邊 , 當動物在盒子裡探索時 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這預測了 , 感測到你周圍的界線和邊界的距離和方向 , 特別對海馬體來說是很重要的 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在海馬體的輸入中 , 細胞會被發現進入海馬體 , 以特定的距離來偵測邊界或邊緣 , 以觀察老鼠或老鼠的方向 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的細胞會發射 , 當動物靠近一面牆或東邊的邊界時 , 不論是方塊的邊緣或圓形的圍牆 , 或甚至是桌邊的邊緣 , 動物會跑來跑去 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞會發射 , 當南邊有邊界時 , 不論是桌邊的邊緣 , 或牆壁 , 或甚至是兩張桌子之間的縫隙 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	這就是我們認為位置細胞會決定動物在哪裡 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也能測試我們認為物體在哪裡 , 比如這個目標國旗 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或你的車子在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以 , 我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看到他們必須記住的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	接著 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 它們很擅長把標記放在他們認為旗幟或車子的地方 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在一些實驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和尺寸 , 就像我們用位置細胞一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在這個例子中 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟的位置是如何改變的 , 因為你如何改變環境的形狀和尺寸 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 舉例來說 , 如果旗幟在一個小平方的環境中交叉的地方 , 然後如果你問問那些人在哪裡 , 但你把環境變大 , 他們認為旗幟已經被伸展到完全一樣的地方 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	彷彿你記得旗幟的位置 , 藉由儲存你位置細胞的位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 藉由移動到那個位置 , 這樣你就可以最好符合你位置細胞的激發模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那引導你回到你想要記住的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們在哪裡進行動作 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 如果我們採取一些外在的路徑 , 也許我們停車了 , 我們就會知道 , 因為我們自己的動作 , 我們可以整合這條路徑 , 大約是前進的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也得到這種整合的輸入方式 , 來自一種叫做網格細胞的細胞 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	現在 , 網格細胞在海馬迴輸入的輸入中 , 它們有點像位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每個細胞會在不同的地點開火 , 這些地點在整個環境中形成了驚人的三角形格子 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從不同顏色的數個格狀細胞記錄 , 每一個顏色都有類似激發的模式 , 每個細胞的格狀圖案都和其他細胞有稍微相似 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	這張格子上的紅色的螢幕上有綠色的 , 上面的藍色是這個 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 這就像老鼠可以把一個虛擬的網格放到它的環境中 , 就像你在地圖上看到的緯度和長度線 , 但用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它移動時 , 電活動可以從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 來追蹤它的位置 , 這樣它就可以利用它自己的動作來知道它在環境的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	有人有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	由於所有類似激發的圖案 , 都有相同的對稱軸 , 相同的網格 , 在橘色的圖像中顯示 , 大腦的網格活動應該根據這六個方向的方向來改變 , 或在六個方向之間運行 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放進mri掃描儀 , 讓他們做個電玩遊戲 , 像我剛給你們看的那個 , 尋找這個信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你確實在人類的腦皮層中看到了電網細胞 , 和老鼠的腦部一樣 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他車子的距離和方向 , 到他停車的地方 , 將建築和邊界擴展 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	它會被邊界偵測細胞的激發所代表 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從汽車公園中走出來的路 , 在格子細胞激發的路上 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	這兩種細胞都能讓位置細胞發射 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回到他移動的地方 , 找到最好的匹配位置 , 讓他現在停在他大腦中的位置 , 讓他停在車子的位置 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	那引導他回到視覺暗示的位置 , 不論他的車在哪裡 。
maybe it's been towed .	可能是被綁架了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去拿它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們尋找整個大腦的這種類似激發模式的圖形 , 我們會在一系列的位置中看到 , 當我們做各種自動記憶任務時 , 總是會主動地發現 , 比如 , 當你上次去婚禮時 , 例如 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 我們身邊的空間 , 神經機制也被用來產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們才能重新創造出空間的場景 , 至少 , 當我們想要想像的時候 , 那些事件發生在我們身上 。
