so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以如果發生了這事 , 你的記憶可以從細胞的位置開始 , 透過這些密集的連接來激活彼此 , 然後啟動邊界細胞 , 創造你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以透過這個空間來移動這個視野 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種我還沒提到的細胞頭部方向盤 , 根據你面對的方向 , 它們就像是羅盤 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義你想要產生視覺影像的視覺方向 , 例如你在婚禮時 , 想像發生了什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是認知神經科學的一個新時代的一個例子 , 我們開始了解心理的過程 , 例如你如何記憶、想像 , 或甚至在腦中產生的數十億個神經元 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝各位 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 由軍事機構、政府、私營部門和大眾合作驅動的全球安全 。 這不僅僅是開源粉絲的遙遠期希望 , 是詹姆士斯•斯特里迪迪迪迪斯的願景 , 納斯托的最高指揮官 , 他在近期的軍事史上共享過的時刻 , 來解釋為何未來的安全應該用橋樑來建造 , 而不是用牆 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開源、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•斯特瓦里迪斯:納多最高層級的指揮官如何看待全球安全 ?
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我會談到開源安全 , 因為在21世紀 , 我們必須要更安全 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先回顧二十世紀 , 看看這個安全是如何運作的 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 一個在法國的戰場 , 就在北方的納多總部 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	1916年 , 在verdun , 超過三百天 , 七十萬人死亡 , 每天大約兩千人 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你把它推向二十世紀的安全 , 推進第二次世界大戰 , 你會看到三百天 , 兩百萬人被殺害 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 我們繼續建造牆 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的戰線 , 到第二次世界大戰的巨線 , 接著我們進入冷戰 , 鐵幕 , 柏林牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的論點是 , 不要建造牆來創造安全 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲著名的橋樑 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	它是一座橋 , 穿越了德林亞河 , 小說的主題是ivoandri奇的 , 它談到如何在歐洲和巴爾幹半島的一部分 , 長久以來 , 已經有了巨大的牆 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 在過去的十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 猶豫地 , 聚集在一起 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我會說 , 開放式安全是要把國際、國際、私人公共事聯繫起來 , 並將它和戰略溝通聯繫在一起 , 主要是在社交網路上 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	讓我來談談為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球公有物受到各式各樣的攻擊 , 沒有威脅到全球公有物的來源會被建築牆解決 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	很顯然 , 我是個水手 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一條線 , 穿過印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	旁邊有音樂廳電線 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	那就是防止海盜攻擊 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	海盜是現今非常積極的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	盜版在馬拉卡的草地上也是非常活躍的 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	它活躍在幾內亞灣 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到它 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	它是全球交通系統中十億美金的不連續性 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 在這個時候 , 有20艘船 , 500艘船員被控告 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要考慮如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	咱們換成另一種海洋 , 網路大海 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這是兩個年輕人的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	目前 , 他們被監禁了 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一套信用卡詐欺 , 讓他們賺超過一百億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 它是全球經濟的2兆美金的2兆美金不連續性 。
two trillion a year .	一年兩兆 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是英國的國內生產總值 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以 , 我們所知道的網路海洋是激進式開放的基礎 , 也受到很大的威脅 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	在全球公有物中 , 我擔心的另一件事 , 就是人口販賣所帶來的威脅 , 由毒品、鴉片所造成的 , 從阿富汗到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心來自安地河脊的古柯鹼 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器和販賣 。 最重要的是 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 以及它的代價 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	人口販賣主要在海上移動 , 但在全球公有物的其他部分 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴你們 , 這是一個非常高科技的美國海軍裝備 , 用來阻止人口販運 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是由毒品汽車所經營的半潛水器 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它是在南美的叢林裡建造的 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用那個低科技的木筏捕捉到它 , 它帶著六噸的古柯鹼 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個組員 。 精密的溝通都打掃了 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種販賣、毒品、人類、武器、上帝禁止大規模破壞的武器 , 是對全球公有物的威脅之一 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	讓我們現在在阿富汗團結起來 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的波普市 。
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	全世界80%到90%的粉末鴉片和海洛因來自阿富汗
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	當然 , 我們也看到恐怖主義 。
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這是基地組織的起始點 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到一個非常強力的緊急狀況 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以 , 這種恐怖主義也是全球公有物的一部分 , 我們必須處理的 。
so here we are , 21st century .	所以 , 我們現在是21世紀 。
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道20世紀的工具行不通 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我認為我們不會只從槍的桶子裡提供安全 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不會只從槍的桶裡提供安全 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這樣做時 , 我們必須做得很好 , 並且有能力 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 開放式安全是關於國際、國際、私人的連結 , 透過網路上的策略性溝通的概念 , 拼湊在一起 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子 , 說明這如何用正面的方式運作 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 。 這些是阿富汗士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都拿著書 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這很奇怪 。 我想我讀到這個人口統計數字 , 年輕男女在20和30年代 , 大部分都是在阿富汗的文盲 。 」
you would be correct .	你是對的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	當他們進入阿富汗安全部隊時 , 85%的人看不到 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為塔利班在這些男人和女人的時期會學會閱讀 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	所以問題是 , 為什麼他們都站在那裡拿著書 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們教導他們在讀識字課程 , 由nato和私營企業合作 , 和發展機構合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們教導了超過二十萬阿富汗安全部隊 , 以基本的層級來閱讀和寫 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你在阿富汗讀和寫的時候 , 你通常會把一支筆放在口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在儀式中 , 當這些年輕男女畢業時 , 她們用很棒的驕傲把筆放在口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	這正是國際聯盟有50個國家參與這項使命聯盟這些發展機構 , 私人公開 , 來處理這種安全 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	當然 , 我們也教導他們對抗技能 , 但我認為 , 開放式安全意味著以創造更長的保安效應的方式連結 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	它叫做舒適感 。
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有一艘姐妹船叫做慈悲 。
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院船 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	這個 , 舒適的 , 在加勒比海和南美海岸進行病人治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	通常他們會做四十萬個病人治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	它並不是嚴格的由軍隊組成 , 而是由人道主義組織組成:營運希望、微笑計劃 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織會派遣義工 。
interagency physicians come out .	內科醫生出櫃了 。
they're all part of this .	他們全部都參與其中 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	舉個例子 , 這個小男孩 , 八歲 , 跟著他的母親走兩天來到舒適的眼科診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他結合時 , 眼睛突然抬頭說: 「 媽媽 , 埃爾米諾 。 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽媽 , 我看到世界 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	將它乘上40萬名病人治療 , 這個私人的合作和安全部隊的合作 , 你開始看到創造安全的力量 , 以非常不同的方式 。
here you see baseball players .	這裡是棒球選手 。
can you pick out the two us army soldiers in this photograph ?	你能在這張照片中挑出兩位美國軍人士嗎 ?
they are the two young men on either side of these young boys . this is part of a series of baseball clinics , where we have explored collaboration between major league baseball , the department of state , who sets up the diplomatic piece of this , military baseball players , who are real soldiers with real skills but participate in this mission , and they put on clinics throughout latin america and the caribbean , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all of the central american and caribbean nations where baseball is so popular , and it creates security .	他們是這兩位小男孩的兩個年輕人 。 這是一系列的棒球診所 , 我們在大聯盟棒球聯盟 , 國家部門 , 設立了外交球隊 , 軍事棒球員 , 他們是真正的士兵 , 但他們參與了這個任務 , 他們在整個美國和加勒比海岸 , 全美各地的拉丁美洲和加勒比亞 , 在各地 , 都在巴黎巴黎 , 創造了海灣 。
it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它向年輕男性和女性展現了榜樣 , 關於健身和生活的榜樣 , 我會爭論 , 為我們創造安全 。
another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	另一方面的合作關係是在災難救援 。
this is a us air force helicopter participating after the tsunami in 2004 which killed 250 , 000 people .	這是美國空軍直升機在2004年被海嘯殺害了25萬人 。
in each of these major disasters — the tsunami in 2004 , 250 , 000 dead , the kashmiri earthquake in pakistan , 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , about 300 , 000 dead , more recently the awful earthquaketsunami combination which struck japan and its nuclear industry — in all of these instances , we see partnerships between international actors , interagency , privatepublic working with security forces to respond to this kind of natural disaster .	在這些大災難中 , 海嘯在2004年、25萬人死亡 , 巴基斯坦的kashmiri地震 , 85000人死亡 , 海地震 , 大約30萬人死了 , 最近發生了很糟的地震組合 , 造成日本和其核子產業 , 在所有這些例子中 , 我們看到了國際關係 , 和國際間的合作 , 和安全部隊合作 。
so these are examples of this idea of opensource security .	這些都是開源安全的想法的例子 。
we tie it together , increasingly , by doing things like this .	我們將它綁在一起 , 漸漸地 , 透過這樣的做法 。
now , you're looking at this thinking , " ah , admiral , these must be sea lanes of communication , or these might be fiber optic cables . "	現在 , 你正在看著這個想法: 「 啊 , 不論是溝通的海道 , 或是這些是光線 。 」
no . this is a graphic of the world according to twitter .	不 , 這是推特的一張圖 。
purple are tweets . green are geolocation .	紫色是推特 , 綠色是定位 。
white is the synthesis .	白人是合成的 。
it's a perfect evocation of that great population survey , the six largest nations in the world in descending order: china , india , facebook , the united states , twitter and indonesia .	人口調查是完美的演化 , 世界上六大國家的下降秩序:中國、印度、印度、臉書、美國、推特和印尼 。
why do we want to get in these nets ?	為什麼我們要用這些網子 ?
why do we want to be involved ?	我們為什麼要參與 ?
we talked earlier about the arab spring , and the power of all this .	我們先前談到阿拉伯之春 , 以及這一切的力量 。
i'll give you another example , and it's how you move this message .	我再舉另一個例子 , 就是你如何移動這個訊息 。
i gave a talk like this in london a while back about this point . i said , as i say to all of you , i'm on facebook . friend me .	我在倫敦做了這樣的演講 。 我說 , 如同我對你們說的 , 我在臉書上 。 朋友我 。
got a little laugh from the audience .	從觀眾身上得到笑聲 。
there was an article which was run by ap , on the wire .	有一篇文章是ap , 在電線上 。
got picked up in two places in the world: finland and indonesia .	在世界上兩個地方被發現:芬蘭和印尼 。
the headline was: nato admiral needs friends .	標題是:納多需要朋友 。
and the story was a catalyst , and the next morning i had hundreds of facebook friend requests from indonesians and finns , mostly saying , " admiral , we heard you need a friend , and oh , by the way , what is nato ? "	故事是一場催化劑 , 隔天早上我有數百個臉書朋友請求來自印尼人和芬蘭 , 大部分都說: 「 阿米拉 , 我們聽說你需要一個朋友 , 哦 , 噢 , 哪個 ? 」
yeah , we laugh , but this is how we move the message , and moving that message is how we connect international , interagency , privatepublic , and these social nets to help create security .	是的 , 我們笑了 , 但這就是我們傳遞訊息的方式 , 轉動訊息是我們如何連結國際、國際、私人、以及這些社會網絡 , 來協助創造安全 。
now , let me hit a somber note .	現在 , 讓我來點一下 。
this is a photograph of a brave british soldier .	這是一張英國士兵勇敢的照片 。
he's in the scots guards .	他在蘇格蘭衛隊裡 。
he's standing the watch in helmand , in southern afghanistan .	他站在helmand南阿富汗的手錶 。
i put him here to remind us , i would not want anyone to leave the room thinking that we do not need capable , competent militaries who can create real military effect .	我讓他來這裡提醒我們 , 我不希望有人離開房間 , 認為我們不需要有能力 , 能創造出真正的軍事效應 。
that is the core of who we are and what we do , and we do it to protect freedom , freedom of speech , all the things we treasure in our societies .	這就是我們是誰的核心 , 我們做的事 , 來保護言論自由、言論自由 , 所有我們在我們的社會珍視的事 。
but , you know , life is not an onandoff switch .	但 , 你知道 , 生命不是一場開關 。
you don't have to have a military that is either in hard combat or is in the barracks .	你不需要有軍隊 , 不論是在戰鬥中 , 或在巴拉克 。
i would argue life is a rheostat .	我認為生命是固定的 。
you have to dial it in , and as i think about how we create security in this 21st century , there will be times when we will apply hard power in true war and crisis , but there will be many instances , as we've talked about today , where our militaries can be part of creating 21stcentury security , international , interagency , privatepublic , connected with competent communication .	你必須把它撥進去 , 正如我所想的 , 我們該如何在21世紀創造安全 , 將有時候我們會用在真正的戰爭和危機上 , 但還有很多的例子 , 如同我們今天所說的 , 我們的軍隊可以成為21世紀的安全、國際的、私密的、私密的、與能力的聯繫在一起 。
i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	最後我會說我們今天早先聽到維基百科 。 我常常用維基百科來查看事實 , 就像你們所有人都很欣賞的 , 維基百科並不是由12位聰明的人鎖在房間寫文章中 。
wikipedia , every day , is tens of thousands of people inputting information , and every day millions of people withdrawing that information .	維基百科 , 每天 , 是數萬人輸入信息 , 每天有數百萬人接受這些信息 。
it's a perfect image for the fundamental point that no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	對於我們所有人一起思考的根本意義來說 , 這是個完美的圖像 。
no one person , no one alliance , no one nation , no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	沒有一個人 , 沒有一個聯盟 , 沒有一個國家 , 沒有一個人像我們所有人一樣聰明 。
the vision statement of wikipedia is very simple: a world in which every human being can freely share in the sum of all knowledge .	維基百科的觀點非常簡單:一個世界 , 每個人都可以自由地分享所有知識 。
my thesis for you is that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in this 21st century , we can create the sum of all security .	我的論點是結合國際、國際、私營、策略性的溝通 , 在21世紀 , 我們可以創造所有安全的總和 。
thank you very much . thank you . thank you .	非常謝謝你們 。 謝謝 。
